The Dispute on Delaying Washing the Feet in Ghusl
A Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on foot-washing sequence in ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on delaying foot washing in ghusl and state the preferred (mufta bihi) view.

Core Idea
The difference is in priority, not permissibility – both delaying and not delaying are valid.

In ghusl, there is a difference of opinion regarding when to wash the feet. Some scholars argue the feet should be washed at the beginning of the wudu, while others postpone it until after pouring water over the body. This lesson explores the Hanafi positions and their basis in the hadith of Aisha and Maymuna, and identifies the mufta bihi view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify the three views within the Hanafi school: (1) delay absolutely (majority), (2) delay only when standing in standing water (al-Mabsut, al-Hidayah), (3) never delay (some Hanafi mashayikh, also Shafi'i).
All three agree that both sequences are valid; the difference is about which is better (afdal).
2
Identify the evidence for each view
The majority base their view on the explicit hadith of Maymuna, which states the Prophet delayed washing his feet. Those who never delay rely on the hadith of Aisha, which does not mention delay, implying immediate washing. The detailed view reconciles both.
The opposition includes both intra-Hanafi scholars and Imam al-Shafi'i.
3
Analyze the Hanafi reconciliation
The reconciliation interprets Aisha's narration to apply when the Prophet was not in standing water (so immediate washing was fine) and Maymuna's narration to apply when he was in standing water (so he delayed to avoid dirtying the water).
This is the view adopted by the author of al-Hidayah and considered most correct.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In practice, a person may wash feet immediately or delay. The mufta bihi recommendation: delay only if the water is standing (e.g., a pool or basin), otherwise wash immediately.
This preserves the spirit of both narrations and avoids conflict.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The preferred view among later Hanafi fatwa authorities is the detailed view of al-Hidayah: delay only when in standing water.
This is the view taught in most Hanafi fiqh manuals.

And in al-Bada'i' it is the apparent of the second narration that he does not delay washing his feet, and there is a dispute on this. According to some of our mashayikh, and it is the most correct according to the madhhab of al-Shafi'i, he does not delay at all. In the narration of Aisha, he performed wudu like his wudu for prayer, and she did not mention delaying the feet, so apparently he washed them immediately. Al-Shafi'i and some of our mashayikh adopted this due to the long companionship and precision in hadith. In the narration of Maymuna, there is explicit mention of delaying washing them, so the majority of our mashayikh adopted it due to its fame. In al-Mujtaba, the most correct is the detail mentioned in al-Hidayah, and its reasoning is reconciliation between the two narrations by interpreting Aisha's narration to apply when he is not in a collection (of water) and Maymuna's narration to apply when he is in a collection of water. And it appears that the difference is in priority, not in permissibility.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether one should delay washing the feet until after pouring water over the body in ghusl. The author presents multiple views: (1) According to al-Mabsut and al-Hidayah, one delays the feet only when standing in standing water (majma' al-ma'). (2) Some Hanafi scholars and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that one never delays. (3) The majority of Hanafis hold that one delays absolutely. The source of the disagreement is two hadith narrations: Aisha's narration does not mention delaying, implying immediate washing; Maymuna's narration explicitly mentions delaying. The preferred view (as in al-Hidayah) is to reconcile: when standing in standing water, one delays (to avoid splashing dirty water onto clean feet), otherwise one does not delay. The author notes the difference is in priority (afdaliyyah), not permissibility (jawaz).

Key Terms
مستنقع الماء (mustanqa' al-ma'): Standing water or a collection of water, such as a pool or basin.
رواية عائشة وميمونة (riwayat 'Aisha wa Maymuna): Two hadith narrations from the Prophet's wives describing his ghusl, with different details about foot washing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view in the Hanafi school, when should one delay washing the feet in ghusl?
A) Always delay.
B) Never delay.
C) Delay only when standing in standing water.
D) Delay only when not in standing water.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school reconciles the hadith of Aisha and Maymuna by making delayed foot washing contingent on standing water, with the difference being priority not permissibility.

The Hanafi Dispute on Delaying Foot Washing in Ghusl
Explains the Hanafi ikhtilaf on delaying foot washing in ghusl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ikhtilaf on delaying foot washing in ghusl and identify the mufta bihi position with its justification.

Core Idea
Delaying foot washing in ghusl is preferred when standing in water, not obligatory.

In ghusl, the timing of washing the feet may seem trivial, but it reveals a nuanced Hanafi internal disagreement based on competing hadith narrations. This lesson unpacks the dispute between narrations of Aisha and Maymuna, the reconciliation offered by later scholars, and the operative ruling for today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The passage discusses whether it is preferable (awla) or even obligatory to delay washing the feet during ghusl until after washing the rest of the body, particularly when standing in standing water (mustanqa').
2
Trace the two hadith narrations
Aisha's narration suggests immediate foot washing (no mention of delay), while Maymuna's explicitly mentions the Prophet delaying his feet. Note the difference in context (standing water vs. not).
3
Map the Hanafi positions
Some Hanafi scholars (and al-Shafi'i) adopt Aisha's narration and do not delay at all. Most Hanafi scholars adopt Maymuna's and delay absolutely. A third, detailed position reconciles both: delay when in standing water, otherwise do not delay.
The detailed position is the mufta bihi.
4
Analyze the role of used water (maa' musta'mal)
The status of used water (tahir vs. najis) influences whether the feet become impure again after washing. On the fatwa of tahara, delay is only preferred; on the narration of najasa, it becomes necessary to avoid using impure water.
The discussion involves both preference (awlawiyya) and necessity depending on the riwaya.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: on the majority view, one may wash feet during wudu before ghusl if not in standing water, but it is better to delay if in standing water. On the other view, one must wash feet during wudu without delay.

Commentary
This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the Hanafi internal disagreement regarding the timing of washing the feet during ghusl (ritual bath). The author begins by noting the consensus that wudu is not obligatory during ghusl, except for Dawud al-Zahiri who held it obligatory for janabah. He then addresses the issue of delaying the washing of the feet. There are two main narrations: from Aisha, which implies immediate washing of the feet, and from Maymuna, which explicitly mentions delaying. The Hanafi school is divided: some scholars (including al-Shafi'i) follow Aisha's narration and do not delay, while most Hanafi scholars follow Maymuna and delay absolutely. The preferred view in al-Mujtaba and al-Hidayah is a detailed distinction: if one is standing in collected water (mustanqa'), he delays; otherwise, he does not. This reconciles the two hadiths. The author then critiques the view that the disagreement is merely about preference (awlawiyya) rather than permissibility. He argues that on the fatwa of tahara (purity of used water), the delay is a matter of preference, but on the narration of najasa (impurity of used water), it becomes a matter of obligation due to necessity. The detailed discussion involves the status of used water (maa' musta'mal) and its effect on the feet after ghusl. The author refutes Ibn al-Malik's understanding that on the narration of non-partition (tajzi), the benefit of washing feet is lost, clarifying that the obligation of washing the feet is agreed upon, and the disagreement is only about benefit.

Key Terms
مستنقع (mustanqa'): Standing water or a pool where water collects, especially during ghusl.
رواية (riwaya): A transmission or narration of a hadith, specifically the hadiths of Aisha and Maymuna regarding the Prophet's ghusl.
ماء مستعمل (maa' musta'mal): Used water that has been employed for ritual purification; its status affects whether it can be reused.
أولوية (awlawiyya): Preference or priority; the disagreement is about what is preferred, not what is obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view in this passage, when is it recommended to delay washing the feet during ghusl?
A) Always, regardless of the situation
B) Never; feet must be washed during wudu
C) Only if the person is standing in collected water (mustanqa')
D) Only if the person is not standing in collected water

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is to delay foot washing only when standing in collected water (mustanqa'), reconciling the hadith of Aisha and Maymuna.

Washing Feet in Ghusl: The Two Riwayat and Their Practical Impact
Analyzing the necessity of rewashing feet based on two Hanafi riwayat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi riwayat (tajzi and adam al-tajzi) regarding the removal of janabah in ghusl and state the mufta bihi ruling on rewashing the feet after ghusl.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school has two riwayat on ghusl; the mufta bihi is that used water is pure and rewashing feet is mustahabb, not wajib.

This lesson explores a practical detail of ghusl: if you wash your feet during wudu before ghusl, do you need to wash them again after completing the ghusl? The answer depends on two narrations within the Hanafi school about how janabah is removed. By understanding these riwayat and the status of used water, you will grasp a key aspect of Hanafi fiqh that balances textual tradition with ease of practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the practical question
The text begins by stating that washing the feet first is beneficial because they become contaminated by subsequent washings, so they need rewashing. The issue is whether rewashing is obligatory or just recommended.
2
Define the two riwayat
Riwayat al-tajzi: the body is divisible into separate parts; janabah is removed from each part when water separates from it. Riwayat 'adam al-tajzi: the body is one integral unit; janabah is only removed when water covers the entire body.
These riwayat are attributed to early Hanafi authorities, especially Imam Muhammad.
3
Apply each riwaya to the scenario
On tajzi: washing feet first removes janabah from them, so no rewashing is needed; the water that later reaches them is not used water. On 'adam al-tajzi: janabah remains until the whole body is washed; after ghusl, the feet may contact used water, which could necessitate rewashing if used water is impure.
The passage clarifies that even on 'adam al-tajzi, the feet are pure from hadath, and used water is pure according to the mufta bihi.
4
Analyze the benefit of washing first
Even if rewashing is not obligatory, washing the feet first provides a benefit: it permits recitation of Quran and touching the mushaf immediately after wudu, before ghusl. So it is not useless.
The author refutes Ibn al-Malik who claimed it is without benefit on 'adam al-tajzi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is that used water is pure (tahir). Therefore, even if the feet come into contact with it, they remain pure. Rewashing the feet is not obligatory but is recommended (mustahabb) as a precaution and for scrupulousness.
The mashayikh have preferred riwayat 'adam al-tajzi, but the obligation to rewash does not follow from it.

البدن بخلاف تنجس الرجلين الماء المستعمل فإنه لا يكون إلا بعد انفصاله وتمام الطهارة .اهـ. قوله : (وقد صرح به الهندي فقال الخ) أقول : لا يخفى أن ما بنى عليه كلامه . من الاختلاف في الأولوية هو أن الماء زالت الجنابة عنهما أو هو موقوف على غسل الباقي؟ فرواية التجزي قائلة بالأوّل، ورواية عدم التجزي قائلة بالثاني لا أنها قائلة بوجوب إعادة غسل الرجلين وفاتدة اختلاف الروايتين أنه لو تمضمض الجنب أو غسل يديه هل يحل له قراءة القرآن ومس المصحف؟ فعلى رواية التجزي يحل له لزوال الجنابة عنه، وعلى رواية عدم التجزي لا يحل له لعدم الزوال الآن، وقد صحح المشايخ هذه الرواية. وقد اندفع بما ذكرنا أيضاً ما استشكله بعض المحشين من زوال الجنابة الماء من الرأس كما هو العادة على رواية التجزي وقال : كما لا يخفى ولم يجب عنه وهو سهو منه وسوء فهم فإنهم اتفقوا على أن البدن في الغسل كعضو واحد وأتفقوا على أن الماء لا يصير مستعملاً إلا بعد الانفصال العضو. فعلى رواية التجزي لا يصير مستعملاً إلا إذا انفصل عن جميع البدن وإن زالت الجنابة عن كل عضو انفصل عنه الماء وهذا ظاهر لا يخفى. والذي يظهر أن القائلين بالتأخير إنما استحبوه ليكون الافتتاح والاختتام بأعضاء الوضوء أخذاً من حديث ميمونة. قال القاضي عياض في شرح مسلم : وليس فيه تصريح بل هو محتمل لأن قولها «توضأ وضوءه للصلاة» الأظهر فيه إكمال وضوئه وقولها آخراً ثم تنحى فغسل رجليه» يحتمل أن يكون لما نالهما من تلك البقعة اهـ. فعلى هذا يغسلهما بعد الفراغ من الغسل مطلقاً أعني سواء غسلهما أو لا إكمالاً للوضوء أو لم يغسلهما، وسواء أصابهما طين أو كانتا في مستنقع الماء المستعمل أو لم يكن شيء من ذلك. ثم لا يخفى تعين غسلهما في حق الواحد منا بعد الفراغ من الغسل إذا كانتا في مستنقع الماء وكان على البدن نجاسة من مني أو غيره والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم . أثم وفي الذخيرة نقلاً عن العيون: خاض الرجل في ماء الحمام بعدما غسل قدميه فإن لم يعلم أن في الحمام جنباً أجزأه أن لا يغسل قدميه، وإن علم في الحمام جنباً قد اغتسل يلزمه أن يغسل قدميه إذا خرج قال رحمه الله في واقعاته وعلى ما اخترناه في الماء المستعمل ينبغي أن لا يلزمه غسل القدمين لكن استثنى الجنب في الكتاب فإنه موضع الاستثناء وغيره قال : إنما استثنى الجنب لأن الجنب يكون على بدنه قذر ظاهراً وغالباً حتى لو لم يكن كان الماء المستعمل للمحدث والجنب سواء ويكون طاهراً على رواية محمد ولا يلزمه غسل الرجلين وهو الظاهر اهـ. وفي بقية حديث ميمونة ثم أتيته بالمنديل فردّه قال النووي : فيه استحباب ترك تنشيف الأعضاء. وقال الإمام: لا خلاف في أنه لا يحرم تنشيف الماء . عن الأعضاء ولا يستحب ولكن هل يكره؟ فيه خلاف بين الصحابة وقال القاضي : يحتمل رده للمنديل
Benefit regarding the precedence of washing them [the feet] because they become contaminated by the washings thereafter, so they need to be washed a second time. Its meaning is that the complete benefit is not achieved by washing them first. We say this because if he washes them first and does not wash them a second time, he leaves the state of janabah and his prayer is permissible according to the relied-upon position, because the water that reaches them from the ground where the washings have collected is used water, and used water is pure according to the relied-upon position. The water that reaches his feet from pouring on the rest of his body, other than what has collected on the ground, is not used water. As for the narration of non-divisibility [of the body into parts], it is apparent; as for the narration of divisibility, this water is not described as used except after its separation from the entire body. So the water that reached the feet is not used because the entire body during the bath is like one limb, to the extent that it is permissible to transfer moisture from one limb to another. Therefore, there is no need to wash them a second time except by way of scrupulousness and preference, not due to obligation, because the used water that reached him from the collected washings, although pure, has transferred impurity to him such that sound natures abhor it. Al-Hindi explicitly stated: This is only applicable according to the narration of the impurity of used water as well. This is indicated by what he mentioned in al-Muhit: 'He does not wash his feet because washing them is of no benefit, as they become impure a second time by the collection of washings.' So from this it is known that it is according to the narration of the impurity of used water. According to that, the meaning of their statement 'it is of no benefit' is that it does not yield a complete benefit; otherwise, the priority has yielded a benefit, namely, the permissibility of reciting the Quran and touching the mushaf, even if his feet become impure with used water. With this, the corruption of what Ibn al-Malik mentioned in Sharh al-Majma' becomes evident: that the lack of benefit is according to the narration of non-divisibility; as for the narration of divisibility, washing them is beneficial because janabah is removed from his feet when he washes them in wudu, and they become pure in the collected water after washing the rest of his body. So he understood from the narration of non-divisibility that if he washes his feet then washes the rest of his body, he must re-wash his feet because janabah is not removed from them. This is a great oversight and a serious error, for they agreed that the obligation of washing the feet... Avoiding extravagance is incorrect because then it permits touching the mushaf and even other prohibitions besides prayer due to the removal of hadath. Is this benefit not sufficient? After its attainment, how can it be said that it is extravagance and that leaving it is obligatory, since he may not pray at that time? And his statement 'there is no difference between impurity and impurity' is also not accepted; rather, the difference is clear because if the real impurity is on the body and water touches it, hadath is not removed due to the impurity, unless the place is purified from it; then hadath is also removed. Due to that, the impurity spreads in the body, unlike the contamination of the feet with used water, which occurs only after its separation and the completion of purification. End quote. His statement: 'Al-Hindi explicitly stated...' I say: It is not hidden that what he built his statement upon, regarding the difference in preference, is that used water is pure. What he mentioned here is based on its impurity; accordingly, there is no difference in preference but rather in obligation or not, because there is no doubt about the obligation of washing them according to this. So how does he strengthen his statement with it while it contradicts his intent? His statement: 'He understood from the narration of non-divisibility...' He took that from his statement 'because janabah is removed from his feet'; its implication is that according to the narration of non-divisibility, it is the opposite, that there is no benefit in washing them first, and that he must re-wash them. His statement: 'And has fallen by giving it precedence, but has janabah been removed from them or is it dependent on washing the rest?' The narration of divisibility says the former; the narration of non-divisibility says the latter, but it does not say that it is obligatory to re-wash the feet. The difference between the two narrations is that if a junub person rinses his mouth or washes his hands, is it permissible for him to recite Quran and touch the mushaf? According to the narration of divisibility, it is permitted due to the removal of janabah from that part; according to the narration of non-divisibility, it is not permitted due to the lack of removal at that moment. The mashayikh have deemed this narration (non-divisibility) as correct. With what we have mentioned, the objection of some commentators regarding the removal of janabah by water from the head, as is customary according to the narration of divisibility, is also refuted. He said: 'as is not hidden' and did not respond to it, which is a mistake and poor understanding from him. For they agreed that the body during the bath is like one limb, and they agreed that water does not become used except after separation from the limb. According to the narration of divisibility, it does not become used except when it separates from the entire body, even if janabah is removed from each limb from which water separates. This is obvious and not hidden. What appears is that those who advocate delaying [washing the feet] only recommended it so that the opening and closing are with the limbs of wudu, taking from the hadith of Maimunah. Qadi Iyad said in Sharh Muslim: There is no explicit statement in it; rather, it is probable because her saying 'he performed wudu like his wudu for prayer' apparently means he completed his wudu, and her later saying 'then he moved aside and washed his feet' may be because they were affected by that place. End quote. Accordingly, he washes them after completing the bath absolutely, i.e., whether he had washed them or not, to complete the wudu, or whether he had not washed them. And regardless of whether dirt touched them, or they were in a pool of used water, or none of that. Then it is not hidden that it is incumbent for us to wash them after completing the bath if they were in a pool of water and on the body was impurity like semen or other. And Allah knows best. In al-Dhakhirah, quoting from al-Uyun: A man waded in the water of a bath after washing his feet; if he does not know that there is a junub person in the bath, it is sufficient for him not to wash his feet. If he knows that there is a junub person who has bathed in the bath, he must wash his feet when he exits. He said in his Waqi'at: According to our chosen view regarding used water, he should not be required to wash his feet, but he excluded the junub in the book, as it is the place of exception. Someone else said: He only excluded the junub because the junub usually has apparent filth on his body; otherwise, the used water for a minor impure person and a junub is the same, and it is pure according to the narration of Muhammad, and he is not required to wash his feet; that is the apparent view. End quote. In the remainder of the hadith of Maimunah: 'Then I brought him a towel and he refused it.' Al-Nawawi said: In it is the recommendation to leave drying the limbs. And Imam [al-Ghazali] said: There is no dispute that drying water from the limbs is not prohibited and not recommended, but is it disliked? There is dispute among the companions. Qadi said: Perhaps his refusal of the towel was...

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a critical refinement. The author, Ibn Nujaym, is analyzing the ruling on washing the feet during ghusl. The issue is whether, after a person has performed ghusl by pouring water over his body, he needs to wash his feet again if they were initially washed during wudu before the ghusl. The dispute is rooted in two Hanafi riwayat (narrations) attributed to Imam Muhammad and others: riwayat al-tajzi (divisibility) and riwayat 'adam al-tajzi (non-divisibility). According to riwayat al-tajzi, each body part is considered separate; janabah is removed from a part as soon as water separates from that part. Thus, if the feet were washed first, the janabah is removed from them, and the subsequent water that flows over them from the rest of the body is not 'used water' (musta'mal) until it separates from the entire body. Hence, the feet become pure and there is no need to rewash them. According to riwayat 'adam al-tajzi, the whole body is one unit; janabah is only removed when water has flowed over the entire body. So washing the feet alone does not remove janabah from them until the rest of the body is washed. Therefore, the feet remain impure until the ghusl is complete, but once the ghusl is complete, the water that has collected on the ground is considered used water, and if the feet become contaminated by that used water, they need to be washed again. The author clarifies that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that used water is pure (tahir). Therefore, even if the feet are in contact with used water, they remain pure, and there is no need to rewash them. However, out of caution (tanazzuh) and preference (afdaliyya), one may wash them again. The author strongly refutes Ibn al-Malik's misunderstanding that on riwayat 'adam al-tajzi, one must rewash the feet. He argues that even on that riwayat, washing the feet first does provide a benefit (e.g., permitting Quran recitation), so it is not without benefit. The passage then discusses a practical scenario from al-Dhakhirah: if one wades in a public bath after washing his feet, if there is no known junub, he need not rewash; if there is a known junub, he must rewash. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq notes that according to his preferred view (that used water is pure), even in the latter case rewashing is not required. Finally, he references the hadith of Maimunah about the Prophet ﷺ not using a towel after ghusl, discussing the ruling on drying limbs.

Key Terms
التجزي (al-tajzi): The view that the body is divided into separate parts for the purpose of removing hadath; each part can independently have janabah removed when water separates from it.
عدم التجزي ('adam al-tajzi): The view that the body is one integral unit; janabah is only removed when water has flowed over the entire body.
الماء المستعمل (al-ma' al-musta'mal): Water that has been used for purification (wudu or ghusl) and has separated from the body.
رواية (riwayah): A narration or transmitted opinion within the Hanafi school, often attributed to Imam Muhammad or other early authorities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in this passage, what is the ruling on rewashing the feet after ghusl if the feet were washed during wudu beforehand?
A) It is wajib (obligatory).
B) It is mustahabb (recommended).
C) It is haram (forbidden).
D) It is makruh (disliked).

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, rewashing the feet after ghusl is not obligatory but recommended, based on the mufta bihi view that used water is pure and the body in ghusl is treated as one unit.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Two Riwāyat on Partial Washing in Ghusl and Their Consequences
Explaining the two transmitted opinions on whether part-washing removes janaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between the two riwayat (tajzi and 'adam tajzi) regarding partial washing during ghusl and apply the relied-upon position to determine the permissibility of reading the Quran or touching the mushaf after partial washing.

Core Idea
Partial washing does not remove janaba; the body is one unit for ghusl.

In this lesson, we explore an internal Hanafi dispute about whether washing part of the body during ghusl removes janaba from that part immediately. The two transmitted opinions (riwayat) lead to different rulings on whether one can recite Quran or touch the mushaf after such partial washing. We will see why the preferred position is that janaba is not removed until the full ghusl is complete.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two riwayat
Recognize that there are two transmitted opinions: riwayat al-tajzi (partial washing removes janaba from that part) and riwayat 'adam al-tajzi (no removal until full wash).
Both riwayat exist within the Hanafi school.
2
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence of the difference is whether a person who has only partially washed can recite Quran or touch the mushaf. On tajzi, it is allowed; on 'adam tajzi, it is not.
This consequence is the key point of fatwa.
3
Examine the Hanafi tarjih
The mashayikh have preferred (sahhahu) the riwayat of 'adam al-tajzi. Understand the reasoning: the body in ghusl is like one limb; water becomes musta'mal only after separating from the entire body, so janaba does not leave the parts until the whole wash is done.
The analogy with wudu or head in ghusl is rejected.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a person who only rinses his mouth during ghusl, according to the mufta bihi position, can he recite Quran? No, because janaba remains.
He must complete the entire ghusl.

فرواية التجزي قائلة بالأوّل، ورواية عدم التجزي قائلة بالثاني لا أنها قائلة بوجوب إعادة غسل الرجلين وفائدة اختلاف الروايتين أنه لو تمضمض الجنب أو غسل يديه هل يحل له قراءة القرآن ومس المصحف؟ فعلى رواية التجزي يحل له لزوال الجنابة عنه، وعلى رواية عدم التجزي لا يحل له لعدم الزوال الآن، وقد صحح المشايخ هذه الرواية. وقد اندفع بما ذكرنا أيضاً ما استشكله بعض المحشين من زوال الجنابة الماء من الرأس كما هو العادة على رواية التجزي وقال : كما لا يخفى ولم يجب عنه وهو سهو منه وسوء فهم فإنهم اتفقوا على أن البدن في الغسل كعضو واحد وأتفقوا على أن الماء لا يصير مستعملاً إلا بعد الانفصال العضو. فعلى رواية التجزي لا يصير مستعملاً إلا إذا انفصل عن جميع البدن وإن زالت الجنابة عن كل عضو انفصل عنه الماء وهذا ظاهر لا يخفى. والذي يظهر أن القائلين بالتأخير إنما استحبوه ليكون الافتتاح والاختتام بأعضاء الوضوء أخذاً من حديث ميمونة. قال القاضي عياض في شرح مسلم : وليس فيه تصريح بل هو محتمل لأن قولها «توضأ وضوءه للصلاة» الأظهر فيه إكمال وضوئه وقولها آخراً ثم تنحى فغسل رجليه» يحتمل أن يكون لما نالهما من تلك البقعة اهـ. فعلى هذا يغسلهما بعد الفراغ من الغسل مطلقاً أعني سواء غسلهما أو لا إكمالاً للوضوء أو لم يغسلهما، وسواء أصابهما طين أو كانتا في مستنقع الماء المستعمل أو لم يكن شيء من ذلك. ثم لا يخفى تعين غسلهما في حق الواحد منا بعد الفراغ من الغسل إذا كانتا في مستنقع الماء وكان على البدن نجاسة من مني أو غيره والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم .
The tradition of tajzi says the first; the tradition of 'adam tajzi says the second, not that it says it is obligatory to repeat washing the feet. The benefit of the difference between the two traditions is that if a junub rinses his mouth or washes his hands, is it permissible for him to recite Quran and touch the mushaf? According to the tradition of tajzi it is permissible for him due to removal of janaba from him; according to the tradition of 'adam tajzi it is not permissible for him due to non-removal at that moment. And the mashayikh have declared this tradition (the latter) correct. What some glossators have questioned about water removing janaba from the head as is customary according to the tradition of tajzi has also been repelled by what we mentioned, and he said: as is not hidden, and he did not answer it, and it is an oversight from him and a bad understanding. For they agreed that the body in ghusl is like a single limb, and they agreed that water does not become musta'mal except after separation from the limb. Thus according to the tradition of tajzi, it does not become musta'mal except when it separates from the entire body, even if janaba is removed from every limb from which water separates, and this is apparent, not hidden. And what appears is that those who advocate delay recommended it so that the opening and closing be with the limbs of wudu, following the hadith of Maimuna. Al-Qadi 'Iyad said in Sharh Muslim: There is no explicit statement in it, rather it is probable, because her saying 'He performed wudu like the wudu for prayer' the most apparent is the completion of his wudu, and her saying at the end 'then he moved away and washed his feet' may be because something soiled them from that spot. Thus, he washes them after completing ghusl absolutely, meaning whether he washed them before or not as a completion of wudu, whether they were soiled with mud or in a pool of used water or not. Then it is not hidden that washing them is obligatory for any of us after finishing ghusl if they were in a pool of used water and there was impurity on the body from semen or otherwise. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of partial washing during ghusl. There are two riwayat (transmitted opinions): riwayat al-tajzi holds that when a junub washes a limb (e.g., rinsing mouth or washing hands), janaba is removed from that limb immediately. Riwayat 'adam al-tajzi holds that janaba is not removed until the entire body is washed, meaning the partial washing is not effective for removing janaba from those limbs. The practical consequence (thamaratu al-khilaf) is whether the person can read Quran or touch the mushaf after such partial washing. According to tajzi, he can; according to 'adam al-tajzi, he cannot. The mashayikh have corrected (sahhahu) the riwayat of 'adam al-tajzi, meaning it is the relied-upon position (mu'tamad). The text then refutes an objection from some glossators who argued that on tajzi, water from the head should remove janaba from the head. The response is that the body is considered one unit in ghusl; water becomes musta'mal only after separating from the entire body, so on tajzi, the water from the head would be musta'mal only after separating from the whole body, not just the head. The discussion then transitions to the timing of washing feet: those who delay washing feet until after ghusl recommend it based on the hadith of Maimuna, but al-Qadi 'Iyad explains that the hadith is not explicit. The final ruling is that washing the feet after ghusl is obligatory (ta'ayyana) if one stands in a pool of used water and there was impurity (e.g., semen) on the body.

Key Terms
التجزي (al-tajzi): The transmitted opinion that washing a part of the body during ghusl removes janaba from that part immediately.
الماء المستعمل (al-mā' al-musta'mal): Water that has been used for a ritual purification (wudu or ghusl) and has separated from the body, making it unsuitable for further purification in some contexts.
الجنابة (al-janābah): The state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, typically due to sexual intercourse or ejaculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, can a person who has only rinsed his mouth during ghusl recite Quran?
A) Yes, because janaba is removed from the mouth.
B) No, because janaba has not been removed from him yet.
C) Yes, because rinsing the mouth is sufficient for removal of janaba from the head.
D) No, because water must become musta'mal first.

Key Takeaway
Partial washing during ghusl does not remove janaba according to the relied-upon Hanafi position; the entire body must be washed for janaba to be removed.

Washing Feet After Ghusl in a Public Bath
Ruling on rewashing feet after ghusl when knowledge of a junub exists in a public bath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on rewashing feet after ghusl in a public bath, distinguishing when knowledge of a junub triggers the obligation.

Core Idea
Wash your feet again if you know a junub used the bath water; otherwise, you need not.

When you perform ghusl in a public bath (hamam), the water may be shared. A common question arises: if you have already washed your feet during ghusl, must you wash them again after stepping out? The answer depends on whether you know a person in major impurity (junub) has used the same water. This lesson examines the Hanafi position, including an important intra-madhhab difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Understand the factual situation: a man has washed his feet during ghusl, then wades in the hamam water. The ruling depends on his knowledge about a junub using that water.
The water is already used; the key is knowledge of a junub.
2
Apply the condition of knowledge
If he does not know of a junub, he does not need to wash his feet again. If he knows a junub has performed ghusl in that water, he must wash his feet upon exiting.
Knowledge is the decisive condition.
3
Understand the underlying reasoning
The junub's body likely carries visible impurity (e.g., traces of semen). Even though according to Imam Muhammad used water is generally pure, the presence of a junub creates a likelihood of contamination, making re-washing necessary.
This is based on qiyas khafi (hidden analogy).
4
Distinguish the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad holds used water pure; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold it impure. The text opts for Muhammad's view as 'al-zahir', but makes an exception for the junub.
The exception is specific to the junub case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الذخيرة نقلاً عن العيون: خاض الرجل في ماء الحمام بعدما غسل قدميه فإن لم يعلم أن في الحمام جنباً أجزأه أن لا يغسل قدميه، وإن علم في الحمام جنباً قد اغتسل يلزمه أن يغسل قدميه إذا خرج قال رحمه الله في واقعاته وعلى ما اخترناه في الماء المستعمل ينبغي أن لا يلزمه غسل القدمين لكن استثنى الجنب في الكتاب فإنه موضع الاستثناء وغيره قال : إنما استثنى الجنب لأن الجنب يكون على بدنه قذر ظاهراً وغالباً حتى لو لم يكن كان الماء المستعمل للمحدث والجنب سواء ويكون طاهراً على رواية محمد ولا يلزمه غسل الرجلين وهو الظاهر اهـ.
And in al-Dhakhirah quoting from al-'Uyun: A man waded in the water of the bathhouse after he had washed his feet; if he does not know that there is a junub in the bathhouse, it suffices him not to wash his feet. But if he knows that there is a junub in the bathhouse who has performed ghusl, he must wash his feet when he comes out. He said, may Allah have mercy on him, in his Waqi'at: According to what we have chosen regarding used water, it would be fitting that washing the feet is not necessary for him, but he made an exception for the junub in the book, for he is the place of exception. Others said: He only made the exception for the junub because the junub has visible and predominant dirt on his body, so even if it were not, the used water for the minor-impure and the junub is the same and is pure according to the riwaya of Muhammad, and washing the feet is not necessary for him, and that is the apparent (view).
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario: a man who has already washed his feet during ghusl in a public bath (hamam) wades in the bath's water. If he does not know that a person in major impurity (junub) has also used the water, he does not need to wash his feet again. However, if he knows that a junub has performed ghusl in that water, then upon exiting he must wash his feet. The reasoning: because the junub's body likely carries visible impurity (e.g., traces of semen), the used water is considered contaminated. The text then quotes from the Waqi'at of Imam Muhammad that according to the chosen view on used water (that it is pure), washing feet would not be necessary, but he made an exception for the junub because his body usually has impurity. Others add that if the junub had no such impurity, the used water would be pure (according to Muhammad's riwaya), and washing feet would not be required. The phrase 'وهو الظاهر' indicates that this lenient view is the apparent one.

Key Terms
الحمام (al-ḥammām): A public bathhouse where people perform ghusl; water may be shared and used by multiple people.
الماء المستعمل (al-mā' al-musta'mal): Water that has been used for purification. In this context, debate on its purity: used by a junub may render it impure if impurity is present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the action wajib upon a man who knows a junub has used the hamam water after he himself has already washed his feet?
A) Repeat the entire ghusl.
B) Wash his feet upon exiting.
C) Wait until the junub leaves before exiting.
D) Perform tayammum.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, washing feet after ghusl in a public bath is wajib only when one knows a junub used the water; otherwise, it is not required.

Drying after Purification: Permissible, Not Recommended
Examining the legal status of drying after purification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on drying the body after ritual purification and explain the basis for the difference between mustahab, makruh, and mubah.

Core Idea
Drying after wudu or ghusl is mubah—permissible but not recommended—based on the Prophet’s refusal of a towel being for humility, not prohibition.

The hadith of Maimuna reports that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was brought a towel after his ghusl but refused it. Some scholars, like al-Nawawi, saw this as a recommendation to leave the body wet. However, Hanafi jurists analyze the context: the refusal could be for various reasons—humility, haste, or rejecting luxury—not to establish a prohibition or recommendation. Hence, drying is permissible (mubah), and the act is only disliked if done out of extravagance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Primary Evidence
The act is drying (tanashshuf) after wudu or ghusl. The key evidence is the hadith from Maimuna where the Prophet refused a towel. Understand the literal event.
The hadith is found in Sahih Muslim.
2
Analyze al-Nawawi's Interpretation
Al-Nawawi (Shafi'i) considered the refusal as a recommendation (istihbab) not to dry. This represents a different fiqh lens.
Shafi'is see an implicit guidance in the act of leaving wet.
3
Apply the Hanafi Method: Contextual Reasoning
Hanafi jurists examine possible reasons for the refusal: humility, prayer haste, or avoidance of luxury habits. The absence of explicit prohibition or command leaves the act legally neutral (mubah).
Qadi 'Iyad's explanations are cited in the text.
4
Distinguish Between Mubah, Makruh, and Mustahab
The majority view: drying is mubah. It becomes makruh tanzihan if done as a habit of luxury. The only dissenter (Munyat al-Musalli) calls it mustahab, but this is not relied upon.
The Hanafi principle: original permissibility (ibahah asliyyah) unless a proof shifts it.
5
Recognize the Practical Consequence
You may dry yourself freely; but avoid excess or showing off. In cold weather, drying is even more justified as a need.
The fatwa follows the majority: mubah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي بقية حديث ميمونة ثم أتيته بالمنديل فردّه قال النووي : فيه استحباب ترك تنشيف الأعضاء. وقال الإمام: لا خلاف في أنه لا يحرم تنشيف الماء عن الأعضاء ولا يستحب ولكن هل يكره؟ فيه خلاف بين الصحابة وقال القاضي : يحتمل رده للمنديل لشيء رآه أو لاستعجاله في الصلاة أو تواضعاً أو خلافاً لعادة أهل الترفه، ويكون الحديث أنه كانت له خرقة يتنشف بها عند الضرورة وشدة البرد ليزيل برد الماء عن اهـ. والمنقول في معراج الدراية وغيرها أنه لا بأس بالتمسح بالمنديل للمتوضيء والمغتسل إلا أن لا يبالغ ويستقصي فيبقي أثر الوضوء على أعضائه ولم أر من صرح باستحبابه ينبغي إلا صاحب منية المصلي فقال : ويستحب أن يمسح بمنديل بعد اغسل،
And in the rest of the hadith of Maimuna: 'Then I brought him a towel and he refused it.' Al-Nawawi said: In it is the recommendation of leaving off drying the limbs. And Imam (al-Haramayn?) said: There is no disagreement that it is not prohibited to dry the water from the limbs, nor is it recommended, but is it disliked? There is disagreement among the companions (of the Prophet?). And al-Qadi said: It is possible that he refused the towel for something he saw, or due to his haste for prayer, or humility, or contrary to the habit of the luxurious, and the hadith means that he had a cloth with which he would dry himself in necessity and severe cold to remove the chill of water from him. And it is transmitted in Mi'raj al-Dirayah and other works that there is no harm in wiping with a towel for the one performing wudu and the one performing ghusl, unless he exaggerates and goes to extremes, leaving the trace of wudu on his limbs. And I have not seen anyone who explicitly stated its recommendation except the author of Munyat al-Musalli, who said: It is recommended to wipe with a towel after ghusl.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on drying the body after ritual purification (wudu or ghusl). The hadith of Maimuna states that the Prophet (peace be upon him) refused a towel (mandil) brought to him after ghusl. Al-Nawawi interprets this as a recommendation (istihbab) not to dry the limbs. However, 'Imam' (likely al-Ghazali or al-Haramayn) clarifies that there is consensus that drying is neither prohibited nor recommended, though there is a difference of opinion among the Sahaba (or scholars) on whether it is disliked (makruh). Al-Qadi 'Iyad offers possible reasons for the Prophet's refusal: something he saw, haste for prayer, humility, or avoiding the habit of luxury. He suggests the Prophet did use a cloth when necessary (e.g., extreme cold). The text then cites Mi'raj al-Dirayah stating that wiping with a towel is permissible as long as one does not exaggerate and retain water on limbs. The only scholar who explicitly declared it recommended is the author of Munyat al-Musalli (al-Sarakhi? Actually, Munyat al-Musalli is by al-Kashghari). The net ruling: tanashshuf (drying) is mubah (permissible), not sunnah, and possibly makruh only if one does so out of luxury or extravagance.

Key Terms
التنشف (al-tanashshuf): The act of drying the body after ritual purification (wudu or ghusl) with a towel or cloth.
المنديل (al-mandīl): A towel or cloth used for drying after purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi interpretation, why did the Prophet (peace be upon him) refuse the towel after his ghusl?
A) Because drying is prohibited.
B) Because he wanted to teach that leaving wet is better.
C) For reasons of humility, haste, or avoiding luxury.
D) Because the cloth was impure.

Key Takeaway
Drying after ritual purification is mubah (permissible) in the Hanafi school; the Prophet's refusal offers a lesson in humility, not a legal prohibition.

Sunan and Mandūbāt of Ghusl and Ruling on Water Usage
Listing sunan of ghusl and clarifying water quantity rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunan of ghusl and explain that the water estimates (sa' and mud) are recommended but not obligatory.

Core Idea
The sunan of wudu apply to ghusl except facing qibla; the sa' and mud are guidelines, not obligations.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq enumerates the sunan and mandubat of ghusl, noting that most of the sunan of wudu carry over, with one key exception: facing the qibla is not recommended because ghusl often involves uncovering the private parts. The passage also addresses the proper use of water, explaining that the estimates of a sa‘ for ghusl and a mud for wudu set by Imam Muhammad are guidelines of minimal sufficiency, not binding limits. Extravagance (israf) is makruh, but one may use more or less water as needed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Sunan of Ghusl
Recognize that the sunan (recommended acts) and mandubat (commendable acts) of wudu are also established for ghusl, such as making intention (niyyah), washing hands, rinsing mouth and nose, etc.
Niyyah is specifically mentioned as sunnah.
2
Note the Exception: Facing Qibla
Understand that facing the qibla, which is sunnah in wudu, is not recommended in ghusl because ghusl involves greater exposure of the private parts.
This is based on the text from al-Bada'i‘ and Sharh Munyat al-Musalli.
3
Understand the Water Estimates
Learn that Imam Muhammad estimated a sa‘ for ghusl and a mud for wudu as minimal sufficiency, but these are non-binding guidelines. One may use more or less as needed, as long as israf (extravagance) is avoided.
The consensus cited by al-Nawawi confirms the non-obligatory nature of these measures.
4
Apply the Ruling on Israf
Recognize that using water excessively (israf) is makruh. The best practice is to follow the Prophet’s example of using a sa‘ for ghusl if it suffices, but it is also permissible to use more if needed, provided it does not lead to waswasa (obsessive doubt).
If staying in flowing water long enough to perform wudu and ghusl, one fulfills the sunnah of water usage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإشارة الثالثة أن جميع السنن والمندوبات في الوضوء ثابتة في هذا الوضوء والغسل فتسن النية ويندب بها. قال في البدائع : وأما آداب الغسل فهي آداب الوضوء لكن يستثنى منه أن آداب من الوضوء استقبال القبلة بخلاف الغسل لأنه يكون غالباً كشف العورة بخلاف الوضوء، مع كذا في شرح منية المصلي. ومن مكروهاته الإسراف وتقدم تفسيره ولهذا قدر محمد رحمه الله في ظاهر الرواية الصاع للغسل والمد للوضوء وهو تقدير أدنى الكفاية عادة وليس بتقدير لازم أن من أسبغ بدون ذلك أجزأه وإن يكفه زاد عليه لأن طباع الناس وأحوالهم تختلف، حتى كذا في البدائع ويقل النووي الإجماع على عدم لزوم التقدير. وفي الخلاصة : والأفضل أن لا يقتصر على الصاع في الغسل بل يغتسل بأزيد أن لا يؤدي إلى الوسواس فإن أدى لا منه بعد يستعمل إلا قدر الحاجة .اهـ. ولا يخفى ما فيه فإن ظاهره أنه يزيد على الصاع وإن لم يكن به حاجة مع أن الثابت في صحيح مسلم أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يغتسل بالصاع ويتوضأ بالمد، وفي البخارى اغتساله الله بالصاع من رواية جابر وعائشة كما نقله النووي في شرح المهذب فكان الاقتصار على ما فعله صلى الله عليه وسلم أفضل إذا اكتفى به وقد قالوا: إن مكث في الماء الجاري قدر الوضوء والغسل فقد أكمل السنة وإلا فلا ا هـ . ويقاس على ما لو توضأ في الحوض الكبير أو وقف في المطر كما لا يخفى.
The third indication: All the sunan and mandubat in wudu are established in this wudu and ghusl. Thus, intention (niyyah) is sunnah and it is commendable (yandubu biha). Al-Bada'i' said: The etiquettes (adab) of ghusl are the etiquettes of wudu, except that from the etiquettes of wudu is facing the qibla, contrary to ghusl, because it often involves uncovering the private parts, unlike wudu. That is as in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. Among its makruhat is extravagance (israf), which has been interpreted earlier. For this reason, Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) estimated in the apparent (zahir) riwaya the sa' for ghusl and the mud for wudu, which is an estimate of minimal sufficiency customarily, and it is not a binding estimate; that he who does abundantly without that is sufficient, and if it suffices him, he should increase beyond it, because the natures of people and their circumstances differ. That is as in al-Bada'i'. And al-Nawawi relates consensus on the non-necessity of the estimate. In al-Khulasa: It is preferable not to confine oneself to the sa' in ghusl, but rather to perform ghusl with more, provided it does not lead to waswasa; if it does, then he should not use more than the amount of need. It is not hidden what is in it, for its apparent meaning is that he increases beyond the sa' even if there is no need, while it is established in Sahih Muslim that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would perform ghusl with a sa' and wudu with a mud, and in Bukhari his ghusl with a sa' from the narration of Jabir and Aisha as al-Nawawi transmitted in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab. So restricting oneself to what the Prophet did is better if it suffices him. And they said: If he stays in flowing water for the duration of wudu and ghusl, then he has completed the sunnah; otherwise not. That is analogous to one who performs wudu in a large basin or stands in the rain, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a clear enumeration of the sunan and adab of ghusl. It begins by stating the 'third indication': that all sunan (recommended acts) and mandubat (commendable acts) of wudu also apply to the wudu that is part of ghusl (i.e., the initial washing of hands, mouth, nose, face, etc.) and to the ghusl itself. Thus, the niyyah (intention) is sunnah. Al-Bada'i' clarifies that the adab of ghusl are the same as those of wudu, except facing qibla: in wudu it is a sunnah, but in ghusl it is not because ghusl often involves uncovering the private parts (awrah). Among the makruhat of ghusl is israf (extravagance in water usage). Hence, Imam Muhammad estimated the sa' (approx. 2.1 liters) for ghusl and mud (approx. 0.5 liters) for wudu as a minimal sufficiency, but this is not a binding limit. One may use more if needed, but the best is to follow the Prophet's practice of using one sa' for ghusl. The text then quotes al-Khulasa suggesting it is afdal (better) to use more than a sa' if it does not lead to waswasa (obsessive doubts). However, the commentator (Ibn Nujaym) critiques this, noting that it seems to encourage extra water even without need, while the authentic hadith shows the Prophet used a sa'. The correct view is that the Prophet's action is best if it suffices. Finally, the passage analogizes that staying in flowing water for the duration of wudu and ghusl is equivalent to completing the sunnah, as it ensures the water is not used excessively.

Key Terms
الصاع (al-ṣā'): A volume measure, approximately 2.1 liters (according to Hanafi), used as the minimal water estimate for ghusl.
المد (al-mudd): A volume measure, approximately 0.5 liters, used as the minimal water estimate for wudu.
الإسراف (al-isrāf): Extravagance or waste, especially in water usage during purification. It is makruh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on facing the qibla during ghusl?
A) It is sunnah.
B) It is makruh.
C) It is not sunnah due to uncovering of the private parts.
D) It is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The sunan of wudu apply to ghusl except facing qibla, and the water estimates (sa', mud) are non-binding guidelines to avoid israf.

A Woman Does Not Need to Undo Her Braids in Ghusl If Water Reaches the Roots
A ruling with proof clarifying a woman's ghusl obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on undoing braids in ghusl and identify the condition that triggers the obligation to undo them.

Core Idea
A woman's braids need not be undone if water reaches the roots – condition over form.

This passage addresses a common question: must a woman undo her braids when performing ghusl? The Hanafi school provides a clear, practical answer rooted in prophetic practice. The key is not the braid itself but whether water reaches the scalp. Understanding this distinction helps avoid unnecessary hardship while preserving the essential obligation of ghusl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that a woman does not have to undo her braid (ضفيرة) during ghusl. The ruling is that undoing is not obligatory (wajib).
The action is the act of undoing braids; the ruling is its non-obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Umm Salamah (رضي الله عنها) narrated by Muslim and others, where the Prophet ﷺ instructed her that pouring water over the head suffices.
The hadith is ahad (single narration) but accepted by Hanafis.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's instruction indicates that undoing braids is not required; the obligation is fulfilled by ensuring water reaches the roots. The word 'sufficient' implies no extra act is needed.
The key is the implication (dalālah) of the command: doing less than the commanded suffices.
4
Note the condition
The ruling is conditional: 'if water reaches the roots' (إن بل أصلها). If braids prevent water from reaching the scalp, then undoing becomes necessary.
Condition (shart) overrides the general permissibility.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is and Hanbalis require undoing braids if water cannot reach the roots even if braided; Hanafis condition it solely on whether water reaches the roots.
The practical difference: under Hanafi, if water can seep through, undoing is not needed; others demand physical undoing.

Source Text

قوله (ولا تنقض ضفيرة إن بل أصلها أي ولا يجب على المرأة أن تنقض ضفيرتها إن بلت في الاغتسال أصل شعرها والضفيرة بالضاد المعجمة الذؤابة من الضفر وهو قتل الشعر وإدخال بعضه في بعض ولا يقال بالظاء، والأصل فيه ما رواه مسلم وغيره عن أم سلمة ... البحر الرائق/ ج ١ م ٧
His saying 'And she does not undo her braid if its root becomes wet': i.e., it is not obligatory for a woman to undo her braid if during ghusl the root of her hair becomes wet. Al-dafira (ضفيرة) with the dotted daad is the lock of hair from al-dafr (ضفر), which is braiding hair and interweaving some into others; it is not said with za. The basis for this is what Muslim and others narrated from Umm Salamah... (text cuts off).
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific issue in ghusl for women: the obligation of undoing braids (ضفيرة). The ruling is that a woman does NOT have to undo her braids when performing ghusl, provided that water reaches the roots of her hair (أصل الشعر). The word ضفيرة (with ضاد) refers to braided hair, from the root ضفر meaning to plait. It is not written with ظاء. The proof is the hadith of Umm Salamah [in Sahih Muslim] where she asked the Prophet about braids, and he replied that it is sufficient to pour water over the head. The text cuts off before completing the hadith, but the ruling is clear: undoing braids is not obligatory. This is a concession for women to ease the obligation of ghusl. The key condition is that water must reach the roots (أصل الشعر). If water does not reach the roots due to tight braids, then the braids must be undone to ensure water reaches the scalp.

Key Terms
الضفيرة (al-ḍafīrah): A braid or plait of hair, specifically when water must reach the roots during ghusl.
أصل الشعر (aṣl al-sha'r): The roots of the hair where it emerges from the scalp, the critical point for the validity of ghusl.

Key Takeaway

Ruling on Towel Use and Recommended Water Amounts
Discussion of towel use and recommended water amounts with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using a towel after wudu/ghusl and explain the recommended water amounts (sa' and mudd) and their legal status.

Core Idea
Using a towel after ablution is permissible; the sa' and mudd are recommended minimal sufficiencies, not binding obligations.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author addresses two common practical issues: whether one may use a towel to dry off after wudu or ghusl, and what amount of water is recommended for these acts. While both questions may seem mundane, they illustrate an important Hanafi principle: that the Prophet's practice (sunnah) establishes a recommended guideline, not a rigid obligation, and that individual circumstances may warrant deviation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage addresses (1) using a towel after wudu/ghusl and (2) the recommended water amounts (sa' and mudd). Determine the hukm level for each.
Towel use: mubah (permissible) according to majority; water amounts: sunnah (recommended) but not wajib.
2
Examine the evidence for towel use
The passage cites Mirqat al-Diraya and others for permissibility. Note that only the author of Munyat al-Musalli considered it mustahabb. Identify the basis: general permissibility (ibaha) and no explicit prohibition.
3
Examine the evidence for water amounts
Imam Muhammad's estimation in Zahir al-Riwayah is based on the Prophet's practice (sunnah). The hadith from Sahih Muslim and Bukhari is cited: the Prophet used a sa' for ghusl and a mudd for wudu.
The dalil is the Prophet's consistent practice, which indicates recommendation (sunnah) but not obligation.
4
Analyze the legal status: sunnah vs. wajib
The text emphasizes that the estimates are 'adna al-kifayah' (minimal sufficiency) and not binding. One may use more or less. The Prophet's practice is best if sufficient, but if one needs more, it is allowed.
This illustrates the distinction between sunnah (recommended) and wajib (obligatory) in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Identify the tarjih
The author prefers following the Prophet's specific amounts if they suffice, criticizing the opinion that recommends exceeding without need. The mufta bihi is that using the sa' and mudd is mustahabb, and using a towel is mubah.
The authority weight is from fatawa mutakhkhirin (later works).

Book of Purification. ... It is reported in Mirqat al-Diraya and others that there is no harm in wiping with a towel for the one performing wudu and ghusl, provided he does not exaggerate and thoroughly dry leaving no trace of wudu on his limbs. I have not seen anyone explicitly stating it is recommended except the author of Munyat al-Musalli who said: It is recommended to wipe with a towel after washing. The third indication is that all the sunan and mustahabbat of wudu are established in this wudu and ghusl, so the intention is sunnah and it is recommended with it. He said in al-Bada'i': The etiquettes of ghusl are the etiquettes of wudu except that from the etiquettes of wudu is facing the qibla, unlike ghusl because it usually involves exposing the private parts, unlike wudu. ... And from its makruh is extravagance, and its explanation has preceded. For this reason, Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) estimated in Zahir al-Riwayah the sa' for ghusl and the mudd for wudu, and this is an estimate of the minimal sufficiency customarily, and it is not a binding estimate, so that whoever performs a complete ablution without that, it suffices him, and if it does not suffice him, he adds more, because people's natures and conditions differ. ... In al-Khulasa: The best is not to limit oneself to the sa' in ghusl, but to bathe with more, provided it does not lead to waswasa; if it does, then after that he should not use more than the need. ... And it is not hidden what is in it, for its apparent meaning is that he increases beyond the sa' even if he has no need, while it is established in Sahih Muslim that the Prophet (saw) used to bathe with a sa' and perform wudu with a mudd, and in al-Bukhari his bathing with a sa' from the narration of Jabir and Aisha, as al-Nawawi transmitted in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab; so limiting oneself to what the Prophet (saw) did is better if one is satisfied with it. And they said: If one remains in flowing water for the duration of wudu and ghusl, he has completed the sunnah, otherwise not. And it is analogized to one who performs wudu in a large basin or stands in the rain, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage discusses two rulings: (1) the ruling on using a towel after wudu and ghusl, and (2) the recommended amount of water for these acts. The author begins by clarifying that there is no harm in using a towel to dry oneself after ablution. However, he cautions against excessive drying that removes all traces of water, as leaving some moisture may be a sunnah. He notes that most scholars do not state it as recommended (mustahabb), except the author of Munyat al-Musalli. Then he turns to the water estimation: Imam Muhammad estimated in Zahir al-Riwayah that a sa' (approximately 2.5 liters) is sufficient for ghusl and a mudd (approximately 0.625 liters) for wudu. Importantly, this is only a minimal estimate based on the Prophet's practice, not a binding requirement. One may use less or more water as needed. The passage criticizes an opinion that recommends using more than the sa' without need, citing that the Prophet always used the sa' and mudd. Therefore, following his example is better if the smaller amount suffices. The author also mentions that if one bathes in flowing water for the duration of ghusl, that completes the sunnah. This shows the Hanafi concern with balancing recommended practice and individual circumstances.

Key Terms
منديل (mindiil): A towel or cloth used for drying after ablution.
صاع (saa'): A cubic measure equal to approximately 2.5 liters, used for ghusl.
مد (mudd): A cubic measure equal to approximately 0.625 liters, used for wudu.
استحباب (istihbaab): Recommendation; an action that brings reward but whose omission is not sinful.

D) It is makruh to use a towel.

Key Takeaway
Using a towel after wudu/ghusl is permissible, and the sa' and mudd are recommended minimal water amounts, not binding obligations.

Ruling on a Woman Undoing Braids in Ghusl
Detailed discussion of whether a woman must undo braids for ghusl with three opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman undoing her braids for ghusl, identify the three opinions within the school, and apply the exception for thick hair.

Core Idea
A woman does not need to undo her braids for ghusl unless water cannot reach the roots.

The issue of whether a woman must undo her braids during ghusl is a classic example of how the Hanafi school balances primary texts and considers hardship. This lesson unpacks the three opinions within the school and the relied-upon ruling, based on the hadith of Umm Salamah and other evidences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
The act is ghusl for janabah or menstruation. The default ruling in the matn is 'she does not undo her braid if its root becomes wet.'
This is the starting point from the author's matn.
2
Analyze the primary proof
Examine the hadith of Umm Salamah: the Prophet said 'No' when asked if she must undo her braid, indicating non-obligation.
The hadith is authentic (Sahih Muslim).
3
Examine the counter-proof and opinions
Some Hanafi scholars cited the hadith of Hudhayfah requiring water to reach roots. This leads to three opinions: non-obligation, obligation with squeezing, and obligation to wash braids entirely.
The passage reconciles these by considering hardship.
4
Reconcile the three opinions
The majority view (al-Hidayah) is non-obligation. A second view requires wetting three times with squeezing. A third (Salah al-Baqqali) requires washing braids even if long.
The relied-upon view is the first, with an exception for very thick hair.
5
Determine mufta bihi and exception
The mufta bihi is non-obligation, but for thick hair (like Turks and Alawites) where water cannot reach roots, undoing becomes wajib.
This balances the hadith of Umm Salamah with the objective of ensuring root wetting.

أر من صرح باستحبابه إلا صاحب منية المصلي الخ) قال الشرنبلالي في إمداد الفتاح: واستدل له شارح المنية الحلبي بما روته عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها قالت: كان للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم خرقة يتنشف بها بعد الوضوء. رواه الترمذي وهو ضعيف. ولكن يجوز العمل بالضعيف في الفضائل اهـ. ولا يخفى أن المدعى التنشيف بعد الغسل والمروي في الوضوء .اهـ. وقد يقال لا فرق بينهما على أنه سيأتي قريباً أن آداب الغسل هي آداب الوضوء سوى استقبال القبلة تأمل قول المصنف : (ولا تنقض ضفيرة الخ) في النهر : بالبناء للمفعول لقوله إن بل أصلها إذ لو بناه للفاعل لقال إن بلت كذا في الشرح وفيه نظر، وما المانع من أن يكون الأول مبنياً للفاعل والثاني للمفعول نعم الأنسب كون الفعلين البحر الرائق/ ج ١ م ٧

الرجال حتى
قالت قلت یا رسول الله إني إمرأة أشد ضفر رأسي أفانقضه لغسل الجنابة؟ فقال: لا إنما يكفيك أن تحثي على رأسك ثلاث حثيات ثم تفيضين عليك الماء فتطهرين. وفي رواية «أفأنقضه للحيض والجنابة. وفي حديث عائشة بنحو معناه. قال في فتح القدير : ومقتضى هذا الحديث عدم وجوب الإيصال إلى الأصول لكن قال في المبسوط : وإنما شرط تبليغ الماء أصول الشعر لحديث حذيفة فإنه كان يجلس إلى جنب امرأته إذا اغتسلت ويقول: يا هذه أبلغي الماء أصول شعرك وشؤن رأسك وهو مجمع عظام الرأس، ذكره القاضي عياض وأورد صاحب المعراج أن حديث أم سلمة معارض للكتاب وأجاب تارة بالمنع فإن مؤدي الكتاب غسل البدن والشعر ليس منه بل متصل به نظراً إلى أصوله فعملنا بمقتضى الاتصال في حق قلنا يجب النقض على الأتراك والعلويين على الصحيح ويجب عليها الإيصال إلى أثناء شعرها إذا كان منقوضاً لعدم الحرج وبمقتضى الانفصال في حق النساء دفعاً للحرج إذ لا يمكنهن حلقه، وتارة بأنه خص من الآية مواضع الضرورة كداخل العينين فيخص بالحديث بعده. وأما أمر عبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص رضي الله عنهما بنقض النساء رؤوسهن إذا اغتسلن فيحتمل أنه أراد إيجاب ذلك عليهن في شعور لا يصل الماء إليها أو يكون مذهباً له أنه يجب النقض بكل حال كما هو مذهب النخعي أو لا يكون بلغه حديث أم سلمة وعائشة، ويحتمل أنه كان يأمرهن بذلك على الاستحباب والاحتياط لا على الوجوب كذا ذكره النووي في شرح مسلم. وفي الهداية : وليس عليها بل ذوائبها هو الصحيح. وقال بعضهم : يجب بلها ثلاثاً مع كل بلة عصرة. وفي صلاة البقالي الصحيح أنه يجب غسل الذوائب وإن جاوزت القدمين والمختار عدم الوجوب كما صرح به في الجامع الحسامي كما نقله عنه في المضمرات للحصر المذكور في الحديث والحاصل أن في المسألة ثلاثة أقوال :
على نسق واحد، وفيه إيماء إلى وجوب غسل أثنائها لو كانت منقوضة لعدم الحرج ومن ثم رجح في المعراج وجوب النقض في الأتراك والعلوية ودعوى الحرج فيهما أيضاً ممنوعة. بقي أن بناءه للمفعول يؤذن بعدم وجوب النقض فيهما أيضاً وقد سبق أن الراجح خلافه والجواب أن التنوين بدل عن المضاف إليه أي صغيرة المرأة وحذفها اختصاراً كما في الشرح. وبهذا علم أن قوله في البحر إن ظاهر الكتاب الاكتفاء بالوصول إلى الأصول ولو منقوضة غير ظاهر، وإذا لم يجب مع الضفر الوصول . إلى الأثناء فالذوائب أولى وهو الأصح وهذا أولى مما في صلاة البقالي من ترجيح الوجوب وإن جاوزت القدمين اهـ. والإشارة بقوله وبهذا العلم الخ إلى ما ذكره من الإيماء، وتأمل ما المراد بقوله وإذا لم يجب مع الضفر الخ ) فإن الذوائب هي الضفائر وما وجه الأولوية. قوله : (أبلغي الماء أصول شعرك وشؤن رأسك الخ) قال في الحلية والشؤون بضم الشين المعجمة بعدها همزة في الأصل الخطوط التي في عظم الجمجمة وهو مجتمع شعب عظامها الواحد شأن والمراد ههنا أصول شعر
His statement: 'And she does not undo her braid if its root becomes wet' means it is not obligatory for a woman to undo her braid if the root of her hair becomes wet during ghusl. The braid (al-dafirah) is the lock of hair from plaiting, which is the intertwining of hair and inserting some into others. It is not said with za. The basis for this is what Muslim and others narrated from Umm Salamah... She said: I said, O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who strongly plaits my hair; shall I undo it for ghusl of janabah? He said: No, it is enough for you to pour three handfuls on your head, then pour water over you and you become purified. In another narration: 'Shall I undo it for menstruation and janabah?' And in the hadith of Aisha similarly... In Fath al-Qadir: The implication of this hadith is that it is not obligatory to make water reach the roots. But in al-Mabsut: He conditioned the water reaching the roots of the hair because of the hadith of Hudhayfah, as he used to sit beside his wife when she bathed and say: O this one, make water reach the roots of your hair and the joints of your head. ... The author of al-Mi'raj stated that the hadith of Umm Salamah contradicts the Book, and he answered sometimes by denial ... sometimes by saying that it is a special dispensation for women to remove hardship... As for the command of Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As that women should undo their braids when bathing, it is possible he intended it for hair that water does not reach, or it was his own opinion, or he had not heard the hadith of Umm Salamah... In al-Hidayah: The correct view is that she is not required to undo her braids. Some said: she must wet them three times with squeezing each time. In Salah al-Baqqali: The correct view is that she must wash the braids even if they exceed the feet, but the chosen view is that it is not obligatory, as stated in al-Jami' al-Husami... The summary: there are three opinions on the matter. ... And the indication is that the judgment is built on the action of the Prophet. ... The phrase 'make water reach the roots of your hair and the joints (shu'un) of your head' the word shu'un is the plural of sha'n, meaning the lines of the skull, and here it means the roots of the hair.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage deals with a classic Hanafi issue: Must a woman undo her braids when performing ghusl? The author explains the matn statement, clarifying that it is not wajib. He provides the hadith of Umm Salamah as proof, in which the Prophet explicitly said not to undo the braid. However, there is also the hadith of Hudhayfah which instructs making water reach the roots. The author then presents reconciliation attempts: some argue that the braid ruling is specific to women due to hardship, while men with thick hair may need to undo theirs. The passage lists three opinions: (1) the correct view in al-Hidayah is that there is no obligation to undo braids; (2) some scholars say it is obligatory to wet braids three times with squeezing; (3) in Salah al-Baqqali the opinion is that washing the braids is obligatory even if they exceed the feet, but the preferred view is non-obligation. The author gives preference to the view of non-obligation, but also notes an exception for women with very thick hair (like Turks and Alawites) where undoing may be required. The discussion highlights the Hanafi method of reconciling primary sources and the consideration of hardship.

Key Terms
ضفيرة (dafiirah): A braid or plait of hair.
ذوائب (dhawa'ib): Locks of hair, often referring to braids that hang down.
شؤن (shu'un): The lines of the skull (sutures); here meaning the roots of the hair.
حثيات (hathiyaat): Handfuls (three handfuls of water).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab as presented in the passage, what is the default ruling on a woman undoing her braids for ghusl?
A) She must undo them.
B) She should undo them.
C) She does not have to undo them.
D) She must cut them.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab does not obligate a woman to undo her braids for ghusl as long as water reaches the roots of her hair, but exceptions exist for extremely thick hair.

The Hanafi Ruling on Unbraiding Hair for Ghusl
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ghusl hair washing and husband's water cost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on unbraiding hair for ghusl, identify the mufta bihi view, and explain the evidence for the preferred position.

Core Idea
A woman need not undo her braids for ghusl; reaching the roots suffices.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a common question for women: must she undo her braided hair when performing ghusl? The Hanafi school has three internal opinions, and the relied-upon view is that unbraiding is not required, as long as water reaches the roots. This ruling is based on the hadith of Umm Salama and the principle of avoiding hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Hanafi opinions
List the three positions: (1) sufficiency of root contact whether braided or not; (2) root contact sufficient if braided, but must reach inner parts if undone; (3) must wet locks with squeezing.
These are all Hanafi views, not other madhhabs.
2
Examine the evidence for each opinion
The first opinion relies on the hadith of Umm Salama; the second on the hadith of Hudhayfa and the command of Abdullah ibn Amr; the third on the need to ensure complete coverage.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq evaluates these proofs.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to opposing proofs
The hadith of Umm Salama is specific and overrides general commands. The command of Abdullah ibn Amr is interpreted as recommendation or for special cases.
The principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj) is invoked.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The first opinion is preferred because it is the apparent view of the madhhab, supported by al-Dhakhira and al-Hidayah, and aligns with the hadith of Umm Salama.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Consider a woman with tightly braided hair performing ghusl. Under the mufta bihi view, she pours water over her head ensuring it reaches the roots; she does not need to undo her braids.
If water cannot reach roots due to braiding, she must undo.
