الماء إليها أو يكون مذهباً له أنه يجب النقض بكل حال كما هو مذهب النخعي أو لا يكون بلغه حديث أم سلمة وعائشة، ويحتمل أنه كان يأمرهن بذلك على الاستحباب والاحتياط لا على الوجوب كذا ذكره النووي في شرح مسلم. وفي الهداية : وليس عليها بل ذوائبها هو الصحيح. وقال بعضهم : يجب بلها ثلاثاً مع كل بلة عصرة. وفي صلاة البقالي الصحيح أنه يجب غسل الذوائب وإن جاوزت القدمين والمختار عدم الوجوب كما صرح به في الجامع الحسامي كما نقله عنه في المضمرات للحصر المذكور في الحديث والحاصل أن في المسألة ثلاثة أقوال : على نسق واحد، وفيه إيماء إلى وجوب غسل أثنائها لو كانت منقوضة لعدم الحرج ومن ثم رجح في المعراج وجوب النقض في الأتراك والعلوية ودعوى الحرج فيهما أيضاً ممنوعة. بقي أن بناءه للمفعول يؤذن بعدم وجوب النقض فيهما أيضاً وقد سبق أن الراجح خلافه والجواب أن التنوين بدل عن المضاف إليه أي صغيرة المرأة وحذفها اختصاراً كما في الشرح. وبهذا علم أن قوله في البحر إن ظاهر الكتاب الاكتفاء بالوصول إلى الأصول ولو منقوضة غير ظاهر، وإذا لم يجب مع الضفر الوصول . إلى الأثناء فالذوائب أولى وهو الأصح وهذا أولى مما في صلاة البقالي من ترجيح الوجوب وإن جاوزت القدمين اهـ. والإشارة بقوله وبهذا علم الخ إلى ما ذكره من الإيماء، وتأمل ما المراد بقوله وإذا لم يجب مع الضفر الخ ) فإن الذوائب هي الضفائر وما وجه الأولوية. قوله : (أبلغي الماء أصول شعرك وشؤن رأسك الخ) قال في الحلية والشؤون بضم الشين المعجمة بعدها همزة في الأصل الخطوط التي في عظم الجمجمة وهو مجتمع شعب عظامها الواحد شأن والمراد ههنا أصول شعر رأسها . قوله: (منقوضاً كان أو معقوصاً) أي مضفوراً. قال في القاموس : عقص شعره يعقصه ضفره وقتله والعقصة بالكسر العقيصة والضفيرة قوله : (وهو ظاهر المذهب كما هو ظاهر الذخيرة) أي أن ظاهر كلام الذخيرة أن هذا هو المذهب. قال شارح المنية العلامة ابن أمير حاج الحلبي : وهذا فيما يظهر من الذخيرة أنه ظاهر المذهب اهـ. فما في بعض النسخ من قوله وهو ظاهر المتن غير صحيح بل ظاهر المتن هو القول الثاني اهـ . قوله : ( يجب بهذه المعاني على طريق البدل) أي أن أتي معنى إذا وجد من هذه المعاني يجب به الغسل ولا مدخل لهذا في الرد فالأولى الاقتصار على قوله الأول الإكتفاء بالوصول إلى الأصول منقوضاً كان أو معقوصاً وهو ظاهر المذهب كما هو ظاهر الذخيرة ويدل عليه الأحاديث الواردة في هذا الباب الثاني الإكتفاء بالوصول إلى الأصول إذا كان مضفوراً ووجوب الإيصال إلى أثنائه إذا كان منقوضاً ومشى عليه جماعة منهم صاحب المحيط والبدائع والكافي. الثالث وجوب بل الذوائب مع العصر وصحح قدمناه. ولو ألزقت المرأة رأسها بالطيب بحيث لا يصل الماء إلى أصول الشعر وجب عليها إزالته . وثمن ماء غسل المرأة ووضوئها على الزوج وإن كانت غنية كذا في فتح القدير فصار كماء الشرب لأن هذا مما لا بد منه وظاهره أنه لا فرق بين غسل الجنابة وغيره من هي الواجب. وذكر في السراج الوهاج تفصيلاً في غسل الحيض فقال : إذا انقطع لأقل من عشرة فعلى الزوج لاحتياجه إلى وطئها بعد الغسل، وإن انقطع لعشرة فعليها لأنها المحتاجة إليه للصلاة. وقد يقال : إن ما تحتاج إليه المرأة مما لا بد لها منه واجب عليه، سواء كان هو محتاجاً إليه أو لا، فالأوجه إطلاق ما قدمناه .
She said: I said, O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman who tightly braids my hair; should I undo it for ghusl from janabah? He said: No, it is sufficient for you to pour three handfuls on your head, then pour water over yourself and you become pure. And in a narration: 'Should I undo it for menstruation and janabah?' And in the hadith of Aisha similarly. He said in Fath al-Qadir: The implication of this hadith is that reaching the roots is not obligatory. But it was said in al-Mabsut: The condition is that water reaches the roots of the hair due to the hadith of Hudhayfa, for he used to sit next to his wife when she bathed and say: O this one, make water reach the roots of your hair and the shu'un of your head, which is the meeting place of the bones of the head, mentioned by Qadi Iyad. And the author of al-Mi'raj argued that the hadith of Umm Salama contradicts the Book, and he answered sometimes by denial, for the import of the Book is washing the body, and hair is not part of it but attached to it by considering its roots; so we acted according to the implication of attachment concerning [women]? He said: It is obligatory to undo [braids] for Turks and Alawites according to the correct view, and it is obligatory for her to make water reach the inner parts of her hair if it is undone due to lack of hardship, and according to the implication of separation concerning women to avoid hardship since they cannot shave it. And sometimes [he answered] that from the verse the places of necessity are excluded, like the inner parts of the eyes, so it is excluded by the hadith after it. As for the order of Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As, may Allah be pleased with them, that women should undo their heads when they bathe, it is probable that he intended to make it obligatory for them concerning hair that water does not reach, or that it is his [personal] opinion that undoing is obligatory in any case, as is the opinion of al-Nakha'i, or that the hadith of Umm Salama and Aisha did not reach him. And it is probable that he ordered them to do so on the basis of recommendation and caution, not obligation. Thus mentioned al-Nawawi in Sharh Muslim. And in al-Hidayah: She is not required to wash the locks of hair; that is the correct [view]. And some said: It is obligatory to wet them three times with a squeeze each time. And in Salat al-Baqqali: The correct [view] is that washing the locks is obligatory even if they exceed the feet, but the chosen [view] is non-obligation as stated in al-Jami' al-Husami as quoted from it in al-Mudmarat due to the restriction mentioned in the hadith. The summary is that there are three opinions in this issue: ... in one sequence, and it contains an indication of the obligation to wash its inner parts if it were undone due to lack of hardship. Hence al-Mi'raj preferred the obligation of undoing for Turks and Alawites, and the claim of hardship for them is also denied. There remains that its being built for the passive indicates non-obligation of undoing for them also, and it has preceded that the preponderant is contrary; the answer is that the tanwin stands for the mudaf ilayh i.e., 'small woman' and its omission for brevity as in the sharh. By this it is known that his statement in al-Bahr that the apparent [meaning] of the Book is that reaching the roots is sufficient even if undone is not apparent. And if reaching the inner parts is not obligatory with braiding, then the locks are more deserving, and this is the most correct, and this is more appropriate than what is in Salat al-Baqqali of preferring obligation even if they exceed the feet. And the reference by his statement 'by this it is known' etc. is to what he mentioned of indication. And consider what is meant by his statement 'and if reaching is not obligatory with braiding etc.', for the locks are the braids, and what is the aspect of priority? His statement (make water reach the roots of your hair and the shu'un of your head etc.) He said in al-Hilya: al-shu'un with damma shin and hamzah originally are the lines in the skull bone, which is the meeting place of its branches, its singular is shan; and what is meant here is the roots of the hair of her head. His statement (whether undone or braided) i.e., braided. He said in al-Qamus: 'aqasa sha'rahu ya'qisuhu: he braided it and twisted it; and al-'uqsa by kasr is the braid. His statement (and it is the apparent [view] of the madhhab as is apparent from al-Dhakhira) i.e., the apparent [meaning] of the words of al-Dhakhira is that this is the madhhab. Sharh al-Munyah's author, the scholar Ibn Amir Haj al-Halabi, said: This is what appears from al-Dhakhira that it is the apparent [view] of the madhhab. So what is in some copies of his statement 'and it is the apparent [view] of the matn' is incorrect; rather the apparent [view] of the matn is the second opinion. His statement (it is obligatory by these meanings by way of substitution) i.e., if a meaning occurs from these meanings, ghusl becomes obligatory by it; and this has no entry in the refutation, so it is better to limit oneself to his statement: The first: sufficing with the reaching of the roots whether undone or braided, and it is the apparent [view] of the madhhab as is apparent from al-Dhakhira, and the ahadith in this chapter indicate it. The second: sufficing with reaching to the roots if braided, and obligation of reaching to its inner parts if undone; and a group followed this, including the author of al-Muhit, al-Bada'i', and al-Kafi. The third: obligation to wet the locks with squeezing, and we have presented the correct [view]. And if a woman affixed her head with perfume such that water cannot reach the roots of the hair, it is obligatory for her to remove it. And the price of the water for a woman's ghusl and wudu is upon the husband even if she is rich; thus in Fath al-Qadir, so it becomes like drinking water because this is something necessary. Its apparent [meaning] is that there is no difference between janabah ghusl and other obligatory baths. And it was mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj a detail concerning menstruation ghusl: if it stops before ten days, it is upon the husband because of his need to have intercourse with her after the bath; and if it stops at ten days, it is upon her because she needs it for prayer. And it may be said: what the woman needs of what is necessary for her is obligatory upon him, whether he needs it or not; so the most appropriate is the absolute [ruling] we have presented.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses the Hanafi ruling on whether a woman must undo her braids (naqd al-dafr) when performing ghusl (ritual bath). The author presents three opinions within the Hanafi school, supported by hadith and rational arguments. The first opinion, which is the relied-upon (mu'tamad) view, holds that it is sufficient for water to reach the roots of the hair, regardless of whether the hair is braided or undone. This is based on the hadith of Umm Salama, where the Prophet (PBUH) told her that pouring three handfuls of water over the head suffices. The second opinion distinguishes between braided and undone hair: if braided, reaching the roots is enough; if undone, water must reach the inner parts (athna'). The third opinion requires wetting the locks (dhawā'ib) even if they exceed the feet, with squeezing. The author ultimately favors the first view, arguing that it is the apparent madhhab and supported by the primary texts. The passage also discusses the husband's obligation to pay for the water used by his wife for ghusl and wudu, likening it to drinking water, and notes a detail regarding menstruation ghusl. The commentary clarifies that the three positions are all Hanafi and the selection of the first is based on the preponderance of evidence.

Key Terms
ضفر (dafr): Braiding of hair tightly.
ذوائب (dhawā'ib): Locks of hair, especially those that hang down, possibly exceeding the feet.
نقض (naqd): Unbraiding or undoing the hair.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view in this passage, what is the ruling on a woman with braided hair performing ghusl?
A) She must undo her braids completely.
B) She must ensure water reaches the roots, and undoing is not required.
C) She must wash each lock three times with squeezing.
D) She must shave her hair if braided.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi view is that a woman need not undo her braids for ghusl; she must only ensure water reaches the roots of her hair.

Taharah — Purification

Cause of Obligation of Ghusl: Sabab vs Shart
Definition and refinement of the legal cause for ghusl obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sabab and shart in the obligation of ghusl and state the preferred Hanafi position.

Core Idea
The intention to perform a forbidden act without purity is the sabab; emission of mani is only a shart.

In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq refines the definition of what actually triggers the obligation of ghusl. While the matn mentions mani, a deeper analysis reveals a dispute among Hanafi scholars: is the emission itself the cause, or is it the intention to perform acts prohibited during janabah? This lesson unpacks the distinction between sabab and shart, central to Hanafi usul, and clarifies the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn and its apparent meaning
Read the opening of the passage: 'And obligatory upon [occurrence of] mani with emission and desire at its separation.' Note that the matn seems to tie the obligation to the physical event.
This is the starting point that prompts the scholarly investigation.
2
Understand the objection from al-Nihayah
Al-Nihayah objects: 'These meanings necessitate janabah, not ghusl, for they nullify [purity] so how can they obligate it?' This highlights the logical problem of impurity causing its own removal.
This objection forces a refinement of the cause.
3
Examine the responses: substitution, no contradiction, shart vs sabab
Three responses are given: (1) Ghusl is obligatory by way of substitution; (2) No contradiction because impurity nullifies past purity and obligates future purity; (3) The preferred response: the physical events are shurut (conditions), not asbab (causes). The obligation arises from the intention to perform prohibited acts.
The third response uses the analogy of zakat al-fitr to show metaphorical attribution.
4
Analyze the preferred view: intention as sabab
Al-Kafi and Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam state: 'The cause of obligation of ghusl is the intention to do what is not permissible according to the majority.' This aligns intention with the obligation.
This view avoids the logical issue and fits the broader Hanafi emphasis on intention.
5
Apply the sabab-shart distinction to the analogy of zakat al-fitr
Just as zakat al-fitr is metaphorically attributed to 'fitr' (breaking fast) though the true cause is possession of wealth and the obligation to give charity, similarly, ghusl is metaphorically attributed to mani, but the true cause is intention.
This analogy reinforces the principle that attribution to a condition does not make it a cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وفرض عند مني ذي دفق وشهوة عند انفصاله أي وفرض الغسل. واختلف المشايخ في سبب وجوبه فظاهر ما في الهداية أن إنزال المني ونحوه سبب له فإنه قال : المعاني الموجبة للغسل إنزال المني إلى آخره. وتعقبه في النهاية بأن هذه معان موجبة للجنابة لا للغسل على المذهب الصحيح من علمائنا فإنها تنقضه فكيف توجبه؟ ورده في غاية البيان بأن المراد أن الغسل يجب بهذه المعاني على طريق البدل وإنما يتوجه ما اعترض به إذا كانت هذه المعاني موجبة لوجود الغسل لا لوجوبه ورد أيضاً بأنها تنقض ما كان وتوجب ما سيكون فلا منافاة. وأجاب في المستصفى أيضاً بأن هذه المعاني شروط في الوجوب لا أسباب فأضيف الوجوب إلى الشرط مجازاً كقولهم صدقة الفطر لأن السبب يتعلق به الوجود والوجوب والشرط يضاف إليه الوجود فشارك الشرط السبب في الوجود وقال في الكافي : وإنما قال «عند مني» ولم يقل بمني لأن سبب وجوب الغسل الصلاة أو إرادة ما لا يحل مع الجنابة والإنزال والالتقاء. وفي مبسوط شيخ الإسلام : سبب وجوب الغسل إرادة ما لا يحل فعله عند عامة المشايخ وتعقبه في غاية البيان بأن الغسل يجب إذا وجد أحد هذه المعاني وجدت
His statement (And obligatory upon [occurrence of] mani with emission and desire at its separation) i.e., obligatory is ghusl. And the mashayikh differed regarding the cause of its obligation. The apparent [meaning] in al-Hidayah is that the ejaculation of mani and the like is a cause for it, for he said: The meanings that necessitate ghusl are ejaculation of mani etc. It was followed up in al-Nihayah that these meanings necessitate janabah, not ghusl, according to the correct [view] of our scholars, for they nullify [purity] so how can they obligate it? And it was refuted in Ghayat al-Bayan that the intended meaning is that ghusl becomes obligatory by these meanings by way of substitution; and the objection would be valid only if these meanings necessitated the existence of ghusl, not its obligation. And it was also refuted that they nullify what has been [previous purity] and obligate what will be [future purity], so there is no contradiction. And in al-Mustasfa he also answered that these meanings are shurut (conditions) for obligation, not asbab (causes); so obligation is metaphorically attributed to the condition, as in the saying 'zakat al-fitr' because the cause is connected to existence and obligation, and the condition is connected to existence, so the condition shares with the cause in [attribution of] existence. And it was said in al-Kafi: He only said 'upon [occurrence of] mani' and not 'by mani' because the cause of obligation of ghusl is prayer or the intention of what is not permissible during janabah, and ejaculation and meeting [of circumcised parts are conditions]. And in Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam: The cause of obligation of ghusl is the intention to do what is not permissible according to the majority of mashayikh. And it was followed up in Ghayat al-Bayan that ghusl becomes obligatory when one of these meanings occurs, [then]...
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage clarifies the Hanafi definition of what triggers the obligation (wujub) of ghusl. The author begins by quoting the matn which states that ghusl becomes fard (obligatory) upon the occurrence of mani that is emitted with desire. However, scholars differed over the sabab (cause) of this obligation. The apparent view from al-Hidayah treats ejaculation itself as the cause. But al-Nihayah objects: ejaculation causes janabah (ritual impurity), not ghusl; ghusl is the removal of impurity, so how can impurity cause its own removal? The author then presents several responses: (1) Ghusl is obligatory by way of substitution (badal) when impurity occurs; (2) Impurity nullifies previous purity and necessitates future purity, so no contradiction; (3) Ejaculation is actually a shart (condition) for the obligation, not a sabab. The true sabab, according to al-Kafi and Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam, is the intention to perform an act that is prohibited during janabah (such as prayer or entering a mosque). The physical events (mani, meeting of circumcised parts) are shurut that make the intention effective. This careful distinction between sabab and shart is a hallmark of Hanafi usul, ensuring that the ruling is anchored in intention (niyyah) rather than mere physical occurrence.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The effective cause that directly triggers the obligation; here, the intention to do an act requiring purity.
شرط (shart): A condition that must be present for the sabab to be effective; ejaculation is a shart for ghusl obligation.
مني (mani): Semen emitted with desire; one of the events that render a person in need of ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view in this passage, what is the true sabab (cause) for the obligation of ghusl?
A) The ejaculation of mani.
B) The meeting of circumcised parts.
C) The intention to perform an act that is prohibited during janabah.
D) The passing of time after janabah.

Key Takeaway
The sabab for ghusl is the intention to perform an act prohibited during janabah; emission of mani is only a shart.

Washing Hair in Ghusl and the Cost of Water
Commentary on three opinions and water cost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions regarding the extent of washing hair in ghusl, explain the obligation of removing hair impediments, and determine the husband's responsibility for the cost of water for ghusl and wudu.

Core Idea
Water must reach the roots of hair in ghusl; the obligation to wet the tresses is disputed, and the cost of water is the husband's duty.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq explores three Hanafi opinions on washing hair during ghusl, a common point of confusion. It also addresses practical matters: removing perfume that blocks water, and the financial responsibility of the husband for the water used in ghusl and wudu. You will learn the relied-upon view and when exceptions apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three opinions on hair washing
Read the first part of the passage and list each opinion: 1) sufficing with roots (apparent madhhab), 2) sufficing with roots only if braided, else wetting interstices, 3) wetting entire tresses with squeezing (commentator's correction).
The first opinion is supported by hadiths; the third is presented as mufta bihi.
2
Determine the mufta bihi view
The commentator states 'we have corrected and presented [the third opinion]', indicating it is the relied-upon view for fatwa.
Ibn Nujaym makes this tarjih in al-Bahr al-Ra’iq.
3
Understand the obstruction of water by perfume
If a woman applies perfume that prevents water from reaching the hair roots, she must remove it; otherwise ghusl is invalid.
This is a condition (shart) for the validity of ghusl.
4
Analyze the husband's responsibility for water cost
The cost of water for a woman's ghusl and wudu is the husband's responsibility, even if she is wealthy, because it is indispensable like drinking water.
Fath al-Qadir equates it to providing food.
5
Evaluate the more appropriate view on hayd
Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj distinguishes: if hayd stops before ten days, husband pays (he needs intercourse); if at ten days, woman pays (she needs prayer). The commentator prefers the absolute rule: husband pays for all indispensable water.
This is a marginal detail; the general rule stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما الأول الإكتفاء بالوصول إلى الأصول منقوضاً كان أو معقوصاً وهو ظاهر المذهب كما هو ظاهر الذخيرة ويدل عليه الأحاديث الواردة في هذا الباب الثاني الإكتفاء بالوصول إلى الأصول إذا كان مضفوراً ووجوب الإيصال إلى أثنائه إذا كان منقوضاً ومشى عليه جماعة منهم صاحب المحيط والبدائع والكافي. الثالث وجوب بل الذوائب مع العصر وصحح قدمناه. ولو ألزقت المرأة رأسها بالطيب بحيث لا يصل الماء إلى أصول الشعر وجب عليها إزالته . وثمن ماء غسل المرأة ووضوئها على الزوج وإن كانت غنية كذا في فتح القدير فصار كماء الشرب لأن هذا مما لا بد منه وظاهره أنه لا فرق بين غسل الجنابة وغيره من هي الواجب. وذكر في السراج الوهاج تفصيلاً في غسل الحيض فقال : إذا انقطع لأقل من عشرة فعلى الزوج لاحتياجه إلى وطئها بعد الغسل، وإن انقطع لعشرة فعليها لأنها المحتاجة إليه للصلاة. وقد يقال : إن ما تحتاج إليه المرأة مما لا بد لها منه واجب عليه، سواء كان هو محتاجاً إليه أو لا، فالأوجه إطلاق ما قدمناه . قوله (منقوضاً كان أو معقوصاً) أي مضفوراً. قال في القاموس : عقص شعره يعقصه ضفره وقتله والعقصة بالكسر العقيصة والضفيرة قوله : (وهو ظاهر المذهب كما هو ظاهر الذخيرة) أي أن ظاهر كلام الذخيرة أن هذا هو المذهب. قال شارح المنية العلامة ابن أمير حاج الحلبي : وهذا فيما يظهر من الذخيرة أنه ظاهر المذهب اهـ. فما في بعض النسخ من قوله وهو ظاهر المتن غير صحيح بل ظاهر المتن هو القول الثاني اهـ .
As the first: sufficing with reaching the roots, whether [hair is] undone or braided, and that is the apparent madhhab as is apparent from al-Dhakhira, and it is supported by the hadiths related in this chapter. The second: sufficing with reaching the roots if it is braided, and the obligation of making [water] reach the interstices if it is undone; and a group followed this, among them the author of al-Muhit, al-Bada'i', and al-Kafi. The third: the obligation of wetting the tresses including squeezing, and we have corrected and presented [this view]. If a woman sticks her head with perfume such that water does not reach the roots of the hair, she is obliged to remove it. The price of water for a woman's ghusl and wudu is upon the husband even if she is wealthy; thus in Fath al-Qadir, so it becomes like drinking water because it is indispensable. And its apparent meaning is that there is no difference between the ghusl of janabah and other obligatory [washes]. And it is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj a detail concerning the ghusl of hayd: he said: if [the bleeding] stops before ten days, it is upon the husband due to his need for intercourse after the ghusl; and if it stops exactly at ten, it is upon her because she needs it for prayer. And it may be said: whatever a woman needs that is indispensable is obligatory upon him, whether he needs it or not, so the most appropriate is the absolute [application] of what we have presented. His saying: 'whether undone or braided' means plaited. He said in al-Qamus: 'aqasa sha'rahu ya'qisuhu: he plaited it and curled it; al-‘uqsa (with kasr) is the braid and the plait. His saying: 'and it is the apparent madhhab as it is apparent in al-Dhakhira' means that the apparent statement of al-Dhakhira is that this is the madhhab. The commentator of al-Munyah, 'Allamah Ibn Amir Haj al-Halabi, said: 'And this, as appears from al-Dhakhira, is the apparent madhhab.' What is in some copies of his statement 'and it is apparent in the matn' is incorrect; rather the apparent of the matn is the second opinion.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq discusses the ruling on washing hair during ghusl. The author presents three opinions among Hanafi scholars. The first opinion, considered the apparent madhhab, holds that it is sufficient for water to reach the roots of the hair, regardless of whether the hair is loose or braided. The commentator supports this with hadiths. The second opinion distinguishes between braided and undone hair: if braided, it suffices to wet the roots; if undone, one must also wet the interstices. The third opinion, which the commentator has corrected and presented, requires wetting the entire length of the tresses, including squeezing them. The passage then addresses a practical case: if a woman applies perfume that prevents water from reaching the roots, she must remove it. The cost of water for a woman's ghusl and wudu is the husband's responsibility, even if she is wealthy, because it is indispensable like drinking water. The author also mentions a distinction in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj regarding the ghusl of hayd: if bleeding stops before ten days, the husband must bear the cost because he needs intercourse; if it stops at ten days, the woman must pay because she needs it for prayer. However, the commentator points out that the more appropriate view is the absolute rule that whatever the woman indispensably needs is obligatory on the husband.

Key Terms
منقوض (manquḍ): Hair that is undone, not braided or plaited.
معقوص (ma‘qūṣ): Hair that is braided or plaited.
ذوائب (dhawā'ib): The pendants or tresses of hair, especially the braided ends.
مضفور (muḍaffar): Braided or plaited (synonym of معقوص).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator of al-Bahr al-Ra’iq, which of the following is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) opinion regarding washing hair in ghusl?
A) It suffices to reach the roots, whether hair is undone or braided.
B) If hair is braided, sufficing with roots suffices; if undone, wetting interstices is required.
C) It is obligatory to wet the entire tresses (dhawā’ib) along with squeezing them.
D) It is obligatory to unbraid the hair completely and wash every strand.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position requires wetting the hair tresses with squeezing in ghusl, and the cost of water is the husband's duty even if the wife is wealthy.

Obligation of Ghusl Upon Emission of Semen with Force and Desire
Commentary on the obligation of ghusl upon forceful and desired semen emission, with intra-Hanafi debate on the sabab and hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl due to semen emission, explain the condition of dafaq and shahwah, and apply the ruling to both intentional and involuntary emissions.

Core Idea
Ghusl is obligatory when semen exits with force and desire—whether intentionally or involuntarily.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq by Ibn Nujaym unpacks a key ruling in taharah: the obligation of ghusl upon the emission of semen. It not only states the ruling but also dives into the underlying cause (sabab) of the obligation and the evidence from hadith. You will see how the Hanafi school navigates early differences to arrive at a clear, consensus-based position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? The passage states that ghusl is obligatory (fard) at the time of semen with force and desire. Note that the ruling is for the obligation of ghusl itself, not for something else like wudu.
The matn says 'wa fardun' meaning it is fard.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator presents two hadiths: 1) 'When he sits between her four limbs and exerts himself, then ghusl becomes obligatory even if he does not ejaculate.' 2) The hadith 'Innamā al-mā' min al-mā'' which is said to be abrogated.
The first hadith is the primary evidence for the Hanafi position on intercourse without ejaculation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove obligation? The explicit statement 'ghusl becomes obligatory' (wajaba al-ghusl) uses a command form indicating wujub. In Hanafi usul, such explicit language is decisive.
The hadith is ahad, but its meaning is clear and supported by consensus.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Early companions (e.g., Ubayy ibn Ka'b) held that ghusl is only required upon ejaculation. Ibn Abbas interpreted 'Innamā al-mā' min al-mā'' as referring to wet dreams. However, later scholars achieved consensus on the Hanafi position.
This ikhtilaf is now resolved; the later consensus is decisive.
5
Understand the condition of dafaq and shahwah
The passage explains that dafaq means a forceful flow from the head of the penis, and shahwah means desire at the time of emission. This condition ensures that only normal ejaculation triggers ghusl, not involuntary leakage due to illness.
The word dafaq implies force; shahwah implies desire. Both must be present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وفرض عند مني ذي دفق وشهوة أي وفرض الغسل. واختلف المشايخ في سبب وجوبه فظاهر ما في الهداية أن إنزال المني ونحوه سبب له فإنه قال : المعاني الموجبة للغسل إنزال المني إلى آخره. وتعقبه في النهاية بأن هذه معان موجبة للجنابة لا للغسل على المذهب الصحيح من علمائنا فإنها تنقضه فكيف توجبه؟ ورده في غاية البيان بأن المراد أن الغسل يجب بهذه المعاني على طريق البدل وإنما يتوجه ما اعترض به إذا كانت هذه المعاني موجبة لوجود الغسل لا لوجوبه ورد أيضاً بأنها تنقض ما كان وتوجب ما سيكون فلا منافاة. وأجاب في المستصفى أيضاً بأن هذه المعاني شروط في الوجوب لا أسباب فأضيف الوجوب إلى الشرط مجازاً كقولهم صدقة الفطر لأن السبب يتعلق به الوجود والوجوب والشرط يضاف إليه الوجود فشارك الشرط السبب في الوجود وقال في الكافي : وإنما قال «عند مني» ولم يقل بمني لأن سبب وجوب الغسل الصلاة أو إرادة ما لا يحل مع الجنابة والإنزال والالتقاء. وفي مبسوط شيخ الإسلام : سبب وجوب الغسل إرادة ما لا يحل فعله عند عامة المشايخ وتعقبه في غاية البيان بأن الغسل يجب إذا وجد أحد هذه المعاني وجدت الإرادة أو لا، فكيف يكون سبباً؟ وقيل السبب الجنابة ورد أيضاً لوجوده في الحيض والنفاس، واختار في غاية البيان أن السبب الجنابة أو ما في معناه ليدخل الحيض والنفاس ويرد بما قدمناه في الحدث والجنابة ولا يجب الوضوء والغسل كما إذا كان قبل الوقت فالأولى أن يقال: سببه وجوب ما لا يحل مع الجنابة وهذا هو الذي اختاره في فتح القدير أعلم أن الأمة مجمعة الآن على وجوب الغسل بالجماع وإن لم يكن إنزال وعلى وجوبه بالإنزال، وكانت جماعة من الصحابة على أنه لا يجب إلا بالإنزال ثم رجع بعضهم وانعقد الإجماع بعد الآخرين وفي الباب حديث «إنما الماء الماء (1) من حديث أبي بن كعب عن رسول الله له في الرجل يأتي أهله ثم لا ينزل قال : يغسل ذكره ويتوضأ. وفيه الحديث الآخر إذا جلس بين شعبها الأربع ثم جهدها فقد وجب الغسل وإن لم ينزل (۲) قال العلماء: العمل على هذا الحديث، وإما حديث «الماء من الماء» فالجمهور من الصحابة ومن بعدهم قالوا إنه منسوخ ويعنون بالنسخ أن الغسل من الجماع بغير إنزال كان ثم صار واجباً. وذهب ابن عباس وغيره إلى أنه ليس منسوخاً بل المراد به نفي وجوب الغسل بالرؤية في النوم إذا لم ينزل وهذا الحكم باقي بلا شك، وأما حديث أبي بن كعب ففيه جوابان: أحدهما أنه منسوخ، والثاني أنه محمول على ما إذا باشرها فيما سوى الفرج كذا ذكر النووي في شرح مسلم لكن عندنا يشترط في وجوب الغسل بالإنزال أن يكون انفصال المني عن شهوة وهو ما ذكره بقوله عند مني ذي دفق وشهوة». يقال دفق الماء دفقاً فقاصبه صباً فيه دفع وشدة كذا في المغرب. وفي ضياء الحلوم دفق الماء دفقاً صبه ودفق الماء دفوقاً يتعدى ولا يتعدى. وعبر عنه في الهداية بقوله : أنزال المني على وجه الدفق والشهوة والأولى أن يقال : نزول المني دون الإنزال لأنه يلزم من النزول الإنزال دون العكس، فإن من احتلم أو وجد على فخذه يجب عليه الغسل بلا قصد الإنزال ذكره الهندي فعلى هذا التقدير يكون ذكر الدفق اشتراطاً للخروج من رأس الذكر فإنه يقال دفق الماء دفوقاً بمعنى خرج من محله وإنما يتوجه الخ». قوله : (رد (أيضاً أي رد ما تعقب به في النهاية وهذا الرد يؤول في المعنى إلى ما في غاية البيان قوله لكن هذا إنما يستقيم الخ هذه الجملة من هنا إلى قوله «لما في ضياء الحلوم موجودة في بعض النسخ بين قوله الآتي فإنه بمعنى صبه صباً، وقوله «وقال الشافعي والموجود فيها بعد قوله هنا كذا في المغرب وفي ضياء الحلوم إلى قوله وقال الشافعي». ولا يخفى
His saying: (And it is obligatory at the time of semen having force and desire) i.e., ghusl is obligatory. The mashāyikh differed concerning the cause of its obligation. What is apparent from al-Hidāyah is that the emission of semen and the like is the cause, for he said: 'The meanings that necessitate ghusl are the emission of semen' etc. It was objected to in al-Nihāyah by saying that these meanings necessitate janābah, not ghusl, according to the correct madhhab of our scholars, for they invalidate it (wudū'), so how can they necessitate it? He refuted it in Ghāyat al-Bayān by saying that what is meant is that ghusl becomes obligatory by these meanings by way of substitution (badal). The objection would only apply if these meanings necessitated the existence of ghusl, not its obligation. It was also refuted by saying that they invalidate what was and necessitate what will be, so there is no contradiction. And he answered in al-Mustasfā also that these meanings are conditions for obligation, not causes; thus obligation is attributed to the condition metaphorically, as in the saying 'sadaqat al-fiṭr' (the alms of fiṭr), because the cause relates to existence and obligation, while the condition is added to existence, so the condition shares with the cause in existence. And he said in al-Kāfī: He only said 'at the time of semen' and did not say 'by semen' because the cause of the obligation of ghusl is prayer or intending what is not permissible with janābah, or emission and meeting. In the Mabṣūṭ of Shaykh al-Islām: the cause of obligation of ghusl is intending what is not permissible to do according to the generality of the mashāyikh. And it was objected in Ghāyat al-Bayān: ghusl becomes obligatory when any of these meanings occur, whether the intention exists or not, so how can it be a cause? And it was said the cause is janābah, and it was also objected to because it exists in ḥayḍ and nifās. He chose in Ghāyat al-Bayān that the cause is janābah or what is in its meaning to include ḥayḍ and nifās, and it is rebutted by what we stated about ḥadath and janābah, and that wudū' and ghusl are not obligatory as if before the time. So it is better to say: its cause is the obligation of what is not permissible with janābah, and this is what he chose in Fatḥ al-Qadīr. Know that the Ummah is now unanimously agreed upon the obligation of ghusl by intercourse even without emission, and upon its obligation by emission. There was a group of companions who held that it is obligatory only by emission, then some of them retracted, and consensus was established after the later ones. In this chapter is the hadith 'Innamā al-mā' min al-mā'' from Ubayy ibn Ka'b from the Messenger of Allah concerning a man who has intercourse with his wife and then does not ejaculate: he said: 'He washes his private part and performs wudū'.' And there is the other hadith: 'When he sits between her four limbs and then exerts himself, then ghusl becomes obligatory even if he does not ejaculate.' The scholars said: the practice is upon this hadith. As for the hadith 'al-mā' min al-mā'', the majority of companions and those after them said it is abrogated, meaning by abrogation that ghusl from intercourse without ejaculation was [not obligatory] then became obligatory. Ibn 'Abbās and others held that it is not abrogated; rather what is meant by it is the negation of obligation of ghusl by seeing [semen] in a dream if one does not ejaculate, and this ruling remains without doubt. As for the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b, there are two answers: one is that it is abrogated; the second is that it is applied to the case where he has intercourse with her in other than the genitals. Thus al-Nawawī mentioned in his commentary on Muslim. But according to us, it is a condition for the obligation of ghusl by ejaculation that the separation of semen be with desire, which he mentioned by his saying: 'at the time of semen having force and desire.' It is said: dafaqa al-mā'a dafqan: he poured it out, pouring with force and severity; thus in al-Mughrib. And in Ḍiyā' al-Ḥulūm: dafaqa al-mā'a dafqan: he poured it, and dafaqa al-mā'a dafūqan is transitive and intransitive. He expressed it in al-Hidāyah as: 'the emission of semen in the mode of force and desire.' It is better to say: the descent of semen without emission, because emission implies descent but not vice versa. Indeed, one who has a wet dream or finds [semen] on his thigh must perform ghusl without intending emission, as mentioned by al-Hindī. So on this estimation, the mention of dafq is a condition for the exit from the head of the penis, for it is said dafaqa al-mā'a dafūqan meaning it came out from its place. And it is directed... His saying: (it was also refuted) meaning the objection to what was objected in al-Nihāyah, and this refutation is essentially the same as in Ghāyat al-Bayān. His saying: (but this is only sound...) This sentence from here to his saying 'because in Ḍiyā' al-Ḥulūm' is present in some copies between his following saying 'for it means pouring it out', and his saying 'and al-Shāfi'ī said' and what is found therein after his saying 'here it is in al-Mughrib and in Ḍiyā' al-Ḥulūm up to his saying 'and al-Shāfi'ī said.' And it is not hidden...
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq is a detailed commentary on the matn statement 'Wa fardun ‘inda maniyyin dhī dafaqin wa shahwah' (Ghusl is obligatory upon emission of semen with force and desire). The commentator begins by clarifying that this refers to the obligation of ghusl. He then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about the cause (sabab) of the obligation. According to al-Hidāyah, the emission of semen is the cause. However, al-Nihāyah objects that these causes (like emission) only necessitate janābah, not ghusl itself, because janābah invalidates wudū’, so how can it necessitate ghusl? Several responses follow: from Ghāyat al-Bayān that the obligation is by way of substitution (badal); from al-Mustasfā that these are conditions, not causes, and the attribution is metaphorical, like sadaqat al-fiṭr attributed to fiṭr though the real cause is something else. The commentator then discusses other views: some say the cause is prayer or intending lawful actions, others say it is janābah itself. He decides the best view is that the cause is the obligation to do what is not permissible while in janābah. He then affirms that the Ummah has consensus after the earlier dispute. The hadiths are presented: the hadith 'Innamā al-mā' min al-mā'' is abrogated according to the majority, upheld by Ibn ‘Abbās for wet dreams. The hadith about sitting between the four limbs is acted upon. Finally, the condition of dafaq (forceful flow) and shahwah (desire) is explained: dafaq means pouring out with force, and it is a condition for the exit from the head of the penis. The commentator quotes lexicons and notes that it is better to say 'nuzūl' (descent) rather than 'inzāl' (emission) to cover involuntary cases like wet dreams.

Key Terms
دفق (dafaq): Forceful flow or pouring out with force and severity, specifically of semen.
شهوة (shahwah): Desire or sexual arousal at the time of emission.
جنابة (janābah): State of ritual impurity requiring ghusl, caused by semen or intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, which of the following conditions is required for ghusl to be obligatory due to emission of semen?
A) The emission must be intentional
B) The emission must occur with force and desire
C) The emission must occur during sexual intercourse
D) The emission must be accompanied by a dream

Key Takeaway
Ghusl is obligatory upon the descent of semen with force (dafaq) and desire (shahwah), whether during wakefulness or sleep, by consensus of the later scholars.

Conditions for Ghusl: Gushing and Desire (Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Explaining the Hanafi conditions for obligatory ghusl due to janabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi conditions for obligatory ghusl from ejaculation and compare the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the requirement of gushing (dafaq).

Core Idea
Ghusl from ejaculation requires desire; but does it also require gushing? Abu Hanifa says yes, the Sahibayn say no – the commentator struggles to reconcile.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines the precise wording of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the conditions for ghusl. The author of Kanz includes both 'gushing' (dafaq) and 'desire' (shahwah) as conditions, but the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that desire alone suffices. The commentator delves into the linguistic and legal arguments, attempting to reconcile the text with the preferred position. This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute and its implications for the obligation of ghusl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
Find the explicit statement in the passage: ghusl is wajib from ejaculation only if the semen separates with desire (shahwah) and gushing (dafaq). Note that this is the author's formulation.
The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq uses the phrase 'عند مني ذي دفق وشهوة'.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
The commentator reveals that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) do not require dafaq; for them, desire alone is sufficient. Abu Hanifa's position is presented as requiring both. Determine who exactly requires dafaq.
The text says: 'إنما يستقيم على قول أبي يوسف، أما عندهما لا يستقيم' – requiring dafaq works only according to Abu Yusuf, not the Sahibayn. This suggests Abu Yusuf also requires dafaq, but the Sahibayn do not.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
Examine the two main hadith: (1) 'When he sits between her four limbs…' which obligates ghusl even without ejaculation, and (2) 'Water is from water' which the majority consider abrogated. Understand how these support the Hanafi position.
The Hanafi school relies on the first hadith for intercourse, and interprets the second as referring to ejaculation with desire.
4
Examine the problem of women
The condition of dafaq seems to exclude women because their semen is not gushing like men's. The commentator tries to reinterpret dafaq to include women.
The commentator suggests dafaq could mean 'force' or that some part pushes another, thus covering women's discharge.
5
Evaluate the commentator's resolution
The commentator offers multiple linguistic interpretations to reconcile the author's wording with the Sahibayn's position, such as taking dafaq as a necessary source (لازم) or making the adverb attach differently. Assess whether these resolutions are convincing.
The commentator acknowledges a degree of difficulty (تكلف) but prefers this over discarding the author's words.

And it was said the cause is janabah, and it was also rejected because it exists in menstruation and postpartum bleeding. The scholars said: the practice is based on this hadith. As for the hadith 'Water is from water', the majority of the Companions and those after them said it is abrogated, meaning by abrogation that ghusl from intercourse without ejaculation was then made obligatory. Ibn Abbas and others held that it is not abrogated but rather it means negation of the obligation of ghusl due to seeing in a dream when one does not ejaculate. This ruling remains without doubt. As for the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b, there are two answers: one is that it is abrogated, and the second is that it is interpreted as when he engages her in other than the private part. This is mentioned by al-Nawawi in Sharh Muslim. But according to us, it is a condition for the obligation of ghusl due to ejaculation that the semen separates with desire. And it is better to say: descent of semen rather than ejaculation, because descent necessitates ejaculation but not vice versa. For one who has a wet dream or finds it on his thigh must perform ghusl without intending ejaculation. Mentioned by al-Hindi. As for according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is not sound because they did not make dafaq a condition; rather desire suffices. I say, with Allah's success, it is possible to direct the author's words in a way that nothing mentioned is objected to it, but with a type of difficulty. That is by taking dafaq as the necessary source as the commentator mentions, i.e., having force, or as what Ibn Atiyyah said as transmitted in al-Nahr: that it is that the water be dafiq (gushing) such that some of it pushes some, i.e., it pushes it, so there is a gusher and a gushed. And the adverb in his saying 'at its separation' is attached to 'assumed' like the adverb in his saying 'with semen', and the meaning of separation is exit. And then it would be true according to both sayings because desire is not restricted to being at separation or at exit. Or the first adverb is attached to 'assumed' with an implied genitive, i.e., at the exit of semen, and the second is attached to dafaq; this is closer than the first. And on both, mentioning desire is a clarification of what is known necessarily, so it is not redundant as was said because their concepts are different even if one implies the other. And later in the commentator's words there is what indicates this second direction. And dafaq, on its two interpretations mentioned, can be before exit. And his words include the woman's semen because it gushes out at exit or some of it pushes some. And the contradiction in his words is also removed. And this explanation, while not very far, especially the second, is better than completely disregarding the author's words and removing them from coherence, especially since they may make efforts in the words of eloquent speakers with even more than this, as is not hidden from one who has familiarity with that. And Allah is the giver of inspiration. His saying: 'i.e., ghusl from ejaculation' - it is better that one of them...
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It deals with the causes of obligatory ghusl (ritual bath). The author first discusses the correct cause of ghusl, rejecting earlier formulations and settling on 'the obligation of what is not permissible with janabah' as chosen in Fath al-Qadir. Then he addresses the historical development of the ruling: the ummah is unanimous that both intercourse and ejaculation obligate ghusl, though some early Companions held that only ejaculation obligates it, and later consensus formed. The key hadith evidence is presented: the hadith 'When he sits between her four limbs...' establishes ghusl even without ejaculation, while the hadith 'Water is from water' (meaning ghusl is from ejaculation) is interpreted by the majority as abrogated, or by others as referring to wet dreams. The author then lays out the Hanafi position that for ghusl to be obligatory from ejaculation, the semen must separate with desire (shahwah) and be gushing (dafaq). He analyzes the phrase 'semen with gushing and desire' from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) do not require dafaq; they consider desire sufficient. Abu Yusuf specifically requires dafaq? Actually the text says Abu Yusuf holds dafaq as condition? Wait: 'bikhilaf dafaq dafqan... hadha innama yastaqimu 'ala qawl Abi Yusuf, amma 'indahuma la yastaqimu' - meaning requiring dafaq (as a condition from Kanz) only works according to Abu Yusuf, not according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). But earlier it said 'amma 'indahuma' meaning according to both of them, but Abu Yusuf is included? The text says 'inda Abi Yusuf' and then 'amma 'indahuma'. So the Sahibayn (both) do not require dafaq, but Abu Yusuf alone does? There is confusion. The commentator tries to reconcile by interpreting the author's wording in various ways. The passage also includes a discussion of whether the woman's semen is covered: it is not gushing like man's, so the condition would exclude women, which is problematic. The commentator suggests alternative interpretations of dafaq to include women. There is also an inter-madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i, who holds that ejaculation obligates ghusl regardless of desire, citing the hadith 'Water is from water'. The Hanafi response is that this hadith is abrogated or interpreted differently. The passage ends with a proposed resolution to the contradictions in the author's wording. Overall, this is a dense legal textual analysis typical of a sharh, intended for advanced students.

Key Terms
دفق (dafaq): Gushing: the forceful exit of semen from the head of the penis. It is a condition for ghusl according to Abu Hanifa (and Abu Yusuf in one interpretation).
شهوة (shahwah): Desire: the sexual pleasure accompanying the ejaculation. It is a condition for ghusl according to all Hanafi imams.
جنابة (janabah): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl, caused by intercourse or ejaculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, what is the condition for ghusl to be obligatory due to ejaculation?
A) Ejaculation with any amount of semen
B) Ejaculation with desire, regardless of gushing
C) Ejaculation with gushing, regardless of desire
D) Ejaculation with gushing and desire

Key Takeaway
Ghusl from ejaculation is wajib only when accompanied by desire (shahwah) and, according to the dominant Hanafi position, gushing (dafaq); the Sahibayn hold that desire alone suffices.

Taharah — Purification

Conditions for Ghusl: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute over Dafq and Shahwah
Expansion of ghusl conditions with intra- and inter-madhhab disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for ghusl obligation according to the Hanafi school and distinguish between the positions of Abu Yusuf and the Sahibayn regarding dafq and shahwah.

Core Idea
Ghusl is wajib only when semen exits with desire; the Sahibayn do not require forceful ejaculation, but Abu Yusuf does.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq by Ibn Nujaym expands on the ruling of ghusl obligation, focusing on an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author reconciles the wording of the base text (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) with the views of Abu Yusuf and the Sahibayn, and also addresses the Shafi'i position. Understanding this dispute clarifies the precise conditions that trigger the obligation of ghusl in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is ghusl (ritual bath) for janabah. The ruling is wajib (obligatory) under specific conditions.
The baseline obligation is from Quran 5:6.
2
State the Hanafi position and its conditions
The Hanafi school holds that ghusl is wajib only when semen (maniy) is emitted with sexual desire (shahwah). The debate is whether forceful ejaculation (dafq) is also required.
Semen without desire (e.g., from illness) does not obligate ghusl.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf requires both dafq and shahwah at the moment of exit from the glans. The Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) require only shahwah at the moment of separation from the spine; dafq is not necessary.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn.
4
Examine the evidence (dalil) for the Hanafi position
The Quranic verse (5:6) defines janabah as one who has fulfilled his desire, linking ghusl to desire. The hadith 'إنما الماء من الماء' is interpreted as referring to emission with desire, not any emission.
The Hanafi response to the Shafi'i literal reading is that the hadith either is abrogated, applies only to wet dreams, or its 'al' denotes a specific water (the one with desire).
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
If semen is emitted without desire (e.g., due to cold), Hanafis do not require ghusl, while Shafi'is do. Within Hanafism, if emission occurs without force, Abu Yusuf would not require ghusl, but the Sahibayn would.
The practical impact is on the validity of prayer without ghusl.

According to the two (Sahibayn) it is not consistent because they did not make dafq a condition; rather, desire (shahwah) suffices, so they said it is obligatory when semen separates from its place with desire even if it exits without dafq. Thus in al-Nihaya, Miraj al-Diraya, etc. He answered in al-Inaya and Ghayat al-Bayan that there is no restriction in his speech, so it is consistent; at most it necessitates omitting some of his requirements according to them in the place of their explanation. It is not hidden what is in it. It can be said: The meaning of 'ejaculation with desire' is that desire has a role in the ejaculation, whether it is concomitant or prior and concomitant with separation. The author's expression is more problematic because it is subject to the same objection as al-Quduri's expression that it does not include a woman's semen because her fluid is not gushing like a man's; rather it descends from her chest to her vulva as mentioned by al-Walwaliji in his Fatawa. Especially the objection of contradiction in structure because conditioning dafq implies conditioning the exit of semen with desire from the glans, and his saying 'at its separation' negates it, so deleting dafq would be better. It is said that dafq is the verbal noun (masdar) of the intransitive verb. Al-Shafi'i said: Its ejaculation necessitates ghusl whether with desire or not, and they argued with his statement (peace be upon him) 'Innama al-ma'u min al-ma'' meaning ghusl is from ejaculation, and this is the view of Muhammad... The careful examiner will see that this found in some copies as we said is better. His statement: 'It can be said that the meaning of ejaculation...' has no entry here, so reflect. His statement: 'His saying 'at its separation' negates it' — then it cannot be carried on Abu Yusuf's view either because he only conditions desire and dafq at exit from the glans, not at separation. I say, with Allah's success, the author's speech can be directed in a way that nothing mentioned refutes it, but with some effort, by interpreting dafq as an intransitive verbal noun as the commentator mentions, i.e., possessing force, or as Ibn Atiyya said as quoted in al-Nahr, that it means the water is gushing because some of it pushes some, i.e., forces it, so there is dafiq (forcer) and madfuq (forced). The adverb in 'at its separation' is attached to 'fard' like the adverb in 'at maniy', and 'separation' means exit; then it applies to both views because desire is not restricted to being at separation or exit, or the first adverb is attached to 'fard' with an implied addition, i.e., at the exit of semen, and the second is attached to dafq, and this is closer. Thus mentioning desire is explicit of what is known implicitly, so it is not redundant as said because their concepts differ even if one entails the other. Later the commentator's speech will indicate this second aspect. Dafq according to its two interpretations can be before exit. His speech includes a woman's semen because it pushes when exiting or some pushes some. Contradiction is also removed from his speech. This exposition, especially the second, is not far-fetched and is better than completely ignoring the author's speech and making it disordered, especially since they make efforts in the speech of eloquent people with more than this, as is clear to those familiar. Allah is the grantor of inspiration. His statement: (i.e., ghusl from ejaculation) the first... Book of Purification. Then, non-existence, non-existence, and Zufar as quoted in Miraj al-Diraya and al-Dhakhira, and it is the choice of some shaykhs. Al-Hidayah argued for us with His statement: 'And if you are in a state of janabah, purify yourselves' (5:6), and janabah in language is a name for one who has fulfilled his desire; obligation of ghusl is suspended on janabah, not on semen exit. It was objected that this appears to be arguing by the concept of the condition (mafhum al-shart) and he did not answer it. It may be said: This is not arguing by mafhum al-shart; rather, since the ruling is suspended on a condition and it does not exist, the ruling is non-existent by original non-existence, not that the condition necessitates the ruling. This is not hidden from those engaged in the usul of our scholars. He said in al-Tanqih: According to us, non-existence is not established by suspension; rather, the ruling remains on original non-existence. Al-Hidayah answered the hadith by interpreting it as referring to exit with desire. The commentators said: It is interpreted this way because the general (al-am) when it cannot be applied to the absolute (al-musammam) intends the most specific of the specific (akhas al-khusus) due to certainty. Here it cannot be applied to the general because ghusl is not obligatory for emission of pre-seminal fluid (madhi) and urine by consensus, and ejaculation with desire is intended by consensus, so nothing else is intended, i.e., ejaculation of semen without desire is not intended. It is not hidden that if this approach were valid, it would be more in line with Abu Yusuf's view because the most specific intended by consensus is that which is with desire at both exit and separation. So the better is what we previously mentioned: that it is abrogated or interpreted as the case of wet dream. Since what we mentioned was valid, he turned away from the method of the commentators in Fath al-Qadir and said: The hadith is interpreted as referring to exit with desire because the lam (in al-ma') denotes mental reference ('ahd dhihni), i.e., the specific water that is known to them is that which exits with desire. How often does it not occur to most people in their entire lives, and they do not see this water devoid of desire. Moreover, that semen can be without desire is denied, for Aisha took desire in her interpretation of it, as Ibn al-Mundhir reported that semen is the greatest water from which comes desire, and in it is ghusl. Similarly from Qatada and Ikrima. So its exit without desire is inconceivable, otherwise the rule (dabit) would be corrupted. Then the scholars of the madhhab agreed that ghusl is not obligatory if it separates from its place in the spine with desire unless it exits at the glans. The only difference is whether the conjunction of desire with exit is required? According to Abu Yusuf, yes, while according to the two (Sahibayn), no. He indicated his choice of their view by his saying 'at its separation', i.e., he made ghusl obligatory at the exit of semen described with dafq and desire at the separation from its place according to them. The basis of Abu Yusuf's view is that the obligation of ghusl is related to the separation and exit of semen, and desire was conditioned at its separation, so it is conditioned at its exit. Their (Sahibayn) view is that it can be said that 'obligation of water is from the descent of semen' to imply the addition of a genitive in both, and to agree with al-Shafi'i, Muhammad, and Zufar (may Allah have mercy on them) that it is obligatory by descent, not by ejaculation. His statement: 'It is not hidden that if this approach were valid' — he indicates that there is no need to interpret 'al' as generic, i.e., the genus of water descending from a human's outlet, but it is far-fetched because there is no possibility of intending that from the hadith; thus the lam is for mental reference as comes from al-Fath. Then the commentators' explanation of al-Hidayah's speech is not completed. His statement: 'Otherwise the rule would be corrupted' i.e., the rule described by Aisha.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion of the ruling on the obligation of ghusl (ritual bath) due to the emission of semen (maniy). The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the conditions of dafq (forceful ejaculation) and shahwah (sexual desire). The base text (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) conditions dafq, which is consistent only with Abu Yusuf's view. The Sahibayn hold that desire alone suffices for ghusl, even if the semen exits without force. The passage then addresses objections: that the condition of dafq excludes women's semen (since it does not gush forcefully), and that the phrasing 'at its separation' (عند انفصاله) contradicts the condition of dafq because it implies desire at separation, not at the moment of forceful exit. The author attempts to reconcile the text's wording with both views through linguistic analysis, interpreting dafq as an intransitive verbal noun or as meaning 'pushing' (one part pushes another). The second part of the passage deals with the Shafi'i position that ghusl is required for any emission of semen, even without desire, based on the hadith 'إنما الماء من الماء' (water is from water). Al-Hidayah argues using the Quranic verse (5:6) that janabah (major impurity) is defined by fulfilling desire, thus linking ghusl to desire, not mere emission. The hadith is interpreted as referring to emission with desire, either by being abrogated, applied to wet dreams, or by understanding 'al' as denoting a specific known water (the one exiting with desire). The passage concludes by noting the consensus among Hanafis that ghusl is obligatory only when semen exits with desire from its place (the spine) except if it reaches the glans. The dispute among Hanafis is whether desire must coincide with the exit (Abu Yusuf's view) or merely at the moment of separation from the spine (Sahibayn's view). The text indicates a preference for the Sahibayn's position.

Key Terms
دفق (dafq): Forceful ejaculation of semen; in this text, a condition for ghusl according to Abu Yusuf, but not according to the Sahibayn.
شهوة (shahwah): Sexual desire; a necessary condition for ghusl according to all Hanafis.
جنابة (janabah): State of major ritual impurity resulting from sexual intercourse or ejaculation with desire; the Quran grounds ghusl on this state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafis (Sahibayn), what is required for ghusl to be obligatory upon emission of semen?
A) Forceful ejaculation (dafq) only
B) Sexual desire (shahwah) only
C) Both desire and force
D) Emission regardless of desire or force

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the obligation of ghusl is tied to the presence of sexual desire (shahwah) at the time of semen emission; forceful ejaculation (dafq) is not required according to the relied-upon position.

The Requirement of Shahwa for Ghusl: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on shahwa condition for ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the requirement of shahwa for ghusl from maniy and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to three scenarios.

Core Idea
Ghusl is wajib when maniy exits after shahwa, but must shahwa be present at exit? Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say no; Abu Yusuf says yes.

This lesson explores a nuanced intra-madhhab dispute: whether sexual desire (shahwa) must be present at the very moment maniy exits for ghusl to be obligatory. The Imamayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that shahwa at separation suffices, while Abu Yusuf requires it at exit. We will analyse the proofs, the response, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed principle
All Hanafi scholars agree that ghusl is not obligatory when maniy separates from its place with shahwa unless it emerges at the tip of the penis. The dispute is only about the moment of shahwa.
The agreed condition is that maniy must exit; mere internal separation is insufficient.
2
State the dispute
Abu Yusuf holds that shahwa must accompany the exit (khuruj) of maniy. The Imamayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that shahwa at the time of separation (infisal) is sufficient.
The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq indicated preference for the Imamayn's view.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf argues that obligation is linked to both separation and exit; since shahwa was conditioned at separation, it must also be present at exit.
4
Analyze the Imamayn's response
The Imamayn respond that the obligation is tied to the descent (nuzul) of maniy, not its emission (inzal). They cite the hadith of 'A'ishah describing maniy as 'the great water' and argue that the existence of the water itself is stronger evidence than the description of gushing.
They also use istihsan and the principle of precaution (ihtiyat).
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference appears in three scenarios: (1) wet dream with holding until desire subsides, (2) looking with desire then holding, (3) residual maniy after ghusl without desire. In each, the Imamayn require ghusl; Abu Yusuf does not.
Consensus exists that after urination, sleep, or walking, residual fluid is not maniy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اتفق أصحاب المذهب أنه لا يجب الغسل إذا انفصل عن مقره من الصلب بشهوة إلا إذا خرج على رأس الذكر، وإنما الخلاف في أنه هل يشترط مقارنة الشهوة الخروج؟ فعند أبي يوسف نعم، وعندهما لا. وقد أشار إلى اختيار قولهما بقوله عند انفصاله أي فرض الغسل عند خروج مني موصوف بالدفق والشهوة عند الانفصال عن محله عندهما وجه قول أبي يوسف أن وجوب الغسل متعلق بانفصال المني وخروجه وقد شرطت الشهوة عند انفصاله فتشترط عند خروجه، ولهما أن يقال أي وجوب الماء من نزول المني ليكون فيه إشارة إلى تقدير المضاف فيهما، وليوافق قول الشافعي ومحمد وزفر رحمهم الله بوجوبه بالنزول لا بالإنزال. قوله: (ولا يخفى أن هذا المسلك لو صح) كأنه يشير إلى أنه لا داعي إلى حمل «أل» على الجنس أي جنس الماء النازل من مخرج الإنسان بل هو بعيد لعدم توهم إرادة ذلك من الحديث فاللام للعهد الذهني كما يأتي عن الفتح وحينئذ لا يتم ما قاله الشارحون في تقرير كلام الهداية. قوله: (وإلا يفسد الضابط) أي الضابط الذي وصفته عائشة. الجنابة قضاء الشهوة بالإنزال فإذا وجدت مع الإنفصال صدق اسمها وكان مقتضى هذا ثبوت حكمها وإن لم يخرج لكن لا خلاف في عدم ثبوت الحكم إلا بالخروج فيثبت بذلك الانفصال من الوجه وهو أقوى مما بقي والاحتياط واجب وهو العمل بالأقوى من الوجهين فوجب. وأورد في النهاية الريح الخارجة من المفضاة لأنها إن خرجت من القبل لا يجب الوضوء، وإن خرجت من الدبر وجب فينبغي ترجيح جانب الوجوب احتياطاً كما قالا هنا. وأجاب بأن الشك هناك جاء من الأصل فتعارض الدليل الموجب وغير الموجب لتساويهما في القوة فتساقطا فعملنا بالأصل الثابت بيقين وهو الطهارة، أما هنا جاء دليل عدم الوجوب من الوصف وهو الدفق ودليل الوجوب من الأصل وهو نفس وجود الماء فكان في إيجاب الاغتسال ترجيح لجانب الأصل على جانب الوصف وهو صحيح الوجوب قد سبق هنا وهو مزايلة المني عن مكانه على سبيل الشهوة وخروجه من العضو لا على سبيل الدفق بقاء ذلك والسبق من أسباب الترجيح فترجح جانب الوجوب لذلك، وأما هناك فاقترن الدليلان على سبيل المدافعة فلا يثبت الحكم الحادث لتدافعهما بل يبقى ما كان على ما كان. وفي المصفى وثمرة الاختلاف تظهر في ثلاث فصول: أحدها أن من احتلم فأمسك ذكره حتى سكنت شهوته ثم خرج المني يجب الغسل عندهما خلافاً له. والثاني إذا نظر إلى امرأة بشهوة فزال المني عن مكانه بشهوة فأمسك ذكره حتى انكسرت شهوته ثم سال بعد ذلك لا دفق فعلى هذا الخلاف والثالث أن المجامع إذا اغتسل قبل أن يبول أو ينام ثم سال منه بقية المني من غير شهوة يعيد الاغتسال عندهما خلافاً له، فلو خرج بقية المني بعد البول أو النوم أو المشي لا يجب الغسل إجماعاً لأن مذي وليس بمني لأن البول والنوم والمشي يقطع مادة الشهوة اهـ. وفي فتح القدير: وكذا لا يعيد الصلاة التي صلاها بعد الغسل الأول قبل خروج ما تأخر من المني اتفاقاً. وقيد المشي بالكثير في المجتبى وأطلقه كثير والتقييد أوجه لأن الخطوة والخطوتين لا يكون منهما ذلك كما لا يخفى. وفي المبتغى بخلاف المرأة يعني تعيد تلك الصلاة إذا كانت مكتوبة إذا اغتسلت ثانياً بخروج بقية منها وفيه نظر ظاهر، والذي رضي الله عنها لتمييز المياه لتعطي أحكامها وذلك حيث قالت كما في فتح القدير: فأما المذي فالرجل يلاعب امرأته فيظهر على ذكره الشيء فيغسل ذكره وأنثييه ويتوضأ ولا يغتسل، وأما الودي فإنه يكون بعد البول يغسل ذكره وأنثييه ويتوضأ ولا يغتسل وأما المني فإنه الماء الأعظم إلى آخر ما مر. قوله: (وهو أقوى مما بقي) وهو الشهوة حالة الخروج كما يظهر من غاية البيان ومن الجواب الآتي، ويكون حاصل ذلك أن الوجوب يتعلق بالانفصال والخروج جميعاً لأنه بمجرد الانفصال لا فبالنظر إلى وجود الشهوة حالة الانفصال يجب وبالنظر إلى عدمها حالة الخروج لا، فوجب من وجه دون وجه وثبوته بالأول أحوط لأنه أقوى. قوله: (من الوصف وهو الدفق) أي الذي هو لازم يجب اتفاقاً
Then the scholars of the madhhab agreed that ghusl is not obligatory when [semen] separates from its place in the spine with desire, except if it emerges at the tip of the penis. The dispute is only: is it required that desire accompany the exit? According to Abu Yusuf, yes; according to the two [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad], no. And he indicated his preference for their view by saying 'at its separation', i.e., he made ghusl obligatory upon the emergence of semen described with gushing and desire at separation from its place according to the two. The justification of Abu Yusuf's view is that the obligation of ghusl is connected to the separation and exit of semen, and desire was conditioned at its separation, so it is required at its exit. For the two, it is said that the obligation of water is from the descent of semen, indicating an implied addition in both, and to agree with the view of al-Shafi'i, Muhammad, and Zufar (may Allah have mercy on them) that it is obligatory by descent, not by emission. His statement: (And it is not hidden that this approach, if correct) he indicates that there is no need to take 'al' as denoting genus, i.e., the genus of water descending from the human orifice; rather it is far-fetched because there is no misconception that such is intended from the hadith; so the 'lam' is for mental reference as will come from al-Fath, and then what the commentators said in establishing the statement of al-Hidayah is not complete. His statement: (Otherwise the rule would be corrupted) i.e., the rule that 'A'ishah described. Janabah is the fulfillment of desire by emission; when it occurs with separation, its name applies, and accordingly its ruling is established even if it does not exit, but there is no dispute that the ruling is not established except by exit. So it is established by that separation in one aspect, and it is stronger than what remains, and caution is obligatory, and that is to act by the stronger of the two aspects, so it is obligatory. And an objection was raised in al-Nihayah regarding wind exiting from an evacuee: if it exits from the front, wudu' is not obligatory; if from the anus, it is obligatory, so the side of obligation should be preferred out of caution, as they said here. He answered that the doubt there came from the original, so the evidence requiring and not requiring conflicted equally, so they fell away, and we acted upon the original established with certainty, which is purity. Here, the evidence for non-obligation comes from a description, which is gushing, and the evidence for obligation comes from the original, which is the very existence of the water. So in making ghusl obligatory, the side of the original is given precedence over the side of the description, and that is correct. The obligation preceded here: it is the displacement of semen from its place in the way of desire and its exit from the organ, not in the way of gushing; the persistence of that and the precedence are causes of preponderance, so the side of obligation preponderated for that reason. There, the two evidences concurred in a conflicting manner, so the new ruling is not established due to their conflict; rather what was remains as it was. And in al-Mustafa: The fruit of the difference appears in three sections: First, one who had a wet dream and held his penis until his desire subsided, then semen emerged: ghusl is obligatory according to the two, contrary to him. Second, if he looked at a woman with desire and semen moved from its place with desire, then he held his penis until his desire broke, then it flowed without gushing: the same dispute. Third, if one who had intercourse performed ghusl before urinating or sleeping, then residual semen emerged without desire, he repeats ghusl according to the two, contrary to him. If residual semen emerged after urination, sleep, or walking, ghusl is not obligatory by consensus because it is madhy and not maniy, since urination, sleep, and walking cut off the substance of desire. In Fath al-Qadir: Likewise, he does not repeat the salah he performed after the first ghusl before the delayed semen emerged, by agreement. And walking was restricted to a lot in al-Mujtaba, and many left it unrestricted; the restriction is more appropriate because one or two steps do not achieve that, as is not hidden. And in al-Mibtagha: contrary to a woman, meaning she repeats that salah if it was an obligatory salah when she performs ghusl a second time due to residual emission, and there is an apparent objection. And the one with whom Allah is pleased said for distinguishing waters to give their rulings: 'As for madhy, it is when a man plays with his wife and a thing appears on his penis: he washes his penis and testicles and performs wudu' and does not perform ghusl. As for wady, it occurs after urination: he washes his penis and testicles and performs wudu' and does not perform ghusl. As for maniy, it is the great water...' to the end of what has passed. His statement: (And it is stronger than what remains) i.e., desire at the time of exit, as appears from Ghayat al-Bayan and from the response to come. The summary is that obligation attaches to both separation and exit together, because with mere separation it is not; so with regard to the presence of desire at separation, it is obligatory, and with regard to its absence at exit, it is not. So it is obligatory from one aspect and not from another, and its establishment by the first is more precautionary because it is stronger. His statement: (from the description, which is gushing) i.e., that which is necessarily agreed upon.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of ghusl (ritual bath) due to the emission of maniy (semen). The agreed principle is that if semen separates from its source (the spine) with shahwa (sexual desire), ghusl is obligatory only if it exits at the tip of the penis. The core dispute is whether shahwa must be present at the actual moment of exit (khuruj) or whether it is sufficient that it was present at the time of separation (infisal) from its place. Abu Yusuf holds that shahwa must accompany the exit, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Imamayn) hold that it is not required. The author indicates his preference for the Imamayn. The text provides proof: Abu Yusuf's view links obligation to both separation and exit, and since shahwa was conditioned at separation, it should also be required at exit. The Imamayn respond by noting that the obligation of ghusl is tied to the descent (nuzul) of maniy, not its emission (inzal), and they align with al-Shafi'i, Muhammad, and Zufar. The author then discusses the implications using the concept of 'al' (the definite article) in the hadith, arguing that it refers to a specific known water, not a generic one. The passage also addresses an objection about wind from an evacuee (mustafda), distinguishing that case because the evidence for obligation and non-obligation are equally strong, so the original state (purity) remains. In contrast, here the evidence for obligation (the existence of water itself) is stronger than the evidence for non-obligation (mere description of gushing). The fruit of the dispute (thamarah al-khilaf) is illustrated through three scenarios: (1) a wet dream where one holds the penis until desire subsides, (2) looking at a woman with desire causing semen to move but then held, and (3) residual semen after ghusl without desire. In each, the Imamayn require ghusl, while Abu Yusuf does not. The text also discusses the distinction between maniy, madhy (pre-ejaculatory fluid), and wady (prostatic fluid) based on the hadith of 'A'ishah. The ruling is that ghusl is obligatory only when the fluid is maniy, characterized by gushing and desire.

Key Terms
المني (al-maniy): Semen, the fluid whose emission from the body with sexual desire necessitates ghusl.
الشهوة (al-shahwa): Sexual desire; the condition that must accompany the separation or exit of maniy for ghusl to be obligatory.
الدفق (al-dafq): Gushing or spurting force with which maniy typically exits; it is a sign of maniy but not a condition for obligation according to the Imamayn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling regarding ghusl for a person who, after having a wet dream, holds his penis until his desire subsides, and then maniy exits without any remaining desire?
A) Ghusl is obligatory according to all Hanafi imams.
B) Ghusl is obligatory according to Abu Yusuf but not according to the Imamayn.
C) Ghusl is obligatory according to the Imamayn but not according to Abu Yusuf.
D) Ghusl is not obligatory by consensus.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi is that ghusl becomes wajib when maniy exits after having been separated with shahwa, even if desire is absent at the moment of exit.
