Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ghusl Obligation: Three Cases
Explaining the practical differences between Abu Hanifa and the two regarding ghusl obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three cases where the Sahibayn require ghusl but Abu Hanifa does not, and justify why the Sahibayn's view is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Ghusl is wajib when mani separates with shahwa, even if exit is without force; this is the relied-upon view.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), on the conditions that make ghusl obligatory. The dispute centers on whether the presence of shahwa at the time of separation of mani suffices, or whether shahwa must also be present at the moment of exit. The commentator explains the logical reasoning behind each view and then illustrates the practical difference through three concrete scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Understand that the disagreement is about the role of shahwa: Abu Hanifa requires shahwa at both separation and exit; the Sahibayn consider separation with shahwa sufficient.
2
Analyze the logical argument
The commentator compares the evidence: the existence of mani (original) vs. the attribute of dafaq (non-essential). Which should prevail?
This is a dalil aqli approach.
3
Examine the three scenarios
Walk through each scenario: wet dream, looking with desire, post-coital leftover. Note the conditions and the split rulings.
These illustrate the thamarah al-khilaf.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The commentator shows preference for the Sahibayn's view by arguing that the original (existence of mani) outweighs the attribute (dafaq). Thus, the mufta bihi position is that of the Sahibayn.
5
Apply the consensus exception
Note that if leftover mani exits after urination, sleep, or walking, it is considered madhi by consensus, and no ghusl is required.
This shows the boundary of the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أجاب بأن الشك هناك جاء من الأصل فتعارض الدليل الموجب وغير الموجب لتساويهما في القوة فتساقطا فعملنا بالأصل الثابت بيقين وهو الطهارة، أما هنا جاء دليل عدم الوجوب من الوصف وهو الدفق ودليل الوجوب من الأصل وهو نفس وجود الماء فكان في إيجاب الاغتسال ترجيح لجانب الأصل على جانب الوصف وهو صحيح الوجوب قد سبق هنا وهو مزايلة المني عن مكانه على سبيل الشهوة وخروجه من العضو لا على سبيل الدفق بقاء ذلك والسبق من أسباب الترجيح فترجح جانب الوجوب لذلك، وأما هناك فاقترن الدليلان على سبيل المدافعة فلا يثبت الحكم الحادث لتدافعهما بل يبقى ما كان على ما كان. وفي المصفى وثمرة الاختلاف تظهر في ثلاث فصول : أحدها أن من احتلم فأمسك ذكره حتى سكنت شهوته ثم خرج المني يجب الغسل عندهما خلافاً له. والثاني إذا نظر إلى امرأة بشهوة فزال المني عن مكانه بشهوة فأمسك ذكره حتى انكسرت شهوته ثم سال بعد ذلك لا دفق فعلى هذا الخلاف والثالث أن المجامع إذا اغتسل قبل أن يبول أو ينام ثم سال منه بقية المني من غير شهوة يعيد الاغتسال عندهما خلافاً له، فلو خرج بقية المني بعد البول أو النوم أو المشي لا يجب الغسل إجماعاً لأن مذي وليس بمني لأن البول والنوم والمشي يقطع مادة الشهوة اهـ.
He answered that doubt there came from the original [principle], so the evidence imposing obligation and the evidence not imposing it were contradictory, equal in strength, so they cancelled each other, and we acted upon the original established with certainty, which is taharah. But here, the evidence of non-obligation comes from the attribute, which is dafaq, and the evidence of obligation comes from the original, which is the very existence of water. So in making ghusl obligatory, there is a preference for the side of the original over the side of the attribute, and it is correct. Obligation has preceded here, and it is the movement of mani from its place by way of desire and its exit from the organ not by way of dafaq. The preservation of that and the precedence are among the causes of preference, so the side of obligation prevails for that reason. There, the two evidences combined in a contradictory manner, so the newly arisen ruling is not established because of their conflict; rather, what was remains as it was. In al-Mustafa: The fruit of disagreement appears in three chapters: First, that if someone has a wet dream and holds his penis until his desire calms, then mani comes out, ghusl is obligatory according to them (the two), contrary to him (Abu Hanifa). Second, if he looks at a woman with desire, and the mani moves from its place with desire, then he holds his penis until his desire breaks, then it flows afterwards without dafaq—on this is the same disagreement. Third, that if a person who has intercourse performs ghusl before urinating or sleeping, then some leftover mani flows from him without desire, he must repeat the ghusl according to them, contrary to him. If leftover mani comes out after urination, sleep, or walking, ghusl is not obligatory by consensus, because it is madhi, not mani, because urination, sleep, and walking cut off the substance of desire.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about when ghusl becomes obligatory upon emission of mani. The commentator first explains why the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differ from Abu Hanifa in certain cases. The core principle: obligation of ghusl requires both the separation of mani from its place (infisal) and its exit (khuruj) with desire (shahwa) and force (dafaq). Abu Hanifa holds that both the initial separation and subsequent exit must occur with desire for ghusl to be obligatory; if desire is present only at separation but not at exit, ghusl is not wajib. The Sahibayn argue that the separation with desire is the stronger indicator, so ghusl is wajib even if exit is without desire. They illustrate this in three scenarios: (1) A sleeping person has a wet dream, wakes, holds his penis until desire subsides, then mani comes out—Sahibayn say ghusl is wajib (because separation with desire occurred), Abu Hanifa says not. (2) Looking at a woman with desire causes mani to move from its place; then he holds his penis until desire breaks, then it flows without force—same dispute. (3) After intercourse, if one does ghusl before urinating or sleeping, then leftover mani comes out without desire—Sahibayn say ghusl must be repeated, Abu Hanifa says no. However, if leftover comes out after urination, sleep, or walking, all agree it is madhi, not mani, so no ghusl. The mufta bihi position is that of the Sahibayn, as the commentator notes 'the precaution is to act on the stronger side'.

Key Terms
المني (al-maniy): Semen; the fluid that necessitates ghusl when emitted with shahwa.
الشهوة (al-shahwa): Sexual desire; a condition for the emission to be considered mani requiring ghusl.
الدفق (al-dafaq): Forceful ejaculation; an attribute of mani, but not a condition for obligation according to Sahibayn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, in which of the following cases is ghusl obligatory?
A) A person has a wet dream, wakes up, holds his penis until desire subsides, then mani comes out.
B) A person looks at a woman without desire, and mani comes out forcefully.
C) A person urinates, then finds some fluid on his thigh and does not remember a wet dream.
D) A person performs ghusl after intercourse, then sleeps, and after waking finds some fluid.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position (Sahibayn) holds that ghusl becomes obligatory when mani separates from its place with sexual desire, regardless of whether the exit is forceful or not.

Ruling on Acting by Abu Yusuf's Opinion for a Guest Fearing Suspicion
Fatwa selection for a guest in case of fear of suspicion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the fatwa distinction between a guest and a non-guest when ruling on the case of finding wetness or fearing suspicion, citing the sources from al-Mustasfa and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.

Core Idea
For a guest, fatwa follows Abu Yusuf to avoid suspicion; for others, the Sahibayn's opinion is followed.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a nuanced ruling: when a person staying as a guest in someone's home finds wetness or fears being suspected of having a wet dream, which opinion should be acted upon? The fatwa selection varies based on social context. Understanding this distinction demonstrates how Hanafi fatwa considers social circumstances to protect individuals from embarrassment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three elements of the ruling
The ruling involves three elements: the person's status (guest vs. non-guest), the condition (fear of suspicion), and the operative opinion (Abu Yusuf vs. Sahibayn).
The condition 'fear of suspicion' is specific to the guest scenario.
2
Understand the source hierarchy
The passage cites two sources: al-Mustasfa (which mentions acting on Abu Yusuf's opinion) and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj (which provides the fatwa distinction). Recognize that al-Siraj al-Wahhaj is a later fatwa source that refines the earlier statement.
This shows the evolution of fatwa within the Hanafi school.
3
Apply the fatwa distinction
For a guest fearing suspicion, follow the opinion of Abu Yusuf. For a non-guest (e.g., at home), follow the opinion of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
The ruling does not specify what Abu Yusuf's actual opinion is; it only directs which authority to follow.
4
Explain the rationale
The distinction protects the guest from social embarrassment and suspicion. The household might misinterpret the need for ghusl, so the more accommodating opinion is adopted.
This reflects the Hanafi principle of considering 'mafsadah' (harm) in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يظهر أنها كالرجل وفي المستصفى : يعمل بقول أبي يوسف إذا كان في بيت إنسان واحتلم أهل البيت أو خاف أن يقع في قلبهم ريبة بأن طاف حول أهل بيتهم مثلاً أنه ويستحيي من ا هـ. وفي السراج الوهاج والفتوى على قول أبي يوسف في الضيف وعلى قولهما في غيره ا هـ.
It appears that she is like a man. And in al-Mustasfa: One acts on the opinion of Abu Yusuf when a person is in someone's house and the people of the house have a wet dream or he fears that suspicion may fall in their hearts, such as when he circumambulates around their family, for example, and he is shy. End. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: The fatwa is on the opinion of Abu Yusuf concerning the guest, and on the opinion of the two (Sahibayn) concerning others. End.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the sharh (commentary) of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. It addresses a specific scenario: a guest who fears that the household may suspect him of having a wet dream (due to wetness found). The text reports two opinions: In al-Mustasfa, it states that the opinion of Abu Yusuf should be acted upon. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, the fatwa (relied-upon position) differentiates: for a guest, Abu Yusuf's view is followed; for others (non-guests), the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is followed. The phrase 'يظهر أنها كالرجل' likely refers back to a previous discussion equating a woman's ruling to a man's. The passage does not provide the reasoning for the distinction but simply records the fatwa. The key term here is 'الضيف' (guest), indicating a specific social context where consideration of suspicion changes the ruling.

Key Terms
الضيف (al-dayf): A guest staying in someone else's home.
الفتوى (al-fatwa): The relied-upon legal opinion issued for practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, whose opinion is followed for a guest?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) Both Sahibayn

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa selects Abu Yusuf's opinion for a guest fearing suspicion, while following the Sahibayn for others, demonstrating contextual ijtihad.

Semen After Urination: Ghusl Required with Erection and Desire
Condition for ghusl when semen exits after urination based on erection and sexual desire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which semen exiting after urination necessitates ghusl and apply the reasoning (ta'lil) to distinguish between maniy and other fluids.

Core Idea
Semen only necessitates ghusl when emitted with erection and desire; otherwise it does not.

The general rule is that semen exiting after urination does not require ghusl, based on consensus. However, an exception arises when the emission occurs with erection and sexual desire, for then the fluid is identified as maniy and ghusl becomes wajib. This lesson examines the condition and its proof from Hanafi sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Base Ruling
The base ruling: semen exiting after urination does not obligate ghusl by consensus. This is the default position.
Understand that this is a starting point; the exception will follow.
2
Locate the Exception Condition
The text introduces an exception: if the penis is erect (منتشر) at the time of exit, ghusl becomes wajib. If not erect, ghusl is not wajib.
Erection serves as an indicator of sexual desire (شهوة).
3
Examine the Reasoning (Ta'lil)
The reasoning: during erection, the exit occurs with force (دفق) and desire, which are the defining characteristics of maniy. This confirms the fluid is maniy, thus requiring ghusl.
The ta'lil is drawn from the work al-Tanjis.
4
Understand the Scope of the Consensus
The passage clarifies that the consensus applies only to cases without erection/desire. With these conditions, the fluid is deemed maniy and the consensus does not apply.
This prevents misunderstanding the exception as contradicting the consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو خرج مني بعد البول وذكره منتشر وجب الغسل وإن لم يكن ذكره منتشراً لا يجب الغسل، كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان وغيره ومحله إذا وجد الشهوة يدل عليه تعليله في التنجيس بأن في حالة الانتشار وجد الخروج والانفصال جميعاً على وجه الدفق والشهوة وهذا يفيد إطلاق ما قدمنا من أن المني الخارج بعد البول لا يوجب الغسل إجماعاً.
And if semen exits after urination while his penis is erect, ghusl becomes obligatory; and if his penis is not erect, ghusl is not obligatory. Thus in Fatawa Qadikhan and others. And its place is when desire is found, as indicated by his reasoning in al-Tanjis: that in the state of erection, both exit and separation occur with force and desire. And this benefits the absoluteness of what we have presented: that semen exiting after urination does not obligate ghusl by consensus.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with an implicit proof (talil). It clarifies the condition for ghusl when semen exits after urination. The key indicator is the presence of erection and sexual desire (shahwa). The ruling: if the penis is erect at the time of exit, ghusl is wajib; if not erect, ghusl is not wajib. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that during erection, the exit occurs with force and desire, which is the defining characteristic of maniy. The text references Fatawa Qadikhan and also cites the author's own earlier work (al-Tanjis). Importantly, the passage states that there is consensus that semen exiting after urination does NOT obligate ghusl in general—this ruling only applies when erection and desire are present, which indicates the substance is indeed maniy. Thus, the earlier statement is qualified: the consensus applies to cases without erection/desire; with them, ghusl is required because the substance is effectively maniy.

Key Terms
المني (al-maniy): Semen that necessitates ghusl when emitted with desire.
الشهوة (al-shahwa): Sexual desire; a condition for considering the fluid as maniy.
الدفق (al-dafq): Forceful ejection; a characteristic of maniy.

Ghusl for Doubtful Wetness: The Hanafi Dispute Between Abu Yusuf and the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ghusl obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and the Sahibayn regarding ghusl when doubt exists about the nature of wetness found after sleep, and apply the qiyas argument used by the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The Sahibayn require ghusl when doubt exists; Abu Yusuf does not – the cause must be certain.

In this lesson, we examine a key intra-Hanafi dispute about whether ghusl is obligatory when a person wakes up, finds wetness, and is unsure whether it is maniy or madhy, without recalling a dream. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue for obligation based on precaution and analogy, while Abu Yusuf (individually) insists that obligation cannot be established by mere doubt. Understanding this dispute reveals the importance of the principle of ihtiyat in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the point of ikhtilaf
A person wakes up, finds wetness on his garment or thigh, does not recall a dream, and doubts whether it is maniy or madhy. The dispute is whether ghusl is obligatory.
The scenario excludes those who remember a dream, which would make the fluid maniy by consensus.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and his reasoning
Abu Yusuf holds that ghusl is not obligatory because the existence of the cause (maniy) is doubtful. The obligation cannot be established by mere doubt.
His principle: certainty is required for obligation.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
The Sahibayn hold that ghusl is obligatory as a precaution (ihtiyat) due to the possibility that the fluid separated with desire, and by analogy (qiyas) to the case where a person remembers a dream and sees thin fluid – in that case ghusl is obligatory by consensus despite the thinness.
The analogy is based on the possibility that the fluid is maniy.
4
Trace the qiyas in detail
Asl: Remembering a dream and seeing thin fluid → ghusl wajib. Far': Waking up with wetness, no dream recall, doubt. Illa: Possibility that fluid separated with desire (and thus is maniy). The Sahibayn extend the ruling from the asl to the far' because the illa is present.
Abu Yusuf objects that in the far' the possibility is weaker due to lack of dream memory.
5
Note the practical difference and tarjih
In practice, the Sahibayn's view imposes ghusl in doubtful cases; Abu Yusuf's view does not. The text does not give a clear tarjih, but later Hanafi fatwa often follows the Sahibayn for precaution.
The earlier passage indicated that the fatwa may differ for guests; here no explicit preference is given.

Source Text

الخروج كذلك كما هو ثابت في الانفصال كذلك، فالحق أنها ليست بناء على الخلاف بل هو يقول لا يثبت وجوب الغسل بالشك في وجود الموجب وهما احتاطا لقيام ذلك الاحتمال وقياساً على ما لو تذكر الاحتلام ورأى ماء رقيقاً حيث يجب اتفاقاً حملاً للرقة على ما ذكرنا، وقوله أقيس وأخذ به خلف ابن أيوب وأبو الليث كذا في فتح القدير. أنه مني واعلم أن هذه المسألة على اثني عشر وجهاً لأنه إما أن يتيقن أو مذي أو ودي أو شك في ولو حمل قوله بخلاف المرأة على أنها لا تعيد أصلاً لأن ما يخرج منها يحتمل أنه ماء الرجل فهذا وجه المخالفة. قوله : وفيه نظر فإن هذا الاحتمال ثابت الخ) أي كما أن الاحتمال موجود في الانفصال عن مقره موجود علم أنه مذي أو شك في الأخيرين ودي مطلقاً ولا يجب مع عدم تذكر الاحتلام ويجب عندهما فيما إذا شك في الأولين أو في الطرفين أو في ثلاثة احتياطاً، ولا يجب عند أبي يوسف للشك في وجود الموجب اهـ. قوله: (وفيما It was said: Based on the preceding disagreement, a person who wakes up and finds wetness on his thigh or garment, does not recall a dream, and doubts whether it is madhy or maniy: according to the two (Sahibayn) it is obligatory (ghusl) due to the possibility that it separated with desire, then he forgot and it dried in the air, contrary to him (Abu Yusuf). And there is consideration in it: for this possibility exists in exit just as it exists in separation. So the truth is that it is not based on the disagreement, but rather he (Abu Yusuf) says that the obligation of ghusl is not established by doubt in the existence of the cause, while the two (Sahibayn) exercised caution due to the existence of that possibility, and by analogy to when he remembers a dream and sees thin water, where it is obligatory by consensus, interpreting thinness as [indicating maniy]. And his statement 'I apply analogy' and it was adopted by Khalaf ibn Ayyub and Abu al-Layth, thus in Fath al-Qadir. That it is maniy. And know that this issue has twelve aspects: because either he is certain it is maniy, or madhy, or wady, or he doubts between the first and second, or the first and third, or the second and third. And each of these six is either with or without the exit with desire. His statement: (And there is consideration in it...) taken from Sharh al-Munyah by Ibn Amir Haj. Al-Maqdisi said: This is based on what was carried in the words of al-Mubtagha? and if his statement regarding the difference of the woman is interpreted that she does not repeat at all because what exits from her may be the man's water, this is the aspect of difference. His statement: And there is consideration, for this possibility is established... meaning just as the possibility exists in separation from its place, it also exists in separation from the tip of the penis, so it is possible that it separated with desire, so it is obligatory by consensus; therefore basing it on the disagreement is not correct from this mentioned angle, nor making it a consequence like the previous three. His statement: (or) in the second and third: Some added 'or in the three' taking from his words, thus they become fourteen aspects. Then he summarized them with his statement: Either he knows it is maniy, or madhy, or wady, or doubts in the first two, or in the two extremes, or in the last two, or in the three. And in each, either he remembers a dream or not. So ghusl is obligatory by consensus in seven images: when he knows it is madhy or doubts in the first two or in the two extremes or in the last two or in the three and remembers the dream in them; or he knows it is maniy by consensus; when he knows it is wady absolutely; and when he knows it is madhy or doubts in the last two [and it is] absolutely wady? And it is not obligatory with no memory of dream, and it is obligatory according to the two when he doubts in the first two or in the two extremes or in the three as a precaution, and it is not obligatory according to Abu Yusuf due to doubt in the existence of the cause. End. His statement: (And when he is certain it is madhy... [unclear]... maniy maniy that it be with memory of a dream or not: ghusl is obligatory by consensus when he is certain it is maniy whether he remembers a dream or not; and when he is certain it is madhy and remembers a dream, or doubts whether it is maniy or madhy or wady or madhy or wady and remembers a dream in all; and ghusl is not obligatory by consensus when he is certain it is wady, whether he remembers a dream or not, or he doubts whether it is madhy or wady and does not remember a dream, or he is certain it is madhy and does not remember a dream. And ghusl is obligatory according to the two but not according to Abu Yusuf when he doubts whether it is maniy or madhy or maniy or wady and does not remember a dream in either case. And this division, though I have not found it in what I have seen, is a requirement of their statements. But in Fath al-Qadir it is said: Certainty is unattainable with sleep. And in al-Khulasa: We do not obligate ghusl for madhy, but maniy becomes thin over a long period, so its appearance becomes the appearance of madhy, not the reality of madhy. End. And all this is concerning the sleeper when he wakes up and finds wetness. But if he faints and then regains consciousness and finds madhy, or if he is drunk and then regains consciousness and finds madhy, there is no ghusl upon him by consensus, thus in al-Khulasa and others. And the difference is that maniy and madhy must have a cause, and in sleep it appears whether he remembers or not, because sleep is a likely occasion for wet dreams, so it is attributed to it. Then it is possible that it is maniy that thinned in the air or due to nutrition, so we consider it maniy as a precaution. It is not so for the drunk and the one who fainted, because this cause did not appear in them.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion (sharh) of a ruling concerning a person who wakes up and finds wetness but is uncertain about its nature. The author, building on a previous dispute (intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf), enumerates twelve (or fourteen) scenarios based on two variables: (1) the substance found (maniy, madhy, wady, or doubt between them), and (2) whether the person remembers having a wet dream (ihtilam). The key legal consequence is the obligation of ghusl. The passage contains an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that ghusl is not required when there is doubt about the existence of the cause (i.e., emission with desire), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require ghusl as a precaution (ihtiyat) and by analogy to the case where the person remembers a dream and sees thin fluid. The text then provides a systematic classification of all possible combinations and the rulings for each, noting where there is consensus (ittifaq) and where there is ikhtilaf. The author also cites Fath al-Qadir to note that certainty is difficult after sleep, and al-Khulasa to explain that maniy can become thin and appear like madhy. Finally, the passage distinguishes the case of sleepers from those who were unconscious or drunk: for the latter, if they find madhy upon awakening, ghusl is not required by consensus, because the cause (ihtilam) is not reasonably present. This ruling is part of the chapter on Taharah regarding the causes of ghusl.

Key Terms
المني (al-maniy): Semen that necessitates ghusl; in sleep it is presumed from the possibility of ihtilam.
المذي (al-madhy): Pre-ejaculatory fluid that does not necessitate ghusl.
الودي (al-wady): Thick white fluid sometimes discharged after urination, not requiring ghusl.
الاحتلام (al-ihtilam): A wet dream; its memory serves as evidence that the fluid is maniy.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Precautionary reasoning used by the Sahibayn to require ghusl in cases of doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The fluid is definitely maniy because it is wet.
B) The possibility that the fluid separated with desire, and by analogy to the dream recall case.
C) The person remembers a dream, so it is maniy.
D) The fluid is madhy and ghusl is always required for any discharge.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when doubt exists about wetness after sleep, the Sahibayn's precautionary position (obligatory ghusl) is generally followed, but Abu Yusuf's view demonstrates the principle that obligation requires proven cause.

The Twelve (or Fourteen) Cases: Systematic Rulings for Wetness After Sleep
Systematic classification of rulings for wetness after sleep

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any scenario of wetness after sleep according to the twelve-case system and determine the corresponding ruling (ghusl wajib or not) based on the substance type, dream recall, and the view of the imams.

Core Idea
There are twelve base cases, each multiplied by dream recall, yielding fourteen – but the system simplifies to: maniy always requires ghusl, wady never, and doubtful cases require precaution according to the Sahibayn.

This lesson builds on the previous dispute by presenting a comprehensive classification of all possible scenarios when a person wakes up and finds wetness. The text enumerates twelve cases based on what substance is found (maniy, madhy, wady, or combinations of doubt) and whether the exit was accompanied by desire. Each case is further divided by whether the person remembers a dream. The rulings are either by consensus (ittifaq) or subject to the ikhtilaf we studied earlier.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six basic scenarios for substance identification
The person may be certain it is maniy, madhy, or wady, or may doubt between two of them: maniy/madhy, maniy/wady, or madhy/wady. That gives six possibilities.
The text calls these six and then each is multiplied by the presence or absence of desire (shahwa) in exit, making twelve.
2
Multiply by desire factor and dream recall
Each of the six is divided into two: with desire or without desire. Additionally, for each scenario, whether the person remembers a dream (ihtilam) further affects the ruling. The text further adds the option of doubt in all three substances, making fourteen.
The total number is either twelve or fourteen depending on inclusion of the triple doubt.
3
Determine ruling by consensus: maniy always wajib, wady never
If the person is certain it is maniy (regardless of dream recall or desire), ghusl is wajib by consensus. If certain it is wady (regardless of dream recall), ghusl is not wajib by consensus.
Wady is not a cause of janabah.
4
Determine ruling for madhy and doubtful cases
If the person is certain it is madhy and does not remember a dream, ghusl is not wajib by consensus. If remembers a dream or doubts between maniy/madhy (with dream recall), ghusl is wajib by consensus. If doubts without dream recall, it is the disputed case: wajib according to the Sahibayn, not according to Abu Yusuf.
The text enumerates seven images where ghusl is wajib by consensus.
5
Note special cases: unconscious and drunk
If a person faints or is intoxicated and upon awakening finds madhy (only), ghusl is not obligatory by consensus. This is because the cause (ihtilam) is not present in these states.
The distinction is based on the fact that sleep is a likely occasion for wet dreams, unlike unconsciousness or intoxication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الأول والثاني أو في الأول والثالث أو في الثاني والثالث، وكل من هذه الستة إما للخروج بشهوة قوله : (وفيه نظر الخ) مأخوذ من شرح المنية لابن أمير حاج قال المقدسي : وهذا مبني على ما حمل كلام المبتغى عليه ولو حمل قوله بخلاف المرأة على أنها لا تعيد أصلاً لأن ما يخرج منها يحتمل أنه ماء الرجل فهذا وجه المخالفة. قوله : وفيه نظر فإن هذا الاحتمال ثابت الخ) أي كما أن الاحتمال موجود في الانفصال عن مقره موجود أيضاً في الانفصال عن رأس الذكر فيحتمل انفصاله عن شهوة فيجب اتفاقاً فلا بناؤها على الخلاف يصح من هذا الوجه المذكور، ولا جعلها من ثمرته كالثلاثة السابقة. قوله : (أو) في الثاني والثالث) زاد بعضهم أو في الثلاثة أخذاً كلامه، وعليه فتكون على أربعة عشر وجهاً. ثم ضبطها بقوله : إما أن يعلم أنه مني أو مذي أو أو شك في الأولين أو في الطرفين أو في الأخيرين أو في الثلاثة. وعلى كل إما أن يتذكر احتلاماً أو لا فيجب الغسل اتفاقاً في سبع صور منها وهي ما إذا علم أنه مذي أو شك في الأولين أو في الطرفين أو في الأخيرين أو في الثلاثة تذكر الاحتلام فيها، أو علم أنه مني اتفاقاً فيما إذا علم أنه ودي مطلقاً وفيما إذا علم أنه مذي أو شك في الأخيرين ودي مطلقاً ولا يجب مع عدم تذكر الاحتلام ويجب عندهما فيما إذا شك في الأولين أو في الطرفين أو في ثلاثة احتياطاً، ولا يجب عند أبي يوسف للشك في وجود الموجب اهـ. قوله: (وفيما إذا تيقن أنه مذي مني مني أن تكون مع تذكر الاحتلام أو لا فيجب الغسل اتفاقاً فيما إذا تيقن أنه مني وتذكر الاحتلام أو لا، وفيما إذا تيقن أنه مذي وتذكر الاحتلام أو شك أنه أو مذي أو أو ودي أو مذي أو ودي وتذكر الاحتلام في الكل، ولا يجب الغسل اتفاقاً فيما إذا تيقن أنه ودي، تذكر الاحتلام أو لا، أو شك أنه مذي أو ودي ولم يتذكر الاحتلام أو تيقن أنه مذي ولم يتذكر الاحتلام. ويجب الغسل عندهما لا عند أبي يوسف فيما إذ شك أنه مني أو مذي أو مني أو ودي ولم يتذكر الاحتلام فيهما. وهذا التقسيم وإن لم أجده فيما رأيت لكنه مقتضى عباراتهم لكن قال في فتح القدير : التيقن متعذر مع النوم. وفي الخلاصة ولسنا نوجب الغسل بالمذي لكن المني يرق بإطالة المدة فتصير صورته صورة المذي لا حقيقة المذي ا هـ . وهذا كله في النائم إذا استيقظ فوجد بللاً. أما إذا غشي عليه فأفاق فوجد مذياً أو كان سكران فأفاق فوجده مذياً لا غسل عليه اتفاقاً كذا في الخلاصة .وغيرها والفرق بأن المني والمذي لا بد له من سبب وقد ظهر في النوم تذكر أو لا، لأن النوم مظنة الاحتلام فيحال عليه. ثم يحتمل أنه مني رق بالهواء أو للغذاء فاعتبرناه منياً احتياطاً ولا كذلك السكران والمغمى عليه لأنه لم يظهر فيهما هذا السبب.
It was said: Based on the preceding disagreement, a person who wakes up and finds wetness on his thigh or garment, does not recall a dream, and doubts whether it is madhy or maniy: according to the two (Sahibayn) it is obligatory (ghusl) due to the possibility that it separated with desire, then he forgot and it dried in the air, contrary to him (Abu Yusuf). And there is consideration in it: for this possibility exists in exit just as it exists in separation. So the truth is that it is not based on the disagreement, but rather he (Abu Yusuf) says that the obligation of ghusl is not established by doubt in the existence of the cause, while the two (Sahibayn) exercised caution due to the existence of that possibility, and by analogy to when he remembers a dream and sees thin water, where it is obligatory by consensus, interpreting thinness as [indicating maniy]. And his statement 'I apply analogy' and it was adopted by Khalaf ibn Ayyub and Abu al-Layth, thus in Fath al-Qadir. That it is maniy. And know that this issue has twelve aspects: because either he is certain it is maniy, or madhy, or wady, or he doubts between the first and second, or the first and third, or the second and third. And each of these six is either with or without the exit with desire. His statement: (And there is consideration in it...) taken from Sharh al-Munyah by Ibn Amir Haj. Al-Maqdisi said: This is based on what was carried in the words of al-Mubtagha? and if his statement regarding the difference of the woman is interpreted that she does not repeat at all because what exits from her may be the man's water, this is the aspect of difference. His statement: And there is consideration, for this possibility is established... meaning just as the possibility exists in separation from its place, it also exists in separation from the tip of the penis, so it is possible that it separated with desire, so it is obligatory by consensus; therefore basing it on the disagreement is not correct from this mentioned angle, nor making it a consequence like the previous three. His statement: (or) in the second and third: Some added 'or in the three' taking from his words, thus they become fourteen aspects. Then he summarized them with his statement: Either he knows it is maniy, or madhy, or wady, or doubts in the first two, or in the two extremes, or in the last two, or in the three. And in each, either he remembers a dream or not. So ghusl is obligatory by consensus in seven images: when he knows it is madhy or doubts in the first two or in the two extremes or in the last two or in the three and remembers the dream in them; or he knows it is maniy by consensus; when he knows it is wady absolutely; and when he knows it is madhy or doubts in the last two [and it is] absolutely wady? And it is not obligatory with no memory of dream, and it is obligatory according to the two when he doubts in the first two or in the two extremes or in the three as a precaution, and it is not obligatory according to Abu Yusuf due to doubt in the existence of the cause. End. His statement: (And when he is certain it is madhy... [unclear]... maniy maniy that it be with memory of a dream or not: ghusl is obligatory by consensus when he is certain it is maniy whether he remembers a dream or not; and when he is certain it is madhy and remembers a dream, or doubts whether it is maniy or madhy or wady or madhy or wady and remembers a dream in all; and ghusl is not obligatory by consensus when he is certain it is wady, whether he remembers a dream or not, or he doubts whether it is madhy or wady and does not remember a dream, or he is certain it is madhy and does not remember a dream. And ghusl is obligatory according to the two but not according to Abu Yusuf when he doubts whether it is maniy or madhy or maniy or wady and does not remember a dream in either case. And this division, though I have not found it in what I have seen, is a requirement of their statements. But in Fath al-Qadir it is said: Certainty is unattainable with sleep. And in al-Khulasa: We do not obligate ghusl for madhy, but maniy becomes thin over a long period, so its appearance becomes the appearance of madhy, not the reality of madhy. End. And all this is concerning the sleeper when he wakes up and finds wetness. But if he faints and then regains consciousness and finds madhy, or if he is drunk and then regains consciousness and finds madhy, there is no ghusl upon him by consensus, thus in al-Khulasa and others. And the difference is that maniy and madhy must have a cause, and in sleep it appears whether he remembers or not, because sleep is a likely occasion for wet dreams, so it is attributed to it. Then it is possible that it is maniy that thinned in the air or due to nutrition, so we consider it maniy as a precaution. It is not so for the drunk and the one who fainted, because this cause did not appear in them.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion (sharh) of a ruling concerning a person who wakes up and finds wetness but is uncertain about its nature. The author, building on a previous dispute (intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf), enumerates twelve (or fourteen) scenarios based on two variables: (1) the substance found (maniy, madhy, wady, or doubt between them), and (2) whether the person remembers having a wet dream (ihtilam). The key legal consequence is the obligation of ghusl. The passage contains an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that ghusl is not required when there is doubt about the existence of the cause (i.e., emission with desire), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require ghusl as a precaution (ihtiyat) and by analogy to the case where the person remembers a dream and sees thin fluid. The text then provides a systematic classification of all possible combinations and the rulings for each, noting where there is consensus (ittifaq) and where there is ikhtilaf. The author also cites Fath al-Qadir to note that certainty is difficult after sleep, and al-Khulasa to explain that maniy can become thin and appear like madhy. Finally, the passage distinguishes the case of sleepers from those who were unconscious or drunk: for the latter, if they find madhy upon awakening, ghusl is not required by consensus, because the cause (ihtilam) is not reasonably present. This ruling is part of the chapter on Taharah regarding the causes of ghusl.

Key Terms
المني (al-maniy): Semen that necessitates ghusl; in sleep it is presumed from the possibility of ihtilam.
المذي (al-madhy): Pre-ejaculatory fluid that does not necessitate ghusl.
الودي (al-wady): Thick white fluid sometimes discharged after urination, not requiring ghusl.
الاحتلام (al-ihtilam): A wet dream; its memory serves as evidence that the fluid is maniy.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Precautionary reasoning used by the Sahibayn to require ghusl in cases of doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which of the following scenarios is ghusl NOT obligatory by consensus?
A) He is certain it is maniy and remembers a dream
B) He is certain it is wady and remembers a dream
C) He is certain it is madhy and remembers a dream
D) He doubts between maniy and madhy and remembers a dream

Key Takeaway
The twelve-case system provides a comprehensive framework: maniy always requires ghusl, wady never, and doubtful cases require precaution according to the Sahibayn, but certain scenarios (like certainty of madhy without dream) have consensus on no ghusl.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
Obligation of Ghusl for a Woman with Wet Dream: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the condition for ghusl after a woman's wet dream.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the condition for ghusl on a woman after a wet dream according to Zahir al-Riwayah, identify the position of Imam Muhammad, and evaluate the tarjih mechanism that settles the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
For a woman's wet dream, ghusl requires external exit — internal emission alone is insufficient.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a disputed point within the Hanafi school: does a woman need to perform ghusl if she has a wet dream but does not see any fluid exiting her body? The majority view (Zahir al-Riwayah) conditions ghusl on visible exit, while Imam Muhammad obligates it upon certainty of internal emission. Understanding this ikhtilaf reveals the school's reliance on qiyas (analogy to men) and the authoritative weight of Zahir al-Riwayah rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed condition
What exactly triggers ghusl for a woman after a wet dream? The dispute centers on whether internal emission alone suffices or external exit is required.
The condition is the exit of maniy to the outer vagina according to the majority.
2
State the majority (Zahir al-Riwayah) position and its evidence
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that ghusl is not obligatory unless water exits to the external vagina. Their evidence includes the hadith of Umm Sulaym ('if she sees water') interpreted as visual sighting, and qiyas on a man's ghusl which requires exit from the penis.
This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
3
State Imam Muhammad's position and its evidence
Imam Muhammad holds that ghusl is obligatory if the woman is certain of emission, even without external sighting. He interprets 'seeing' as knowledge and attaches obligation to the existence of maniy.
This view is considered weaker in the school.
4
Analyze the tarjih
Multiple later authorities (al-Halabi, al-Tatarkhaniyya) affirm that the majority view is mufta bihi because it is from Zahir al-Riwayah, consistent with qiyas, and avoids undue burden from uncertain sleep experiences.
The tarjih is based on authority weight and methodological consistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة
أعرض عنه وليس ببعيد فيما يظهر والقياس أنه لا يجب الغسل على واحد منهما لوقوع الشك. وإذا لم يجب عليهما لا يجوز لها أن تقتدي به والوجه فيه ظاهر، ولا يخفى أن هذا كله فيما إذا لم يكن الفراش قد نام عليه غيرهما قبلهما، وأما إذا كان قد نام عليه غيرهما وكان المني المرئي يابساً فالظاهر أنه لا يجب الغسل على واحد منهما.
ولو احتملت المرأة ولم يخرج الماء إلى ظاهر فرجها، عن محمد يجب، وفي ظاهر الرواية لا يجب لأن خروج منيها إلى فرجها الخارج شرط لوجوب الغسل عليها وعليه الفتوى كذا في معراج الدراية، والذي حرره في فتح القدير وقال إنه الحق الاتفاق على تعلق وجوب الغسل بوجود المني في احتلامهما، والقائل بوجوبه في هذه الخلافية إنما يوجبه على وجوده وإن لم تره فالمراد بعدم الخروج في قولهم ولم يخرج منها لم تره خرج فعلى هذا إلا وجه وجوب الغسل في الخلافية. والمراد بالرؤية في جواب النبي أم سليم لما سألته هل على المرأة من غسل إذا هي استيقظت في فور الاحتلام فأحست بيدها البلل ثم نامت فاستيقظت حتى جف فلم تر بعينها شيئاً لا القول بأن لا غسل عليها مع أنه لا رؤية بصر بل رؤية علم ورأي تستعمل يسع حقيقة في علم باتفاق أهل اللغة قال : رأيت الله أكبر كل شيء . ا هـ. ولو جومعت فيما دون الفرج فسبق الماء إلى فرجها أو جومعت البكر لا غسل عليها إلا إذا ظهر الحبل لأنها لا تحبل إلا إذا أنزلت وتعيد ما صلت إن لم تكن اغتسلت لأنه ظهر أنها صلت بلا طهارة. ولو جومعت فاغتسلت ثم خرج منها مني الرجل لا غسل عليها، ولو قالت معي جني يأتيني في النوم مراراً وأجد ما أجد إذا جامعني زوجي لا غسل عليها. وفي فتح القدير: ولا يخفى أنه مقيد بما إذا لم تر الماء فإن رأته صريحاً وجب كأنه احتلام وقد يقال : ينبغي وجوب الغسل من غير إنزال لوجود الإيلاج لأنها تعرف أنه يجامعها كما لا يخفى ولا يظهر هذا الاشتراط
عن محمد أنها يجب عليها الغسل وبه أخذ صاحب التنجيس معللاً بما تقدم وهو ليس بقوي إذ لا أثر في نزول مائها من صدرها غير دافق في وجوب الغسل فإن وجوب الغسل في الاحتلام متعلق بخروج المني من الفرج الداخل كما تعلق في حق الرجل بخروجه من رأس الذكر، فكما أن الرجل لو انفصل منيه عن الصلب بالدفق والشهوة لا يجب عليه الغسل ما لم يخرج إلى ما يلحقه حكم التطهير لا يجب عليها الغسل على أن في مسألتنا لم يعلم انفصال منيها عن صدرها وإنما حصل ذلك في النوم وأكثر ما يرى في النوم لا تحقق له فكيف يجب عليها الغسل ؟ نعم قال بعضهم: لو كانت مستلقية وقت الاحتلام يجب عليها الغسل لاحتمال الخروج ثم العود فيجب الغسل احتياطاً وهو غير بعيد إلا من حيث إن ماءها إذا لم ينزل فقابل سيلاناً يلزم إما عدم الخروج إن لم يكن الفرج في صبب أو عدم العود إن كان في صبب فليتأمل قوله : (فإنها لا تحبل إلا إذا أنزلت) أقول : لا يخفى أن الحبل يتوقف على انفصال الماء عن مقره لا على خروجه ، فالظاهر أن وجوب الغسل مبني على الرواية السابقة عن محمد تأمل. ثم رأيت العلامة الحلبي صرح بذلك في شرح المنية الكبير جازماً بذلك فقال : ولا شك أنه مبني على وجوب الغسل عليها بمجرد انفصال منيها إلى رحمها وهو خلاف الأصح الذي هو ظاهر الرواية. قال في التتارخانية : وفي ظاهر الرواية يشترط الخروج من الفرج الداخل إلى الفرج الخارج لوجوب الغسل حتى لو انفصل منها عن مكانه ولم يخرج عن الفرج الداخل إلى الفرج الخارج لا غسل عليها وفي النصاب وهو الأصح .اهـ. فالحمد لله رب العالمين. قوله: (فاغتسلت ثم خرج منها مني الرجل لا غسل عليها) قال الرملي : أقول وعليها الوضوء كما في التتارخانية نقلا عن مجموع النوازل قوله : ( وقد يقال ينبغي وجوب الغسل من غير إنزال) لا يخفى أن هذا مما لا ينبغي لأن الكلام فيما إذا كان يأتيها في النوم وهي في هذه الحالة لو رأت أنه جامعها مائة أنسي لا يجب عليها الغسل ما لم تنزل، نعم لو كانت تراه في حالة اليقظة يتأتى ما قال وكأنه نسي التقييد بالنوم وإلا فلا وجه له كما علمت ثم رأيت الشيخ اسماعيل ضبط قوله في اليوم صرح به
Book of Purification. He turned away from it and it is not far in what appears, and by analogy ghusl is not obligatory on either of them due to doubt. And since it is not obligatory on both of them, she may not follow him in prayer, and the point is clear. And it is not hidden that all this applies when no one else had slept on the bed before them. But if someone else had slept on it and the visible semen was dry, then apparently ghusl is not obligatory on either of them. If a woman had a wet dream and water did not come out to her external vagina, according to Muhammad it is obligatory, but in Zahir al-Riwayah it is not obligatory because the exit of her semen to her external vagina is a condition for the obligation of ghusl, and on this is the fatwa, as in Miraj al-Dirayah. And what was edited in Fath al-Qadir and he said that it is correct that there is agreement that the obligation of ghusl is attached to the presence of semen in their wet dreams, and the one who says it is obligatory in this disputed case only obliges it based on its existence even if she did not see it. So the meaning of 'did not come out' in their statement 'and did not come out from her' is that she did not see it come out. On this basis, the obligation of ghusl in the disputed case is understandable. And what is meant by 'seeing' in the Prophet's answer to Umm Sulaym when she asked whether a woman has ghusl if she wakes up immediately after a wet dream and feels wetness with her hand, then sleeps again and wakes up after it dried, and saw nothing with her eyes—there is no statement that there is no ghusl on her, although there is no visual seeing but rather seeing of knowledge and opinion. 'Seeing' is used in reality for knowledge by agreement of linguists. He said: I saw that Allah is greater than everything. End. And if she was penetrated below the vagina and water preceded to her vagina, or a virgin was penetrated, there is no ghusl on her unless pregnancy appears, because she does not conceive unless she has an orgasm, and she must repeat what she prayed if she did not perform ghusl because it becomes apparent that she prayed without purification. And if she was penetrated and performed ghusl, then the man's semen came out from her, there is no ghusl on her. And if she says, 'A jinn comes to me in my sleep repeatedly and I feel what I feel when my husband has intercourse with me,' there is no ghusl on her. And in Fath al-Qadir: 'And it is not hidden that this is conditioned by her not seeing water; if she clearly sees it, it becomes obligatory, as if it were a wet dream. And it may be said that ghusl should be obligatory without orgasm due to the occurrence of penetration because she knows he is having intercourse with her, as is not hidden, and this condition is not apparent.' From Muhammad that ghusl is obligatory on her, and the author of al-Tanjis adopted it, giving the reason mentioned earlier, but it is not strong because there is no effect of her water descending from her chest without being ejaculated in the obligation of ghusl. Indeed, the obligation of ghusl in a wet dream is related to the exit of semen from the inner vagina, just as it is related in the man to its exit from the head of the penis. So just as a man, if his semen separates from the spine with ejaculation and desire, ghusl is not obligatory on him until it exits to a place subject to purification, similarly ghusl is not obligatory on her. Moreover, in our case it is not known that her semen separated from her chest; that only happened in sleep, and most of what is seen in sleep has no reality, so how can ghusl be obligatory? Some said: if she was lying on her back at the time of the wet dream, ghusl is obligatory on her due to the possibility of exit and then return, so ghusl is obligatory as a precaution. This is not far, except that since her water does not flow easily, it entails either non-exit if the vagina is not in a downward slope, or non-return if it is. So reflect on his statement: 'She does not conceive unless she has an orgasm.' I say: it is not hidden that conception depends on the separation of water from its place, not on its exit. So apparently the obligation of ghusl is based on the previous narration from Muhammad; reflect. Then I saw al-Halabi explicitly state in Sharh al-Munya al-Kabir, affirming that, saying: 'There is no doubt that this is based on the obligation of ghusl on her merely by the separation of her semen into her womb, which is contrary to the more correct view that is Zahir al-Riwayah.' He said in al-Tatarkhaniyya: 'In Zahir al-Riwayah, exit from the inner vagina to the outer vagina is a condition for the obligation of ghusl, such that even if it separates from its place and does not exit from the inner to the outer vagina, there is no ghusl on her. And in al-Nisab this is the more correct.' End. So praise be to Allah. His statement: 'She performed ghusl then the man's semen came out from her, there is no ghusl on her.' Al-Ramli said: I say, and she must perform wudu, as in al-Tatarkhaniyya quoting from Majmu' al-Nawazil. His statement: 'And it may be said that ghusl should be obligatory without orgasm.' It is not hidden that this is not appropriate because the discussion is about sleep; in this state, if she sees that he has intercourse with her a hundred times, ghusl is not obligatory on her unless she has an orgasm. Yes, if she saw him in wakefulness, what he said could apply. It is as if he forgot the restriction of sleep; otherwise there is no basis for it, as you know. Then I saw Shaykh Isma'il recorded his statement as 'in the day,' he explicitly stated it.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the obligation of ghusl (ritual bath) on a woman after experiencing a wet dream (ihtilam) without observing any fluid externally. The discussion centers on the condition for ghusl: is the mere internal emission of maniy sufficient, or must it exit to the outer vagina? The text opens by revisiting an earlier ruling about a shared bed where doubt arises; the preferred view (zahir al-riwayah) is that ghusl is not obligatory on either person due to doubt. It then moves to the specific case of a woman who has a wet dream but does not see water exiting. According to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, ghusl is obligatory because she may have emitted without noticing. However, the majority opinion in Zahir al-Riwayah—represented by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf—holds that ghusl is not obligatory unless the water exits to the external vagina. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi). The author of Fath al-Qadir attempts to reconcile by arguing that all agree obligation attaches to presence of semen; the dispute is only about what constitutes 'seeing' in the hadith of Umm Sulaym. But the commentator al-Halabi and the author of al-Tatarkhaniyya reaffirm the Zahir al-Riwayah position: exit to the outer vagina is a necessary condition. The passage also discusses subsidiary issues: if a woman is penetrated but water does not exit, ghusl is not required unless pregnancy appears; if she performs ghusl and then man's semen exits, no further ghusl but wudu may be needed; and claims of jinn intercourse in sleep do not necessitate ghusl without emission. The text refutes the suggestion that ghusl could be obligatory due to penetration alone without orgasm, emphasizing that in sleep, ghusl requires either seeing water or certainty of emission. The overall authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah, and the mufta bihi is that exit to the outer vagina is required.

Key Terms
احتلام (ihtilam): A wet dream; experiencing a nocturnal emission or sexual dream.
مني (maniy): The fluid emitted during orgasm; for men it is thick, for women it is thin and yellow. Its exit triggers ghusl.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known and transmitted rulings from the early Hanafi masters (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) as compiled by Imam Muhammad in his six books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, when is ghusl obligatory on a woman after a wet dream?
A) Whenever she is certain she had a wet dream, even if no water is seen.
B) Only if water exits to the outer part of her vagina.
C) Whenever she sees any wetness on her body, regardless of source.
D) Only if she experienced orgasm during the dream.

Key Takeaway
A woman's ghusl after a wet dream is conditioned upon visible external exit of water, per the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Ghusl After a Wet Dream: The Condition of Exit
Primary ruling and full intra-Hanafi dispute analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl for a woman who feels wetness after a dream but sees no water, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the condition of exit.

Core Idea
Ghusl after a wet dream requires actual exit of semen from the inner private part, not mere knowledge of wetness.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a specific scenario: a woman wakes from a wet dream, feels wetness, but does not see any water. The author presents the default ruling (no ghusl), then unpacks an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether certainty of discharge suffices. The resolution hinges on the legal analogy between male and female ghusl obligations, and the precise definition of 'exit' in Hanafi fiqh. Understanding this ruling refines your sense of how Hanafi jurists apply conditions (shurūṭ) and evaluate conflicting narrations within the school.

Guided Path
1
State the default ruling
Identify the act (woman after wet dream) and the ruling given: no ghusl required.
The author initially states 'no ghusl upon her' despite her feeling wetness.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note that Imam Muhammad (in a rare narration) holds ghusl obligatory if she is certain of discharge. Understand why the author rejects this view as weak.
The author labels Muhammad's narration as 'laysa bi-qawī' (not strong).
3
Trace the analogy (qiyas)
The Hanafi position uses analogy to a man: just as a man requires emission from the penis, a woman requires exit from the inner private part to the outer. See how the author links ghusl obligation to actual exit, not mere separation.
The 'farj dākhil' to 'farj khārij' condition is central.
4
Evaluate the tarjīḥ
The author cites later authorities (al-Halabi, al-Tartarkhani) confirming that the apparent narration (ẓāhir al-riwāya) is the soundest (al-aṣaḥḥ). Understand why the muftā bihī requires either sight of water or actual exit.
Al-Nisab is mentioned as affirming the soundest view.

Source Text

غسل إذا هي استيقظت في فور الاحتلام فأحست بيدها البلل ثم نامت فاستيقظت حتى جف فلم تر بعينها شيئاً لا القول بأن لا غسل عليها مع أنه لا رؤية بصر بل رؤية علم ورأي تستعمل يسع حقيقة في علم باتفاق أهل اللغة قال : رأيت الله أكبر كل شيء . ا هـ. ولو جومعت فيما دون الفرج فسبق الماء إلى فرجها أو جومعت البكر لا غسل عليها إلا إذا ظهر الحبل لأنها لا تحبل إلا إذا أنزلت وتعيد ما صلت إن لم تكن اغتسلت لأنه ظهر أنها صلت بلا طهارة. ولو جومعت فاغتسلت ثم خرج منها مني الرجل لا غسل عليها، ولو قالت معي جني يأتيني في النوم مراراً وأجد ما أجد إذا جامعني زوجي لا غسل عليها. وفي فتح القدير: ولا يخفى أنه مقيد بما إذا لم تر الماء فإن رأته صريحاً وجب كأنه احتلام وقد يقال : ينبغي وجوب الغسل من غير إنزال لوجود الإيلاج لأنها تعرف أنه يجامعها كما لا يخفى ولا يظهر هذا الاشتراط
احتلمت؟ قال : نعم إذا رأت الماء العلم مطلقاً فإنها لو تيقنت الإنزال بأن
عن محمد أنها يجب عليها الغسل وبه أخذ صاحب التنجيس معللاً بما تقدم وهو ليس بقوي إذ لا أثر في نزول مائها من صدرها غير دافق في وجوب الغسل فإن وجوب الغسل في الاحتلام متعلق بخروج المني من الفرج الداخل كما تعلق في حق الرجل بخروجه من رأس الذكر، فكما أن الرجل لو انفصل منيه عن الصلب بالدفق والشهوة لا يجب عليه الغسل ما لم يخرج إلى ما يلحقه حكم التطهير لا يجب عليها الغسل على أن في مسألتنا لم يعلم انفصال منيها عن صدرها وإنما حصل ذلك في النوم وأكثر ما يرى في النوم لا تحقق له فكيف يجب عليها الغسل ؟ نعم قال بعضهم: لو كانت مستلقية وقت الاحتلام يجب عليها الغسل لاحتمال الخروج ثم العود فيجب الغسل احتياطاً وهو غير بعيد إلا من حيث إن ماءها إذا لم ينزل فقابل سيلاناً يلزم إما عدم الخروج إن لم يكن الفرج في صبب أو عدم العود إن كان في صبب فليتأمل قوله : (فإنها لا تحبل إلا إذا أنزلت) أقول : لا يخفى أن الحبل يتوقف على انفصال الماء عن مقره لا على خروجه ، فالظاهر أن وجوب الغسل مبني على الرواية السابقة عن محمد تأمل. ثم رأيت العلامة الحلبي صرح بذلك في شرح المنية الكبير جازماً بذلك فقال : ولا شك أنه مبني على وجوب الغسل عليها بمجرد انفصال منيها إلى رحمها وهو خلاف الأصح الذي هو ظاهر الرواية. قال في التتارخانية : وفي ظاهر الرواية يشترط الخروج من الفرج الداخل إلى الفرج الخارج لوجوب الغسل حتى لو انفصل منها عن مكانه ولم يخرج عن الفرج الداخل إلى الفرج الخارج لا غسل عليها وفي النصاب وهو الأصح .اهـ. فالحمد لله رب العالمين.
Ghusl: If she wakes up in the immediate aftermath of a wet dream and feels wetness with her hand, then sleeps and wakes up after it has dried, and does not see anything with her eyes, the ruling is that there is no ghusl upon her, even though there is no sight with the eyes, but rather knowledge and opinion that is used broadly in knowledge by consensus of the people of language. He said: I saw God is Greater than everything. End quote. And if she is engaged in intercourse without the front (without penetration) and water precedes to her private part, or a virgin is married (consummated), there is no ghusl upon her unless pregnancy appears, because she does not become pregnant unless she has discharge. And she must repeat what she prayed if she did not perform ghusl, because it becomes clear that she prayed without purity. And if she is engaged in intercourse and performs ghusl, then the man's semen comes out of her, there is no ghusl upon her. And if she says, 'A jinn comes to me in sleep repeatedly and I find what I find when my husband has intercourse with me,' there is no ghusl upon her. And in Fath al-Qadir: It is not hidden that this is conditioned upon her not seeing water; if she sees it clearly, it becomes obligatory as if it were a wet dream. And it may be said that ghusl should be obligatory without discharge due to the presence of insertion, because she knows that he is having intercourse with her, as is not hidden, and this condition is not apparent. 'She had a wet dream?' He said: Yes, if she sees water, absolutely in knowledge, for if she is certain of discharge, according to Muhammad, ghusl is obligatory upon her, and the author of al-Tanjis adopted this, reasoning with what preceded, but it is not strong, because there is no effect of the descent of her water from her chest non-ejaculatory in requiring ghusl. Indeed, the obligation of ghusl in a wet dream is connected to the emission of semen from the inner private part, just as it is connected for a man to its emission from the head of the penis. And just as if a man's semen separates from his spine with force and desire, ghusl is not obligatory upon him until it exits to what is subject to the rule of purification, so ghusl is not obligatory upon her. Moreover, in our case, it is not known that her semen separated from her chest; rather, that happened during sleep, and most of what is seen in sleep has no reality. So how is ghusl obligatory upon her? Yes, some said: If she was lying on her back at the time of the wet dream, ghusl is obligatory upon her due to the possibility of emission and then return, so ghusl is obligatory as a precaution. This is not far-fetched, except that if her water does not descend, the possibility of flowing necessitates either no emission if the private part is not in a downward slope, or no return if it is in a downward slope, so let it be pondered. His statement: (For she does not become pregnant unless she discharges.) I say: It is not hidden that pregnancy depends on the separation of the water from its reservoir, not on its exit. So it appears that the obligation of ghusl is based on the earlier narration from Muhammad. Ponder. Then I saw al-Allama al-Halabi stated this clearly in Sharh al-Munyah al-Kabir, affirming it, saying: There is no doubt that it is based on the obligation of ghusl upon her simply due to the separation of her semen into her womb, which is contrary to the soundest opinion that is the apparent narration. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: In the apparent narration, it is a condition that it exits from the inner private part to the outer private part for the obligation of ghusl, such that if it separates from its place and does not exit from the inner private part to the outer private part, there is no ghusl upon her. And in al-Nisab, it is the soundest. End quote. So praise be to God, Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with extensive intra-Hanafi dispute analysis. The core issue is whether a woman must perform ghusl after a wet dream if she feels wetness but does not see any water upon waking. The author first states the ruling: no ghusl is required, because mere knowledge (ʿilm) without sight (baṣar) is not sufficient. He cites the linguistic point that the word 'ra'ā' (to see) can be used for knowledge, but in this legal context it requires actual sight. He then mentions a narration from Imam Muhammad that if a woman is certain of discharge, ghusl is obligatory. The author dismisses this as weak, arguing that ghusl in a wet dream is linked to the actual exit of semen from the inner private part (farj dākhil), analogous to a man where ghusl is required only when semen exits the penis. Since there is no evidence of actual exit in this case, ghusl is not obligatory. He discusses a precautionary view for a woman lying on her back (mustalqiyya), but ultimately the relied-upon position (al-aṣaḥḥ) is that exit from the inner to the outer private part is necessary. The verse and hadith are briefly referenced but the argument is mainly rational (dalīl ʿaqlī) and based on analogy. The passage also includes a secondary ruling about a woman who has intercourse without penetration or a virgin: no ghusl unless pregnancy appears, because pregnancy requires discharge. The author concludes with praise.

Key Terms
رؤية علم (ruʾyat ʿilm): Knowledge-based 'seeing' that is not literal visual sight, but certain inference.
الفرج الداخل (al-farj al-dākhil): The inner part of the female genitalia from which semen must exit to require ghusl.
الدفق (al-dafq): Forceful ejection of semen accompanied by sexual desire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent narration (ẓāhir al-riwāya), what is the condition for ghusl to be obligatory on a woman after a wet dream?
A) She must have certainty of discharge.
B) The semen must exit from the inner private part to the outer private part.
C) She must see water clearly with her eyes.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi muftā bihī for ghusl after a wet dream requires either clear sight of water or actual exit of semen from the inner private part; mere feeling or certainty is insufficient.

Ghusl for Women: Post-Intercourse Semen and Jinn Encounters
Rulings on ghusl for women in specific scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on ghusl for a woman who bathes after intercourse and later experiences semen emission, and explain the ruling for a woman visited by a jinn in sleep.

Core Idea
A woman does not repeat ghusl if her husband's semen emerges after her bath, but must perform wudu; jinn visit in sleep requires ghusl only if discharge occurs.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies two common scenarios that often confuse. The first ruling addresses a woman who has performed ghusl after intercourse and later finds her husband's semen exiting; she does not need to repeat ghusl, only wudu. The second ruling deals with a woman visited by a jinn in her sleep, explaining when ghusl becomes obligatory, such as when she sees water or if the jinn appears in human form and insertion occurs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine whether the case involves a woman after intercourse with a human or a jinn encounter in sleep.
The two scenarios have distinct rulings.
2
Extract the ruling for the human scenario
The text states that if a woman bathes after intercourse and later the man's semen comes out, she does not need ghusl. She only needs wudu as al-Ramli adds.
This is a concession based on the principle that ghusl is not repeated for residual traces.
3
Extract the ruling for the jinn scenario
For a woman visited by a jinn in sleep, ghusl is not obligatory unless she discharges or sees water. If the jinn appears in human form and insertion occurs, ghusl becomes wajib.
The key is actual discharge or clear evidence of emission, not mere dreaming.
4
Apply the rulings
Test your understanding by applying these rulings to similar cases, such as a woman who bathes and later finds her own emission or a woman who dreams of a jinn without seeing water.

إلا إذا لم يظهر لها في صورة الآدمي. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : إذا استيقظ فوجد بللاً في احليله وشك في أنه مني أو مذي فعليه الغسل إلا إذا كان ذكره منتشراً قبل النوم فلا يلزمه الغسل إلا أن يكون أكبر رأيه أنه مني فيلزمه الغسل، وهذه المسألة يكثر وقوعها والناس عنها غافلون، وهذه تقيد الخلاف المتقدم بين أبي يوسف وصاحبيه بما إذا لم يكن ذكره منتشراً. ثم إن أبا حنيفة في هذه المسألة ومسألة المباشرة الفاحشة ومسألة الفأرة المنتفخة أخذ بالاحتياط يوسف وافقه في الاحتياط في مسألة المباشرة الفاحشة لوجود فعل هو سبب خروج المذي وخالفه في الفصلين الأخيرين لانعدام الفعل منه ومحمداً وافقه في الاحتياط في مسألة النائم نفسه فكان عنده موضع الاحتياط بخلاف الفصلين الأخيرين فإن المباشر ليس بغافل عن نفسه فيحس بما يخرج منه كذا في المبسوط . وفي المحيط : ولو أن رجلاً عزباً به فرط شهوة له أن يستمني بعلاج لتسكن شهوته ولا يكون مأجوراً عليه ليته ينجو رأساً برأس . هكذا روي عن أبي حنيفة. وفي الخلاصة معزياً إلى الأصل: المراهق لا يجب عليه الغسل لكن يمنع من الصلاة حتى يغتسل، وكذا لو أراد الصلاة بدون الوضوء وكذا المراهقة وفي القنية : لو أنزل الصبي مع الدفق وكان سبب بلوغه فالظاهر أنه لا يلزمه الغسل ا هـ. قال بعض المتأخرين ولا يخفى أنه على هذا لا بد من توجيه المتون ولم يذكر توجيهاً. وقد يقال : أن غير المكلف مخصوص من إطلاق عباراتهم ، فقولهم وموجبه إنزال مني» معناه أن إنزال المني موجب للغسل على المكلف لا على غيره وسيأتي خلاف هذا في آخر بحث الغسل إن شاء الله تعالى. واعلم أنه كما ينتقض الوضوء بنزول البول إلى القلفة يجب الغسل بوصول المني إليها ذكره في البدائع .
His statement: (She performed ghusl then the man's semen came out of her, there is no ghusl upon her.) al-Ramli said: I say that wudu is required upon her, as in al-Tatarikhaniyya, transmitted from Majmuʿ al-Nawazil. His statement: (And it may be said that ghusl should be obligatory without discharge due to the presence of insertion) — it is not hidden that this is not appropriate, because the discussion is about when he comes to her in sleep, and in this situation if she saw that he had intercourse with her a hundred times, ghusl is not obligatory unless she discharges. Yes, if she were to see him in a wakeful state, his statement would apply, and it is as if he forgot the restriction to sleep; otherwise it has no basis as you know. Then I saw al-Shaykh Ismail recorded his statement in the day; he stated it clearly. Except if it does not appear to her in human form. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: If he wakes up and finds wetness in his penis and doubts whether it is semen or pre-semen, then ghusl is required upon him unless his penis was erect before sleep, then ghusl is not required unless his strongest opinion is that it is semen, then ghusl is required. This issue frequently occurs and people are neglectful of it. This qualifies the earlier difference between Abu Yusuf and his two companions (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) to when his penis was not erect. Then Abu Hanifa in this issue, the issue of shameless touching (mubashara fahisha), and the issue of the swollen mouse, adopted precaution. Abu Yusuf agreed with him in precaution in the issue of shameless touching because there is an action that is a cause of pre-semen emission, but differed in the other two chapters due to the absence of action from him. Muhammad agreed with him in precaution in the issue of the sleeping person himself, so in his view precaution applied, unlike the other two chapters, because the one who touches is not heedless of himself and feels what comes out of him. This is in al-Mabsut. And in al-Muhit: A bachelor who has excessive desire may perform masturbation (istimna) by treatment to calm his desire, and he will not be rewarded for it; may he escape head to head. Thus it is reported from Abu Hanifa. And in al-Khulasa, attributed to al-Asl: The adolescent (murahiq) does not have to perform ghusl, but he is prevented from prayer until he performs ghusl, and similarly if he wants to pray without wudu, and similarly the female adolescent. And in al-Qunyah: If a boy ejaculates with dafq and that was the cause of his puberty, it appears that ghusl is not required of him. End quote. Some later scholars said: It is not hidden that in this case the texts must be explained, but he did not provide an explanation. And it may be said that the non-obligated is excluded from the absolute import of their expressions. So their statement 'its requirement is the emission of semen' means that the emission of semen necessitates ghusl upon the obligated, not upon others. This will be discussed later at the end of the chapter on ghusl, God willing. And know that just as wudu is invalidated by the descent of urine to the foreskin, ghusl is required by the arrival of semen to it. This is mentioned in al-Bada'iʿ.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a series of ruling statements on ghusl for women (and some related rulings for men). The first ruling: a woman who has intercourse, performs ghusl, and later the man's semen comes out of her does not need to repeat ghusl, but she must perform wudu according to Ramli. The second: the case of a woman visited by a jinn in sleep — she does not need ghusl unless she actually discharges or sees water. The author criticizes the view that ghusl should be obligatory due to insertion, clarifying that the scenario is in sleep, where ghusl is not required without discharge. The jinn encounter is then detailed: if the jinn appears in human form and insertion occurs, ghusl becomes wajib. The passage then shifts to Fatawa Qadikhan's ruling on a man who finds wetness and doubts: he must perform ghusl unless his penis was erect before sleep, in which case he is not required unless his strongest opinion says it is semen. The author then discusses the ihtiyat (precaution) positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad in three cases: the sleeping person (this doubt case), shameless touching (mubashara fahisha), and the swollen mouse. Abu Hanifa took precaution in all three; Abu Yusuf agreed in the touching case but not the others; Muhammad agreed only in the sleeping case. The bachelor's masturbation ruling is given from Abu Hanifa: it is permissible but not rewarded. The adolescent's ghusl is not required but he is prevented from prayer until he does it. Finally, a rule is stated: just as wudu is nullified by urine reaching the foreskin, ghusl becomes required upon arrival of semen there.

Key Terms
الاستمناء (al-istimnāʾ): Masturbation by manual or other stimulation to calm excessive sexual desire.
المراهق (al-murāhiq): An adolescent who has not yet officially reached puberty (usually by wet dream or age 15).
المباشرة الفاحشة (al-mubāshara al-fāḥisha): Shameless touching between spouses, e.g., direct skin-to-skin contact of genitals without intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a woman who performs ghusl after intercourse and later finds her husband's semen exiting?
A) She must repeat ghusl.
B) She needs only wudu.
C) She does not need anything; it is pure.
D) She must repeat ghusl and wudu.

Key Takeaway
Residual semen after ghusl does not require a new ghusl, only wudu; jinn encounters require ghusl only upon discharge or when the jinn appears in human form with insertion.

Ghusl Obligation on Doubt Upon Waking and Intra-Hanafi Ihtiyat
Ruling on doubt upon waking and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on precaution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl when a man wakes up with wetness and doubts its nature, and explain the ihtiyat (precaution) positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on this and related issues.

Core Idea
If a man wakes up with wetness and doubts if it is semen, ghusl is wajib unless his penis was erect before sleep; Abu Hanifa takes precaution in three cases, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad vary.

This passage from Fatawa Qadikhan and Al-Mabsut deals with a frequent situation: a man wakes up with wetness and is unsure if it is semen (maniy) or pre-semen (madhi). The ruling depends on whether his penis was erect before sleep. The passage further discusses the ihtiyat (precaution) approach of the three main Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, in three distinct cases. Understanding this ikhtilaf helps a mufti decide which ruling to apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The man wakes up and finds wetness on his penis. He does not remember a dream and doubts whether it is semen or pre-semen.
2
Apply the primary ruling
If his penis was not erect before sleep, ghusl is obligatory. If it was erect, ghusl is not required unless his strongest opinion is that it is semen.
The erect penis before sleep suggests the wetness might be pre-semen due to arousal, not an actual discharge.
3
Understand the ihtiyat positions
Abu Hanifa took precaution in three cases: this sleeping doubt case, shameless touching (mubashara fahisha), and the 'swollen mouse' case. Abu Yusuf agreed only in the touching case; Muhammad agreed only in the sleeping doubt case.
Precaution means requiring ghusl to avoid missing an obligatory act.
4
Apply the ihtiyat logic
The difference lies in whether the person has an action that could cause emission. In shameless touching, there is an action; in the sleeping case, the sleeper is unaware; in the mouse case, it's a doubtful object causing wetness.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
