إلا إذا لم يظهر لها في صورة الآدمي. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان : إذا استيقظ فوجد بللاً في احليله وشك في أنه مني أو مذي فعليه الغسل إلا إذا كان ذكره منتشراً قبل النوم فلا يلزمه الغسل إلا أن يكون أكبر رأيه أنه مني فيلزمه الغسل، وهذه المسألة يكثر وقوعها والناس عنها غافلون، وهذه تقيد الخلاف المتقدم بين أبي يوسف وصاحبيه بما إذا لم يكن ذكره منتشراً. ثم إن أبا حنيفة في هذه المسألة ومسألة المباشرة الفاحشة ومسألة الفأرة المنتفخة أخذ بالاحتياط يوسف وافقه في الاحتياط في مسألة المباشرة الفاحشة لوجود فعل هو سبب خروج المذي وخالفه في الفصلين الأخيرين لانعدام الفعل منه ومحمداً وافقه في الاحتياط في مسألة النائم نفسه فكان عنده موضع الاحتياط بخلاف الفصلين الأخيرين فإن المباشر ليس بغافل عن نفسه فيحس بما يخرج منه كذا في المبسوط . وفي المحيط : ولو أن رجلاً عزباً به فرط شهوة له أن يستمني بعلاج لتسكن شهوته ولا يكون مأجوراً عليه ليته ينجو رأساً برأس . هكذا روي عن أبي حنيفة. وفي الخلاصة معزياً إلى الأصل: المراهق لا يجب عليه الغسل لكن يمنع من الصلاة حتى يغتسل، وكذا لو أراد الصلاة بدون الوضوء وكذا المراهقة وفي القنية : لو أنزل الصبي مع الدفق وكان سبب بلوغه فالظاهر أنه لا يلزمه الغسل ا هـ. قال بعض المتأخرين ولا يخفى أنه على هذا لا بد من توجيه المتون ولم يذكر توجيهاً. وقد يقال : أن غير المكلف مخصوص من إطلاق عباراتهم ، فقولهم وموجبه إنزال مني» معناه أن إنزال المني موجب للغسل على المكلف لا على غيره وسيأتي خلاف هذا في آخر بحث الغسل إن شاء الله تعالى. واعلم أنه كما ينتقض الوضوء بنزول البول إلى القلفة يجب الغسل بوصول المني إليها ذكره في البدائع .
His statement: (She performed ghusl then the man's semen came out of her, there is no ghusl upon her.) al-Ramli said: I say that wudu is required upon her, as in al-Tatarikhaniyya, transmitted from Majmuʿ al-Nawazil. His statement: (And it may be said that ghusl should be obligatory without discharge due to the presence of insertion) — it is not hidden that this is not appropriate, because the discussion is about when he comes to her in sleep, and in this situation if she saw that he had intercourse with her a hundred times, ghusl is not obligatory unless she discharges. Yes, if she were to see him in a wakeful state, his statement would apply, and it is as if he forgot the restriction to sleep; otherwise it has no basis as you know. Then I saw al-Shaykh Ismail recorded his statement in the day; he stated it clearly. Except if it does not appear to her in human form. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: If he wakes up and finds wetness in his penis and doubts whether it is semen or pre-semen, then ghusl is required upon him unless his penis was erect before sleep, then ghusl is not required unless his strongest opinion is that it is semen, then ghusl is required. This issue frequently occurs and people are neglectful of it. This qualifies the earlier difference between Abu Yusuf and his two companions (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) to when his penis was not erect. Then Abu Hanifa in this issue, the issue of shameless touching (mubashara fahisha), and the issue of the swollen mouse, adopted precaution. Abu Yusuf agreed with him in precaution in the issue of shameless touching because there is an action that is a cause of pre-semen emission, but differed in the other two chapters due to the absence of action from him. Muhammad agreed with him in precaution in the issue of the sleeping person himself, so in his view precaution applied, unlike the other two chapters, because the one who touches is not heedless of himself and feels what comes out of him. This is in al-Mabsut. And in al-Muhit: A bachelor who has excessive desire may perform masturbation (istimna) by treatment to calm his desire, and he will not be rewarded for it; may he escape head to head. Thus it is reported from Abu Hanifa. And in al-Khulasa, attributed to al-Asl: The adolescent (murahiq) does not have to perform ghusl, but he is prevented from prayer until he performs ghusl, and similarly if he wants to pray without wudu, and similarly the female adolescent. And in al-Qunyah: If a boy ejaculates with dafq and that was the cause of his puberty, it appears that ghusl is not required of him. End quote. Some later scholars said: It is not hidden that in this case the texts must be explained, but he did not provide an explanation. And it may be said that the non-obligated is excluded from the absolute import of their expressions. So their statement 'its requirement is the emission of semen' means that the emission of semen necessitates ghusl upon the obligated, not upon others. This will be discussed later at the end of the chapter on ghusl, God willing. And know that just as wudu is invalidated by the descent of urine to the foreskin, ghusl is required by the arrival of semen to it. This is mentioned in al-Bada'iʿ.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a series of ruling statements on ghusl for women (and some related rulings for men). The first ruling: a woman who has intercourse, performs ghusl, and later the man's semen comes out of her does not need to repeat ghusl, but she must perform wudu according to Ramli. The second: the case of a woman visited by a jinn in sleep — she does not need ghusl unless she actually discharges or sees water. The author criticizes the view that ghusl should be obligatory due to insertion, clarifying that the scenario is in sleep, where ghusl is not required without discharge. The jinn encounter is then detailed: if the jinn appears in human form and insertion occurs, ghusl becomes wajib. The passage then shifts to Fatawa Qadikhan's ruling on a man who finds wetness and doubts: he must perform ghusl unless his penis was erect before sleep, in which case he is not required unless his strongest opinion says it is semen. The author then discusses the ihtiyat (precaution) positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad in three cases: the sleeping person (this doubt case), shameless touching (mubashara fahisha), and the swollen mouse. Abu Hanifa took precaution in all three; Abu Yusuf agreed in the touching case but not the others; Muhammad agreed only in the sleeping case. The bachelor's masturbation ruling is given from Abu Hanifa: it is permissible but not rewarded. The adolescent's ghusl is not required but he is prevented from prayer until he does it. Finally, a rule is stated: just as wudu is nullified by urine reaching the foreskin, ghusl becomes required upon arrival of semen there.

Key Terms
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyāt): Legal precaution; choosing the strictest ruling when in doubt to ensure the act is valid.
المذي (al-madhī): Pre-semen, a thin fluid that emits due to sexual arousal, not necessarily with orgasm.
المني (al-manī): Semen, emitted with lust and gush; requires ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Fatawa Qadikhan, if a man wakes up with wetness and his penis was erect before sleep, when must he perform ghusl?
A) Always.
B) Only if his strongest opinion is that it is semen.
C) Never.
D) Only if he remembered a dream.

Key Takeaway
In doubt upon waking, ghusl is wajib unless the penis was erect before sleep; Abu Hanifa's ihtiyat extends this to other cases, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ based on the presence of action.

Masturbation for a Bachelor and Ghusl for Adolescents
Rulings on masturbation, adolescent's ghusl, and foreskin rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on masturbation for a bachelor with excessive desire, explain the ruling on ghusl for an adolescent (murahiq), and apply the rule that ghusl is required when semen reaches the foreskin.

Core Idea
A bachelor with excessive desire may masturbate to avoid sin but is not rewarded; an adolescent does not have to perform ghusl but is prevented from prayer until doing so; semen reaching the foreskin necessitates ghusl.

This passage addresses three additional rulings: (1) masturbation for a bachelor who has overwhelming sexual desire — it is permissible but not rewarded; (2) the adolescent (murahiq) who emits semen — he does not owe ghusl as an obligation, but he is prevented from praying until he purifies himself; (3) a general rule that just as urine reaching the foreskin invalidates wudu, semen reaching the same point requires ghusl.

Guided Path
1
Understand the masturbation ruling
For a bachelor who has excessive desire and fears sin, masturbation is permissible as a last resort, but it is a 'head-to-head' escape — no reward, just avoiding harm.
This is a concession (rukhsa) for necessity.
2
Understand the adolescent ruling
An adolescent (male or female) who emits semen (maniy) is not obligated to perform ghusl as a religious duty, but if they want to pray, they must purify themselves (ghusl or wudu).
The adolescent is not fully obligated (mukallaf), but prayer requires taharah.
3
Apply the foreskin rule
Just as wudu is invalidated when urine reaches the foreskin (the tip of the penis), ghusl becomes obligatory when semen reaches that point, even if not fully emitted.
This establishes a threshold for ghusl based on contact with the private part.
4
Synthesize the three rulings
Each ruling addresses a different aspect of taharah: permissibility of a means to prevent sin, the status of a minor's ghusl, and the boundary for when ghusl becomes required.

Waking Up with Wetness: Doubt Between Mani and Madhi
Ruling on ghusl with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl when doubt exists after waking with wetness, apply the exception for erect penis, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on ihtiyat.

Core Idea
When doubt arises between mani and madhi, ghusl is wajib unless the penis was erect before sleep — then no ghusl unless dominant opinion says mani.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: waking up to find wetness but not knowing whether it is mani (requiring ghusl) or madhi (requiring only wudu). The Hanafi school gives a detailed ruling that balances caution (ihtiyat) with evidence. We will unpack the main rule, its exception, and the subtle intra-madhhab differences among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its exception
Read the first sentence of the source: the default ruling is that ghusl is required. Note the exception: if the penis was erect before sleep, then no ghusl unless the dominant opinion (aghlab al-rajāʾ) says it is mani.
The phrase 'dominant opinion' is a juristic standard, not mere speculation.
2
Understand the criterion for doubt
The presence or absence of an erection before sleep is the key indicator. An erect penis suggests the wetness is more likely madhi (pre-ejaculatory fluid), while no erection leaves doubt that it could be mani.
This criterion is derived from the nature of these fluids, not from direct textual evidence.
3
Recognize the role of dominant opinion in the exception
Even if the penis was erect, if the person's dominant opinion is that the wetness is mani (e.g., he had a vivid sexual dream), then ghusl becomes wajib. This shows that caution (ihtiyat) still applies when the evidence suggests mani.
Dominant opinion is a personal judgment based on external signs.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on ihtiyat
The source explains that Abu Hanifa applied caution in three cases: this sleeping case, overt fondling, and a dead mouse found in water. Abu Yusuf agreed only in the fondling case; Muhammad agreed only in the sleeping case. Analyze why each imam differed.
The dispute centers on whether caution should be applied when the person is not aware of the fluid's emission.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling to real-life situations
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the first ruling given: ghusl is wajib in the sleeping case unless the penis was erect. If erect, no ghusl unless dominant opinion says mani. Apply this to various scenarios.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa; the ikhtilaf is noted but not acted upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا استيقظ فوجد بللاً في احليله وشك في أنه مني أو مذي فعليه الغسل إلا إذا كان ذكره منتشراً قبل النوم فلا يلزمه الغسل إلا أن يكون أكبر رأيه أنه مني فيلزمه الغسل، وهذه المسألة يكثر وقوعها والناس عنها غافلون، وهذه تقيد الخلاف المتقدم بين أبي يوسف وصاحبيه بما إذا لم يكن ذكره منتشراً. ثم إن أبا حنيفة في هذه المسألة ومسألة المباشرة الفاحشة ومسألة الفأرة المنتفخة أخذ بالاحتياط يوسف وافقه في الاحتياط في مسألة المباشرة الفاحشة لوجود فعل هو سبب خروج المذي وخالفه في الفصلين الأخيرين لانعدام الفعل منه ومحمداً وافقه في الاحتياط في مسألة النائم نفسه فكان عنده موضع الاحتياط بخلاف الفصلين الأخيرين فإن المباشر ليس بغافل عن نفسه فيحس بما يخرج منه كذا في المبسوط .
If he wakes up and finds wetness in his urethra and doubts whether it is mani or madhi, then ghusl is required for him, unless his penis was erect before sleep, then ghusl is not required unless his dominant opinion is that it is mani, in which case ghusl is required. This case occurs frequently and people are negligent about it. This restricts the previous disagreement between Abu Yusuf and his two companions (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) to the case where his penis was not erect. Then, Abu Hanifa in this case and the case of overtly lewd fondling and the case of the swollen mouse adopted caution. Abu Yusuf agreed with him in caution in the case of overtly lewd fondling because there is an action that is the cause of madhi coming out, but disagreed with him in the last two cases because of the absence of action on his part. Muhammad agreed with him in caution in the case of the sleeping person himself, so caution was applicable in his view, unlike the last two cases because the fondler is not unaware of himself and feels what comes out of him. This is in al-Mabsut.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling when a person wakes up and finds wetness but is unsure whether it is mani (semen, requiring ghusl) or madhi (pre-ejaculatory fluid, requiring only wudu). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is given in the first sentence: ghusl is required unless he knows his penis was erect before sleep, which suggests the fluid is likely madhi, unless he strongly thinks it is mani. The passage then explains how this ruling qualifies the earlier disagreement among the three imams. Abu Hanifa took a cautious approach in three cases: this wet dream case, overt lewd fondling (direct contact without intercourse), and the case of finding a dead swollen mouse in water. Abu Yusuf agreed in the fondling case because there was an action likely causing madhi, but disagreed in the other two because no action occurred. Muhammad agreed only in the sleeping person case because the person is unaware, thus caution applies. The passage emphasizes the practical importance of this ruling.

Key Terms
مني (mani): Semen which requires ghusl
مذي (madhi): Pre-ejaculatory fluid which requires wudu only
احتياط (ihtiyat): Legal caution, preferring the more restrictive ruling in cases of doubt

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person wakes up to find wetness and his penis was erect before sleep, what is the ruling?
A) Ghusl is always required.
B) No ghusl is required unless his dominant opinion is that it is mani.
C) Only wudu is required.
D) Ghusl is required only if he had a sexual dream.

Key Takeaway
When waking up with wetness and doubt, ghusl is wajib unless the penis was erect before sleep — then no ghusl unless dominant opinion says mani.

Masturbation for a Bachelor: When Necessity Permits
Ruling on masturbation to calm sexual desire for a bachelor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on masturbation for a bachelor with excessive desire and explain the basis of permissibility and the reward status.

Core Idea
Masturbation for a bachelor fearing zina is permissible but earns no reward; it is a mere escape from sin.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Imam Abu Hanifa on masturbation (istimna') for an unmarried man who cannot control his sexual urge. The passage, from al-Muhit, presents a clear permission with a notable absence of reward. Understanding this ruling requires appreciating the Hanafi principle of averting greater harm (zina) through a lesser permissible act, even if that act carries no spiritual merit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and condition
The passage specifies a 'bachelor' (a'zab) who has 'excessive sexual desire' (fart shahwa). This condition is key: the ruling applies only when desire is overwhelming and cannot be otherwise satisfied lawfully.
The term 'bachelor' implies no spouse or lawful means to satisfy desire.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The text says 'he may masturbate' (lahu an yastamni) — this is a permission (ibaha) to use a means (ilaj) to calm his desire. The act is permissible (mubah) under this specific condition.
The permission is conditional on necessity to avoid zina.
3
Note the absence of reward
The passage explicitly states 'he will not be rewarded for it' (wa la yakunu ma'juran 'alayh). The phrase 'head to head' (ra'san bi ra's) means he escapes sin without earning reward — a neutral act.
This distinguishes it from recommended acts; it is merely a lawful escape from sin.
4
Recognize the source authority
The ruling is attributed to Abu Hanifa via a narration (haka dha ruwiya 'an Abi Hanifa). This gives it weight as part of the madhhab's transmitted positions.
Later Hanafi scholars specify this applies only when there is genuine fear of zina.
5
Understand the legal basis
The underlying principle is darurah (necessity): preventing a greater harm (zina) justifies a normally discouraged act. Without necessity, masturbation becomes haram in the Hanafi school.
This aligns with the maxim: 'Necessity permits prohibited things' (al-darurat tubih al-mahzurat), but here the act is not originally prohibited, only discouraged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : ولو أن رجلاً عزباً به فرط شهوة له أن يستمني بعلاج لتسكن شهوته ولا يكون مأجوراً عليه ليته ينجو رأساً برأس . هكذا روي عن أبي حنيفة.
And in al-Muhit: If a bachelor has excessive sexual desire, he may masturbate with a means to calm his desire, and he will not be rewarded for it; it is as if he escapes head to head. Thus it is narrated from Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from Imam Abu Hanifa on masturbation for a bachelor who cannot control his desire. The ruling: it is permissible (ja'iz) to masturbate by some means (e.g., using the hand) to calm his desire, but he is not rewarded for this act. The phrase 'head to head' means he just barely escapes sin without earning reward. The ruling is based on necessity (darurah) to avoid the greater sin of zina. Later scholars have differentiated: if done to prevent zina, it is mubah; if done purely for pleasure, it is haram. The text does not discuss the reward aspect further, but notes that this is a transmitted narration from Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
استمناء (istimna'): Masturbation, specifically performed by hand or other means
عزب (a'zab): Unmarried person (bachelor)
فرط شهوة (fart shahwa): Excessive sexual desire that overwhelms a person

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is forbidden and a major sin.
B) It is permissible but he is not rewarded.
C) It is recommended and rewarded.
D) It is permissible and rewarded if he fears zina.

Key Takeaway
Masturbation is permissible for a bachelor when necessary to avoid zina, but it carries no reward; it is a neutral act of escape from sin.

Ghusl Obligation for a Minor after Ejaculation
Ruling on ghusl for a minor who ejaculates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl for a minor who ejaculates and explain why it is not obligatory.

Core Idea
Ghusl is not wajib on a minor, but salah requires taharah

The passage addresses a common scenario: a minor who experiences ejaculation. Although emission of mani is normally a cause for obligatory ghusl, the Hanafi school distinguishes between the ruling for a legally responsible adult (mukallaf) and a minor (murahiq). Understanding this distinction helps clarify the role of taklif (legal responsibility) in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person and the event
The subject is a murahiq (adolescent minor who has not yet reached puberty). The event is ejaculation (inzal al-mani).
2
Determine the hukm (ruling)
The passage clearly states: al-murahiq la yajibu 'alayhi al-ghusl – ghusl is not obligatory on the minor.
This is the Hanafi position.
3
Note the practical consequence
Despite not being wajib, the minor is prevented from praying (yumna' min al-salah) until he performs ghusl. This is for purity and training.
The same applies to wudu for a minor female (murahiqah).
4
Understand the rationale
The ruling is based on the principle that the minor is not mukallaf (legally responsible). The general texts ordering ghusl for mani are restricted to those who are mukallaf.
As stated later in the passage: 'non-obligated person is excluded from the absolute nature of their statements.'
5
Apply to similar cases
If ejaculation occurs and it is the cause of puberty (i.e., the boy becomes an adult by that emission), still ghusl is not required according to the passage from al-Qunyah, because the act happened before puberty.
This shows the delicate boundary of taklif.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخلاصة معزياً إلى الأصل: المراهق لا يجب عليه الغسل لكن يمنع من الصلاة حتى يغتسل، وكذا لو أراد الصلاة بدون الوضوء وكذا المراهقة وفي القنية : لو أنزل الصبي مع الدفق وكان سبب بلوغه فالظاهر أنه لا يلزمه الغسل ا هـ. قال بعض المتأخرين ولا يخفى أنه على هذا لا بد من توجيه المتون ولم يذكر توجيهاً. وقد يقال : أن غير المكلف مخصوص من إطلاق عباراتهم ، فقولهم وموجبه إنزال مني» معناه أن إنزال المني موجب للغسل على المكلف لا على غيره وسيأتي خلاف هذا في آخر بحث الغسل إن شاء الله تعالى.
And in al-Khulasah, attributed to al-Asl: The adolescent minor (murahiq) is not obligated to perform ghusl, but he is prevented from praying until he does ghusl. Similarly, if he wants to pray without wudu, and likewise for a female adolescent. And in al-Qunyah: If a boy ejaculates with force and it is the cause of his puberty, apparently ghusl is not required for him. End quote. Some later scholars said: It is not hidden that according to this, it is necessary to interpret the texts (al-mutun) and he did not mention an interpretation. And it may be said: The non-obligated person is excluded from the absolute nature of their statements. So their saying 'and its cause is the emission of mani' means that emission of mani obligates ghusl for the obligated person, not for others. And there will come a disagreement about this at the end of the discussion of ghusl, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on ghusl for a minor (pre-pubescent) who experiences ejaculation. The primary ruling: ghusl is not wajib on the minor because he is not yet mukallaf (legally responsible). However, he is prevented from performing salah until he does ghusl, as a means of teaching and to avoid impurity. The same applies to a minor female. The text then cites a narration from al-Qunyah: if a boy ejaculates with force and that marks his puberty, still ghusl is not required. Later scholars comment that the general texts about ghusl being obligatory due to emission of mani are restricted to those who are legally responsible. The author notes that there will be a later discussion on this point at the end of the chapter on ghusl.

Key Terms
مراهق (murahiq): An adolescent minor approaching puberty but not yet legally responsible
مكلف (mukallaf): Legally responsible person, i.e., adult and sane
وجوب (wujub): Legal obligation; omission entails sin

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a minor (murahiq) who ejaculates?
A) Ghusl is obligatory on him.
B) Ghusl is not obligatory, but he is prevented from praying until he does ghusl.
C) He is exempt from all purification requirements.
D) He must only wash his clothes.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl is not wajib on a minor who ejaculates due to lack of legal responsibility, but it remains necessary for prayer.

Ghusl Required When Mani Reaches the Prepuce
Analogical ruling extending interior boundary from wudu to ghusl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when ghusl becomes obligatory due to mani reaching the prepuce and explain the analogical reasoning (qiyas) that supports it.

Core Idea
Ghusl is wajib when mani reaches the prepuce, just as wudu breaks when urine does.

This brief passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq establishes a clear analogy between wudu and ghusl concerning the inner skin. Understanding this ruling helps clarify the Hanafi position on the boundaries of ritual purity and the role of the prepuce as an interior boundary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
The passage states two rulings: (1) wudu is invalidated when urine reaches the prepuce; (2) ghusl becomes obligatory when mani reaches the prepuce. Note that both involve the prepuce as a critical boundary.
The prepuce (qulfah) is the fold of skin covering the glans; in Hanafi fiqh, it is considered part of the interior.
2
Recognize the analogy (qiyas)
The ruling on ghusl is derived by analogy from the ruling on wudu. The original case (asl) is urine reaching the prepuce nullifying wudu; the analogous case (far') is mani reaching the prepuce obligating ghusl.
Qiyas jaliy: the illa is that both are impurities entering an internal area.
3
Determine the effective cause (illa)
The illa is the arrival of an impurity (najis) to a part of the body that is considered interior. Both urine and mani are impure, and the prepuce is deemed part of the interior, so the same principle applies.
This illa is explicit in the analogy: 'just as ... so ...'.
4
Apply the ruling to the far'
Consequently, if mani reaches the prepuce – even if it does not exit the body – ghusl becomes wajib. This extends the ruling beyond the common understanding that emission must be complete.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
5
Note the source authority
The passage cites al-Bada'i' by Imam al-Kasani, a major Hanafi reference. This indicates the ruling is well-established within the school.
Al-Bada'i' is a commentary on al-Quduri, part of the later Hanafi tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنه كما ينتقض الوضوء بنزول البول إلى القلفة يجب الغسل بوصول المني إليها ذكره في البدائع . اهـ.
Know that just as wudu is invalidated by the arrival of urine to the prepuce, so ghusl becomes obligatory by the arrival of mani to it. This is mentioned in al-Bada'i'. End.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This is a brief ruling drawing an analogy between wudu and ghusl regarding the prepuce (the skin covering the glans in uncircumcised men). In the Hanafi school, if urine reaches the area of the prepuce (but does not exit), wudu is invalidated because the prepuce is considered part of the interior. Similarly, if mani reaches the prepuce without exiting (e.g., due to a wet dream where emission stops before exiting), ghusl becomes obligatory. This is based on qiyas: just as urine reaching the prepuce nullifies wudu, mani reaching it necessitates ghusl. The ruling is cited from al-Bada'i' by al-Kasani.

Key Terms
قلفة (qulfah): Prepuce, the fold of skin covering the glans of the penis

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does ghusl become obligatory?
A) When mani exits the body completely.
B) When mani reaches the prepuce.
C) Only if there is sexual intercourse.
D) When urine reaches the prepuce.

Key Takeaway
Mani reaching the prepuce triggers the obligation of ghusl, based on qiyas to the nullification of wudu by urine.

Ghusl Upon Intercourse with a Jinn in Human Form
Ruling on ghusl when a jinn appears in human form

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl for intercourse with a jinn in human form and explain the qiyas khafi used to derive it.

Core Idea
Ghusl is required upon insertion with a jinn in human form due to formal similarity; otherwise, it requires ejaculation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explores a unique boundary case: intercourse with a jinn that appears human. The Hanafi ruling hinges on the concept of formal similitude (mujanasah suriyyah) and the strength of the cause (sabab). We will trace the qiyas argument and the counterargument based on meaningful difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The passage considers two cases: a jinn appearing as a man to a human woman, and a female jinn appearing as a woman to a human man.
2
State the Ruling
If the jinn appears in human form, ghusl is required upon mere insertion of the glans (ghaybah al-hashafah).
Ruling: ghusl wajib.
3
Analyze the Qiyas
The ruling is analogized (qiyas) to human-human intercourse: the formal similarity (mujanasah suriyyah) establishes the cause (sabab) that obligates ghusl.
This is qiyas khafi: the common attribute is form, not essence.
4
Examine the Objection
Some argue that the meaningful difference (mubayanah ma'nawiyyah) between jinn and humans (e.g., prohibition of marriage) breaks the analogy, so ghusl should require ejaculation as with animals or corpses.
This counteranalogy uses the same qiyas method but with a different effective cause.
5
Resolve the Dispute
The commentator concludes that if the person is unaware of the jinn's true nature, ghusl is required upon insertion because the cause is complete; if aware, the deficiency in cause might limit it to ejaculation, but the relied-upon position is the former.
The 'mufta bihi' is that ghusl is required upon mere insertion when in human form.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالياء المثناة التحتية قوله : (إلا) إذا لم يظهر لها في صورة (الآدمي أقول: هذا التقييد مأخوذ من شرح المنية لابن أمير حاج الحلبي فإنه قال : ينبغي أن يكون هذا إذا لم يظهر لها في صورة آدمي، أما إذا ظهر لها في صورة رجل من بني آدم فإنه يجب عليها الغسل بمجرد إيلاج قدر الحشفة من ذكره، وكذا إذا ظهر للرجل من الإنس جنية في صورة آدمية فوطئها فإنه يجب عليه الغسل بمجرد إيلاج حشفته فيها إلحاقاً له بإيلاج آدمي لآدمية لوجود المجانسة الصورية إلا أن يقال : إنما يتم هذا لو لم يوجد بينهما مباينة معنوية وهي محققة ومن ثم علل به بعضهم حرمة التناكح بينهما فينبغي حينئذ أن لا يجب إلا بالإنزال كما في وطء البهيمة والميتة. ثم أورد وأجاب ثم قال: نعم لو ظهر لها في صورة آدمي فوطئها غير عالمة بأنه جني أو ظهرت له جنية كذلك فوطئها كذلك علما بما كان في نفس الأمر وجب الغسل عليهما فيما يظهر لانتفاء ما يفيد قصور السببية. قوله : (إلا إذا كان ذكره منتشراً قبل النوم الخ) قيد في المنية عدم وجوب الغسل في هذه الصورة بما إذا نام قائماً أو قاعداً، أما إذا نام مضطجعاً فعليه الغسل وعزاه إلى المحيط والذخيرة. ثم
With the dotted 'ya' (the letter ya with two dots below), his statement: (Unless) when it does not appear to her in the form of a human. I say: This restriction is taken from Sharh al-Munyah by Ibn Amir Haj al-Halabi, for he said: It should be that this is when it does not appear to her in the form of a human. But if it appears to her in the form of a man from the sons of Adam, then ghusl is required for her merely by the insertion of the glans of his penis. Similarly, if a human man sees a female jinn in human form and has intercourse with her, then ghusl is required for him merely by the insertion of his glans into her, analogically to insertion of a human into a human due to the existence of formal similarity. However, it may be said: This would only apply if there were no meaningful difference (mubayanah ma'nawiyyah) between them, and that is established, and some have used it as the reason for the prohibition of marriage between them. Therefore, in that case ghusl should only be required with ejaculation, as in the case of intercourse with an animal or a corpse. Then he presented and answered, then said: Yes, if it appears to her in the form of a human and she has intercourse with him unaware that he is a jinn, or if a female jinn appears to him likewise and he has intercourse with her likewise, knowing the reality, ghusl is required for both in what appears to be, because there is no deficiency in the cause. His statement: (Unless his penis was erect before sleep, etc.) In al-Munyah, the ruling of no ghusl in this case is conditioned by the person sleeping standing or sitting; if he sleeps lying down, ghusl is required. He attributed this to al-Muhit and al-Dhakhirah. Then.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on ghusl when a human has intercourse with a jinn (spirit) that appears in human form. The main discussion differentiates based on whether the jinn appears in the form of a human or not. If the jinn appears in human form, then ghusl is required upon mere insertion (ghaybah al-hashafah) because of the formal similarity (mujanasah suriyyah) to intercourse between two humans. Some argue that the meaningful difference (mubayanah ma'nawiyyah) between jinn and humans prevents this analogy, and by analogy to intercourse with animals or corpses (where ghusl is required only upon ejaculation), ghusl should be limited to ejaculation. The commentator suggests that if the parties are unaware of the jinn's true nature, ghusl is required because the cause (sabab) is complete. The passage also comments on the earlier ruling about the erect penis before sleep, clarifying that the exemption from ghusl applies only if the person slept standing or sitting, but if lying down, ghusl is required. This shows the careful distinction in Hanafi fiqh regarding the causes (asbab) of ghusl.

Key Terms
جني (jinni): A jinn (spiritual being) that can appear in human form.
مجانسة صورية (mujanasah suriyyah): Formal similarity; resemblance in outward form.
مباينة معنوية (mubayanah ma'nawiyyah): Meaningful difference; essential difference in nature.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what triggers ghusl when a jinn appears in human form and intercourse occurs?
A) Only if ejaculation occurs.
B) Only if the person is unaware of the jinn's true nature.
C) Mere insertion of the glans.
D) Ghusl is never required.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl is wajib upon insertion with a jinn in human form by analogy to human-human intercourse, based on formal similarity.

Condition of Ghusl When Sleeping with Erection
Conditional ruling on ghusl when waking with erection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which ghusl is not required if a person wakes up with an erection after sleeping.

Core Idea
If a person sleeps erect but not lying down, no ghusl is required; lying down implies the need for ghusl.

This short passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq refines a ruling from al-Munyah about ghusl when a person wakes up with an erection. The default ruling (no ghusl if penis was erect before sleep) is conditioned on sleeping position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Base Ruling
The base ruling (from the matn) states that if a person's penis was erect before sleep, and upon waking it is still erect, ghusl is not required if no wetness is found.
2
Note the Condition Added
The commentator from al-Munyah adds that this exception applies only if the person slept standing or sitting; if lying down, ghusl is required.
3
Understand the Rationale
Lying down makes it more likely that an emission occurred unnoticed, so ghusl becomes precautionarily obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Therefore, in that case ghusl should only be required with ejaculation, as in the case of intercourse with an animal or a corpse. Then he presented and answered, then said: Yes, if it appears to her in the form of a human and she has intercourse with him unaware that he is a jinn, or if a female jinn appears to him likewise and he has intercourse with her likewise, knowing the reality, ghusl is required for both in what appears to be, because there is no deficiency in the cause. His statement: (Unless his penis was erect before sleep, etc.) In al-Munyah, the ruling of no ghusl in this case is conditioned by the person sleeping standing or sitting; if he sleeps lying down, ghusl is required. He attributed this to al-Muhit and al-Dhakhirah. Then.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on ghusl when a human has intercourse with a jinn (spirit) that appears in human form. The main discussion differentiates based on whether the jinn appears in the form of a human or not. If the jinn appears in human form, then ghusl is required upon mere insertion (ghaybah al-hashafah) because of the formal similarity (mujanasah suriyyah) to intercourse between two humans. Some argue that the meaningful difference (mubayanah ma'nawiyyah) between jinn and humans prevents this analogy, and by analogy to intercourse with animals or corpses (where ghusl is required only upon ejaculation), ghusl should be limited to ejaculation. The commentator suggests that if the parties are unaware of the jinn's true nature, ghusl is required because the cause (sabab) is complete. The passage also comments on the earlier ruling about the erect penis before sleep, clarifying that the exemption from ghusl applies only if the person slept standing or sitting, but if lying down, ghusl is required. This shows the careful distinction in Hanafi fiqh regarding the causes (asbab) of ghusl.

Key Terms
قائم (qa'im): Standing; sleeping in a standing position (e.g., leaning against something)
قاعد (qa'id): Sitting; sleeping in a seated position
مضطجع (mudtaji'): Lying down; reclining on one's side

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which sleeping position is ghusl NOT required if a person wakes with an erection but no wetness?
A) Lying down
B) Standing
C) Stomach
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Ghusl is not required when waking with an erection if the person slept standing or sitting; if lying down, ghusl becomes wajib as a precaution.

Ghusl Upon Insertion: Conditions and the Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Ruling on ghusl upon insertion and Hanafi restriction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl upon insertion, identify the conditions that restrict the obligation to living human females, and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i objection using istihsan and takhsis bi al-ma'na.

Core Idea
Ghusl is fard upon insertion into a living woman, but not into a beast or corpse unless ejaculation occurs.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi position on the obligation of ghusl upon sexual insertion. The author explains that the key trigger is concealment of the glans (ghaybah al-hashafah) in the vulva or anus of a living woman who is normally sexually active. The ruling is then contrasted with the Shafi'i school, which extends the obligation to any insertion based on the general hadith. We will analyze the Hanafi use of istihsan and specification of the text by meaning to limit the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position and its conditions
State the basic ruling: ghusl becomes fard upon ghaybah al-hashafah in a living human female (normal age), even without ejaculation. Note the three conditions: (1) the partner must be a living human female who is normally sexually active; (2) the orifice must be vulva or anus; (3) the glans must be fully concealed.
The text uses قيد (restricted) three times to clarify these conditions.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the general hadith 'When the two circumcised parts meet, ghusl is obligatory' applies to all cases of insertion, including beast and corpse, and does not require ejaculation.
The hadith is authentic (sahih) and its generality is explicit.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to restrict the general text. The underlying cause (illah) of ghusl is the virtual emission of semen (inzal hukmi) when desire reaches its peak. In insertion into a beast or corpse, desire does not peak, so no virtual emission occurs. Therefore, the general text is specified by rational meaning (takhsis bi al-ma'na).
This is a key principle: the cause (sabab) of janabah is real or virtual semen emission.
4
Evaluate the usul framework
The passage notes that this reasoning entails 'takhsis al-nas bi al-ma'na ibtida'an' – specifying a general text by rational meaning without another textual evidence. This is valid in Hanafi usul because the meaning is derived from the purpose (hikmah) of the legislation.
Other schools, especially Shafi'i, require a textual specifier (takhsis bi al-nas) to restrict a general text.
5
Determine the practical difference
The consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is clear: if a person inserts into a beast or corpse without ejaculation, the Hanafi school rules no ghusl, while the Shafi'i school requires ghusl. The Hanafi view is relied upon (mufta bihi).
This difference may arise in cases of bestiality or necrophilia, which are sinful acts but still have legal implications for purification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وتواري حشفة في قبل أو دبر (عليهما أي فرض الغسل عند غيبوبة ما فوق الختان وكذلك غيبوبة مقدار الحشفة من مقطوعها في قبل امرأة يجامع مثلها أو دبر على الفاعل والمفعول به وإن لم ينزل والتعبير بغيبوبة الحشفة أولى من التعبير بالتقاء الختانين لتناوله الإيلاج في الدبر، ولأن الثابت في الفرج محاذاتهما لا التقاؤهما لأن ختان الرجل هو موضع القطع وهو ما دون خرة الحشفة وختان المرأة موضع قطع جلدة منها كعرف الديك فوق الفرج وذلك لأن مدخل الذكر هو مخرج المني والولد والحيض، وفوق مدخل الذكر مخرج البول كإحليل الرجل وبينهما جلدة رقيقة يقطع منها من الختان، فحصل أن ختان المرأة متسفل تحت مخرج البول وتحت مخرج البول مدخل الذكر فإذا غابت الحشفة في الفرج فقد حاذى ختانه ولكن يقال لموضع ختان المرأة الخفاض فذكر الختانين بطريق التغليب، قيد بالتواري لأن مجرد التلاقي لا يوجب الغسل ولكن ينقض الوضوء على الخلاف المتقدم، وقيدنا بكونه في قبل امرأة لأن التواري في فرج البهيمة لا يوجب الغسل إلا بالإنزال، وقيدنا بكونها يجامع مثلها لأن التواري في الميتة والصغيرة لا يوجب الغسل إلا بالإنزال، وقد تقدم الدليل من السنة والإجماع على وجوب الغسل بالإيلاج وإن لم يكن معه إنزال وهو بعمومه يشمل الصغيرة والبهيمة وإليه ذهب الشافعي لكن أصحابنا رضي الله عنهم منعوه إلا أن ينزل لأن وصف الجنابة متوقف على خروج المني ظاهراً أو حكماً عند كمال سببه مع لقلته وتكسله في المجرى لضعف الدفق بعدم بلوغ الشهوة منتهاها كما يجده المجامع في أثناء الجماع من اللذة بمقاربة المزايلة، فيجب حينئذ إقامة السبب مقامه وهذا علة كون الإيلاج فيه الغسل فتعدى الحكم إلى الإيلاج في الدبر وعلى الملاط به إذ ربما يتلذذ فينزل، ويخفى لما قلنا. وأخرجوا ما ذكرنا لكنه يستلزم تخصيص النص بالمعنى ابتداء كذا في فتح القدير. وحاصله أن الموجب إنزال المني حقيقة أو تقديراً عند كمال سببه، وفيما ذكرناه لم يوجد حقيقة ولا تقدير النقصان سببه لكن هذا يستلزم تخصيص النص بالمعنى ابتداء والعام لا تناء خروجه
His statement: (And the concealment of the glans in the vulva or anus) means: fard (obligatory) ghusl upon the disappearance of what is above the circumcision, and likewise the disappearance of the amount of the glans from the one whose glans is cut off, in the vulva of a woman who is normally sexually active or in the anus, upon the doer and the receiver even if he did not ejaculate. The expression 'concealment of the glans' is better than 'meeting of the two circumcisions' because it includes anal insertion, and because what is established in the vagina is their alignment, not their meeting. The man's circumcision is the place of cutting which is below the corona of the glans, and the woman's circumcision is the place of cutting a piece of skin from her, like a rooster's comb above the vagina, because the entrance of the penis is the exit of semen, child, and menses, and above the entrance is the exit of urine like the man's urethra. Between them is a thin skin from which the circumcision is cut. So it turns out that the woman's circumcision is below the exit of urine, and below that is the entrance of the penis. So when the glans disappears into the vagina, it aligns with his circumcision. But the place of the woman's circumcision is called khifad, so mentioning 'circumcisions' is by way of inclusion (taghlib). He restricted it with 'concealment' because mere touching (talaqi) does not necessitate ghusl but does invalidate wudu according to the previous disagreement. And we restricted it to 'the vulva of a woman' because concealment in the vagina of a beast does not necessitate ghusl except with ejaculation. And we restricted it to 'one who is normally sexually active' because concealment in a dead woman or a young girl does not necessitate ghusl except with ejaculation. The proof from the Sunnah and Ijma' for the obligation of ghusl upon insertion even without ejaculation has already been presented, and its generality includes the young girl and beast. Imam al-Shafi'i adopted this, but our scholars (may Allah be pleased with them) prohibited applying it except with ejaculation, because the state of janabah depends on the real or virtual exit of semen when its cause is complete, due to its small amount and its sluggishness in the passage due to the weakness of the flow because the desire has not reached its peak, as the person engaged in intercourse experiences pleasure at the approach of separation. So at that point the cause (the insertion) is made to stand in the place of the effect (the virtual emission). This is the effective cause (illah) for ghusl being required upon insertion. Therefore, the ruling extends to anal insertion and to mutual fondling (al-mulat) because perhaps he may experience pleasure and ejaculate, but it is hidden due to what we said. They (the Shafi'is) adduced what we have mentioned, but this entails specifying the general text by mere meaning (takhsis al-nas bi al-ma'na ibtida'an), as in Fath al-Qadir. The summary is that the obligating factor is the real or virtual emission of semen when its cause is complete. In what we have mentioned (i.e., insertion into a beast or corpse), neither real nor virtual emission exists because the cause is incomplete. However, this entails specifying the general text by meaning from the outset, and the general is not abandoned [while it is possible to specify]. The text cuts off: 'wa al-'am la tana' khurujahu'.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This is a major passage on the obligation of ghusl upon sexual insertion. The author explains the matn: ghusl becomes fard when the glans (hashafah) is concealed in the vulva or anus of a living woman who is of age to have intercourse, even without ejaculation. The passage clarifies that mere touching (talaqi) does not require ghusl but invalidates wudu. The key Hanafi position is that ghusl is required upon insertion into a living human female, but not upon insertion into a beast, dead woman, or minor girl unless ejaculation occurs. This contrasts with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that the general hadith (e.g., 'When the two circumcised parts meet, ghusl is obligatory') applies to all cases. The Hanafi school uses istihsan: janabah (major impurity) depends on the real or virtual emission of semen. In normal intercourse, the desire reaches its peak and semen virtually exits, even if it does not come out due to sluggishness. Therefore, insertion is treated as the cause (sabab) of emission, and ghusl is required. However, with a beast or corpse, desire does not reach its peak, so no virtual emission occurs, and ghusl is only required if actual ejaculation happens. The text also explains that the ruling extends to anal intercourse and perhaps to mutual fondling (if it leads to hidden emission). The author notes that this reasoning entails specification of the general text (takhsis) by rational meaning (ma'na), which is a valid method in Hanafi usul. The passage ends with a discussion of the principle that the general text is not abandoned when specification is possible.

Key Terms
غيبوبة الحشفة (ghaybah al-hashafah): Concealment of the glans (the entire circumcised part or equivalent) inside the orifice
التقاء الختانين (al-tiqa' al-khitanayn): Meeting of the two circumcised parts
استحسان (istihsan): Juridical preference overriding strict analogy or literal text for a more suitable ruling
تخصيص النص بالمعنى (takhsis al-nas bi al-ma'na): Specifying a general text by rational meaning (ma'na) rather than by another textual evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on ghusl for a man who inserts into a dead woman without ejaculation?
A) Ghusl is required.
B) Ghusl is not required unless he ejaculates.
C) Ghusl is required if he intended intercourse.
D) Ghusl is required if the woman was alive recently.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl upon insertion is fard only for living human females; for beasts and corpses, ejaculation is required, based on the principle of virtual semen emission.

Ghusl Obligation by Penetration: Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Commentary explaining the ruling of ghusl by penetration and Hanafi position against Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ghusl obligation by penetration, explain the condition of actual or virtual ejaculation, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Ghusl requires actual or virtual ejaculation; mere penetration in non-desired orifices is insufficient.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq addresses a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: is ghusl obligatory by any penetration of the glans, or does it depend on ejaculation? The author explains the Hanafi view that the obligator is semen, but ejaculation may be virtual when the cause is complete. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, the evidence, and the practical implications of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Clearly state the contested ruling: Is ghusl wajib by mere penetration without ejaculation in all cases?
The issue revolves around animals, minors, and dead bodies.
2
State the Hanafi position and its conditions
Summarize the Hanafi ruling: ghusl is wajib when ejaculation occurs actually or virtually. Virtual ejaculation applies when the cause is complete – penetration in a desired human orifice (vagina or anus) of a live normally copulable person.
Animals, minors, and dead bodies do not fulfill the complete cause.
3
Present the Shafi'i position and its evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that ghusl is wajib by any penetration without ejaculation, based on the general meaning of the hadith 'When the two circumcisions meet...' and consensus.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response and harmonization of hadiths
The Hanafis use the hadith 'Water is obligatory by the meeting of the two circumcisions without ejaculation' to show that the obligator is semen. They harmonize the second hadith by interpreting it as referring to virtual ejaculation when the cause is complete.
This is not a specification of the general by qiyas initially, but an interpretation giving effect to both texts.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, a Hanafi does not perform ghusl after penetrating an animal or minor unless ejaculation occurs, while a Shafi'i would require ghusl regardless.
This difference affects daily life rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وتواري حشفة في قبل أو دبر) عليهما أي فرض الغسل عند غيبوبة ما فوق الختان وكذلك غيبوبة مقدار الحشفة من مقطوعها في قبل امرأة يجامع مثلها أو دبر على الفاعل والمفعول به وإن لم ينزل والتعبير بغيبوبة فوق الفرج وذلك لأن مدخل الذكر هو مخرج المني والولد والحيض، وفوق مدخل الذكر مخرج البول كإحليل الرجل وبينهما جلدة رقيقة يقطع منها من الختان، فحصل أن ختان المرأة متسفل تحت مخرج البول وتحت مخرج البول مدخل الذكر فإذا غابت الحشفة في الفرج فقد حاذى ختانه ولكن يقال لموضع ختان المرأة الخفاض فذكر الختانين بطريق التغليب، قيد بالتواري لأن مجرد التلاقي لا يوجب الغسل ولكن ينقض الوضوء على الخلاف المتقدم، وقيدنا بكونه في قبل امرأة لأن التواري في فرج البهيمة لا يوجب الغسل إلا بالإنزال، وقيدنا بكونها يجامع مثلها لأن التواري في الميتة والصغيرة لا يوجب الغسل إلا بالإنزال، وقد تقدم الدليل من السنة والإجماع على وجوب الغسل بالإيلاج وإن لم يكن معه إنزال وهو بعمومه يشمل الصغيرة والبهيمة وإليه ذهب الشافعي لكن أصحابنا رضي الله عنهم منعوه إلا أن ينزل لأن وصف الجنابة متوقف على خروج المني ظاهراً أو حكماً عند كمال إلى الإيلاج في الدبر وعلى الملاط به إذ ربما يتلذذ فينزل، ويخفى لما قلنا. وأخرجوا ما ذكرنا لكنه يستلزم تخصيص النص بالمعنى ابتداء كذا في فتح القدير. وحاصله أن الموجب إنزال المني حقيقة أو تقديراً عند فإن الماء اسم جنس محلى بلام الاستغراق فمعناه من المني فيما يتعلق بعين الماء لا مطلقاً لوجوبه بالحيض والنفاس. والثاني حديث «إذا جلس بين شعبها الأربع ثم جهدها فقد وجب الغسل وإن لم ينزل» ومقتضاه عموم وجوب الغسل بغيبوبة الحشفة من غير إنزال فيشمل الصغيرة والبهيمة والميتة فيعارض الأول وإذا أمكن العمل بهما وجب فقال علماؤنا: أن الموجب للغسل هو إنزال المني كما أفاده الحديث الأول لكن المني تارة يوجد حقيقة وتارة يوجد حكماً عند كمال سببه وهو غيبوبة الحشفة في محل يشتهى مع خفاء خروجه ولو كان في الدبر لكمال السببية فيه لأنه لخروج المني غالباً كالإيلاج في القبل لاشتراكهما ليناً وحرارة وشهوة حتى إن الفسقة اللوطة رجحوا قضاء الشهوة من الدبر على قضائها من القبل ومنه خبراً عن قوم لوط «لقد علمت ما لنا في بناتك من حق وأنك لتعلم ما نريد» [هود: 79] وفي الصغيرة ونحوها لم يكن الإيلاج سبباً كاملاً لإنزال المني لعدم الداعية إليه فلم يوجد إنزال المني حقيقة ولا تقديراً. فلو قلنا بالوجوب من غير إنزال لكان فيه ترك العمل بالحديث أصلاً وهو لا يجوز فكان هذا منا من هذا عليه الصلاة والسلام إذا التقى الختانان وتوارت الحشفة فقد وجب الغسل يتناول الصغيرة والبهيمة والعام قطعي فيما يتناوله حتى يجوز نسخ الخاص به عندنا ولا يجوز تخصيصه ابتداء بظني كالقياس وخبر الواحد ما لم يخصص أوّلاً بدليل مستقل لفظي مقارن، فإن خصص بذلك لا يبقى قطعياً على الصحيح فيخص بالقياس والآحاد على ما بسط في كتب الأصول، وما هنا ليس القبيل فإنه تخصيص بالقياس ابتداء وهو لا يخصص القطعي.
His saying: (And the disappearance of the glans in the front or back) on both of them, i.e., the obligation of ghusl upon the concealment of what is above the circumcision, and likewise the concealment of the amount of the glans from the one whose glans is cut in the front of a woman whom one like him would copulate with, or in the back, upon the doer and the one done to, even if he did not ejaculate. And the expression by the disappearance of the glans is better than the expression by the meeting of the two circumcisions because it includes penetration in the back, and because what is established in the private part is their approximation, not their meeting, because the man's circumcision is the place of cutting which is below the glans, and the woman's circumcision is the place of cutting a skin from her like the cock's comb above the private part. That is because the entrance of the penis is the exit of semen, child, and menstruation, and above the entrance of the penis is the exit of urine like the man's urethra, and between them is a thin skin from which the circumcision is cut. So it is established that the woman's circumcision is low under the exit of urine, and under the exit of urine is the entrance of the penis. So when the glans disappears in the private part, it has approximated his circumcision, but the place of the woman's circumcision is called al-khifad; thus mentioning the two circumcisions is by way of predominance. He restricted by concealment because mere meeting does not necessitate ghusl but invalidates wudu' according to the preceding difference. And we restricted it being in the front of a woman because concealment in the private part of an animal does not necessitate ghusl except with ejaculation, and we restricted it being such that one like him would copulate with her because concealment in a dead person and a minor does not necessitate ghusl except with ejaculation. And the proof from the Sunnah and consensus has preceded on the obligation of ghusl by penetration even if there is no ejaculation with it, and in its generality it includes the minor and the animal, and this is the view of al-Shafi'i, but our authorities (may Allah be pleased with them) prevented it except if he ejaculates, because the description of janabah depends on the exit of semen apparently or virtually upon the completion of its cause, with its [the semen's] scarcity and laziness in the duct due to the weakness of the flow by the desire not reaching its peak, as the one copulating experiences during intercourse of pleasure at the approach of separation. So then it is necessary to put the cause in place of it, and this is the reason for penetration necessitating ghusl. So the ruling extends to penetration in the back and upon the one who rubs, because perhaps he will feel pleasure and ejaculate, and it is hidden for what we said. And they objected to what we mentioned, but it entails specification of the text by meaning initially, as in Fath al-Qadir. Its summary is that the obligator is the ejaculation of semen really or virtually upon the completion of its cause, and in what we mentioned it was not found really nor virtually due to the deficiency of its cause. But this entails specification of the text by meaning initially, and the general is not specified by meaning initially according to us, so our imams need to answer this, and they also need to answer what al-Nawawi mentioned in Sharh al-Muhadhdhab, that it is contradicted by intercourse with an ugly old woman, extremely ugly, blind, leprous, with severed limbs, for it necessitates ghusl by consensus even though no pleasure is intended in it customarily. And I have not found an answer to these two objections, and it has become apparent to me in the answer to the first that this is not specification of the text by meaning initially, and its clarification needs more investigation. So I say, and with Allah is success: There have come two hadiths whose apparent meanings conflict: The first: 'Water is obligatory by the meeting of the two circumcisions without ejaculation.' For 'water' is a generic noun definite by the lam of istighraq, so its meaning is [that water is from] semen regarding what relates to the essence of water, not absolutely because of its obligation due to menstruation and postpartum. And the second hadith: 'When he sits between her four branches and then exerts himself, then ghusl has become obligatory even if he did not ejaculate.' Its implication is the generality of obligation of ghusl by disappearance of the glans without ejaculation, so it includes the minor, the animal, and the dead person, thus conflicting with the first. And when it is possible to act upon both, it is necessary. So our scholars said: That which obligates ghusl is the ejaculation of semen as indicated by the first hadith, but semen is sometimes found really and sometimes found virtually upon the completion of its cause, which is the usual disappearance of the glans in a desired place with the concealment of its exit, even if it is in the back, due to the completeness of causality therein, because it is for the exit of semen usually, like penetration in the front, due to their sharing softness, heat, and desire, so much so that the fornicating sodomites prefer fulfilling desire from the back over fulfilling it from the front. And from it is the news about the people of Lut: 'You know that we have no right to your daughters, and indeed you know what we want' (Hud 79). And in the minor and the like, penetration is not a complete cause for ejaculation of semen due to the lack of inclination to it, so ejaculation of semen was not found really nor virtually. So if we said with obligation without ejaculation, that would entail abandoning acting upon the hadith entirely, and that is not permissible. So this from us is based on this. Upon him be peace: 'When the two circumcisions meet and the glans disappears, then ghusl has become obligatory' includes the minor and the animal, and the general is definitive regarding what it encompasses, such that it is permissible to abrogate the specific with it according to us, and it is not permissible to specify it initially by something conjectural like qiyas or khabar wahid unless it is first specified by an independent verbal evidence that is connected. Then if it is specified by that, it does not remain definitive according to the correct view, so it may be specified by qiyas and ahad reports as elaborated in usul books. And what is here is not of that category, for it is specification by qiyas initially, and it does not specify the definitive.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa’iq, regarding the obligation of ghusl by penetration. The author explains the matn's ruling: ghusl becomes obligatory upon disappearance of the glans (hashafa) in the front or back of a live woman who is penetrable, even without ejaculation. He clarifies that the expression 'disappearance of the glans' is preferred over 'meeting of the two circumcisions' because it covers anal intercourse and is more precise regarding anatomy. The ruling is restricted to a woman of the type that is normally copulated with, excluding animals, minors, and dead persons, for whom ghusl is only obligatory if ejaculation occurs. The author notes that a general hadith and consensus indicate ghusl by penetration without ejaculation, which would include minors and animals – this is Imam al-Shafi'i's position. However, the Hanafi school restricts it to cases where ejaculation occurs actually or virtually, because the description of janabah (major ritual impurity) is tied to the exit of semen. The cause (sabab) for ghusl is the completion of the cause for ejaculation, which occurs when the glans disappears in a place that is desired and typically leads to ejaculation, like the vagina or anus of a normal woman. In minors, animals, or dead bodies, the cause is incomplete because there is no natural inclination, so ghusl is not obligatory unless actual ejaculation happens. The author then addresses an objection: that this Hanafi position entails specifying a general text (the hadith and consensus) by qiyas (analogy) initially, which is not allowed in Hanafi usul for definitive texts. The author responds by citing two hadiths: one stating that ghusl is by meeting of circumcisions (interpreted to mean ejaculation), and another stating that ghusl is obligatory by penetration without ejaculation. He harmonizes them by explaining that the obligator is ejaculation, but it can be virtual when the cause is complete – i.e., penetration in a desired place where ejaculation is typical. In cases like minors or animals, the cause is not complete, so virtual ejaculation is not assumed. This is not specification by qiyas initially but rather interpreting the texts in a way that gives effect to both. The author also mentions an objection by al-Nawawi regarding intercourse with an ugly woman, but the text does not provide a full answer here. The passage concludes with a discussion of the definitiveness of the general hadith and the permissibility of specification by qiyas in conjectural texts, reaffirming the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
حشفة (hashafah): The glans of the penis; the part that must disappear for ghusl to become obligatory.
غيبوبة الحشفة (ghaybubat al-hashafah): The complete disappearance of the glans into the orifice; the condition for ghusl obligation.
ختان (khatan): Circumcision; here refers to the circumcised parts of male and female.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, when is ghusl obligatory after penetration?
A) Whenever the glans disappears, regardless of the partner.
B) Only if ejaculation occurs actually or virtually in a normal human orifice.
C) Only if the partner is a living human adult.
D) Only if the partner is a woman.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires actual or virtual ejaculation for ghusl obligation by penetration, restricting the general hadith to cases where the cause for ejaculation is complete.

Ghusl is Obligatory for Anal Intercourse
Defends ghusl obligation for dabr with proof from consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl for anal intercourse and explain the proof from consensus.

Core Idea
Insertion into the anus obligates ghusl, just as vaginal intercourse does.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defends a key ruling: ghusl is wajib for anal intercourse, just as for vaginal intercourse. The commentator addresses an objection that a general text cannot be specified by analogy, refutes a weak alternative view, and anchors the ruling on consensus. You will learn the proof structure and why the opposing view is rejected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The commentator establishes that ghusl is obligatory (wajib) for anal intercourse. Note which act triggers this obligation: insertion of the glans (hashafa) into the anus.
The ruling applies to both active and passive partners.
2
Locate the Proof
The proof is consensus (ijma) as cited from Ghayat al-Bayan: 'They agreed on the obligation of ghusl from insertion in the anus.' Recognize that ijma is a binding source in Hanafi fiqh.
The word 'ittafaqo' indicates unanimous agreement.
3
Understand the Refutation of the Opposing View
The commentator reports a view from al-Mibtagha that no ghusl is required, likening anus to an animal. He rejects this as 'very remote' and notes the consensus overrides it.
The opposing view is weak (da'if) and not followed in the madhhab.
4
Address the Misunderstanding
Some argue that the anus is not a place of desire, so ghusl is not required. The commentator counters that even if true, it is rare; the ruling is based on the act of insertion, not desire.
The Hanafi position is based on the general principle that any insertion of the glans into a private part necessitates ghusl.
5
Confirm the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that ghusl is wajib. This is the operative ruling for fatwa, based on consensus and the authority of the six core books (Zahir al-Riwayah).
The minority view is recorded but not acted upon.

Source Text

الماء قولاً بموجب العلة لا تخصيصاً للنص بالقياس ابتداء، ويكون إنزال المني هو الموجب وهو إما حقيقة أو تقديراً هو الذي ذكره مشايخنا في أصولهم في بحث المفاهيم قاطعين النظر عن كون الماء منسوخاً كما لا يخفى وجواب آخر أنه يجوز تخصيص النص العام بالمعنى ابتداء من عند جمهور الفقهاء منهم الشيخ أبو منصور ومن تابعه من مشايخ سمرقند لأن موجبه عندهم ليس بقطعي، وأكثر أصحابنا يمنعونه لكونه عندهم قطعياً والقياس ظني، أما إذا كان العام ظنياً جاز تخصيصه بالقياس ابتداء وما نحن فيه من هذا القبيل لأنه ظني الثبوت وإن كان قطعي الدلالة. وأما الجواب عن الثاني فلا نسلم أن المحل لا يشتهى ولئن سلم فاجتماع هذه الأوصاف الشنيعة في امرأة نادر ولا اعتبار به. هذا وقد ذكر في المبتغى خلافاً فيمن غابت الحشفة في فرجه فقال : وقيل لا غسل عليه كالبهيمة والمراد بالفرج الدبر ونقله في فتح القدير ولم يتعقبه. وقد يقال : إنه غير صحيح فقد قال في غاية البيان واتفقوا على وجوب الغسل من الإيلاج في الدبر على الفاعل والمفعول به وجعل الدبر كالبهيمة بعيد جداً كما لا يخفى.
Water? in accordance with the cause, not specification of the text by analogy initially, and that the discharge of semen is the obligator, either actually or constructively, that is what our mashayikh mentioned in their usul in the discussion of concepts, cutting off consideration from the water being abrogated as is not hidden. And another answer: that it is permissible to specify a general text by meaning initially according to the majority of jurists, including Shaykh Abu Mansur and those who followed him from the mashayikh of Samarqand, because its obligator according to them is not categorical. And most of our ashab prevent it because according to them it is categorical and analogy is speculative. But if the general is speculative, it is permissible to specify it by analogy initially, and our case is of this type because it is speculative in transmission even if categorical in meaning. And as for the answer to the second, we do not concede that the place is not desired, and even if conceded, the gathering of these ugly descriptions in a woman is rare and not to be considered. This has been mentioned in al-Mibtagha: a difference regarding one whose glans disappears into his private part, and it was said: no ghusl upon him like an animal, and by private part is meant the anus, and it was transmitted in Fath al-Qadir and he did not comment on it. And it may be said: it is not correct, for it was said in Ghayat al-Bayan: they agreed on the obligation of ghusl from insertion in the anus on both the active and passive partner, and considering the anus like an animal is very remote as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a commentary defending the obligation of ghusl for anal intercourse (dabr). The commentator begins by addressing an objection that the general text (about ghusl from janabah due to semen) cannot be specified by qiyas (analogy). He provides two answers: (1) It is permissible to specify a general text by meaning (ma'na) initially according to many Hanafi jurists, especially if the general text is zanni al-thubut (speculative in transmission), which it is here. (2) The argument that the anus is not a place of desire is rejected; even if conceded, such a case is rare. He then reports a differing opinion from al-Mibtagha that no ghusl is required for anal intercourse, likening it to bestiality. The commentator refutes this by citing Ghayat al-Bayan, which states consensus (ittifaq) on the obligation of ghusl for both parties. Thus, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that ghusl is wajib for anal intercourse, and the opposing view is dismissed as weak.

Key Terms
دبر (dubr): anus, as a site of insertion that may necessitate ghusl
إيلاج (ilaj): insertion of the glans into the private part

D) The opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa

Key Takeaway
Ghusl is wajib for anal intercourse based on consensus, and the opposing view comparing it to bestiality is rejected as unsound.

Ghusl for Finger Insertion into Anus
Reports and prefers the ruling that no ghusl required for finger insertion into anus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl for finger insertion into the anus and apply the analogy (qiyas) that the finger is not an instrument of intercourse.

Core Idea
No ghusl required because the finger is not a sexual organ — it is like inserting a stick.

Many assume any insertion into a private part necessitates ghusl, but the Hanafi school distinguishes based on the nature of the object. This lesson examines a specific ruling: a man inserting his finger into his anus while fasting. The relied-upon position is that neither ghusl nor qada' is necessary, derived from the principle that ghusl only becomes obligatory when the inserted object is an instrument of intercourse, i.e., the glans. Understanding this distinction clarifies the boundaries of ritual purity and fasting invalidation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Contested Ruling
The act is inserting a finger into the anus. The controversy is whether this obligates ghusl (ritual bath) and, if done while fasting, requires qada' (making up the fast).
The text states 'different opinions' but does not name the opposing view.
2
Extract the Hanafi Preferred View
Find the phrase 'al-mukhtār' (the chosen view). The author states that the preferred position is that no ghusl and no qada' are required.
The word 'mukhtār' indicates the muftā bihī (operative ruling).
3
Understand the Legal Reasoning (ʿIllah)
The ʿillah (effective cause) given is that the finger is not a tool for intercourse ('laysa ālah li-l-jimāʿ'). Therefore it is analogous to a piece of wood (khashabah).
The analogy (qiyās) compares the finger to a wooden stick, which clearly does not require ghusl.
4
Apply the Principle to Other Cases
Generalize: any object that is not a sexual organ (e.g., a medical instrument, a finger, a piece of cloth) inserted into the anus or vagina does not trigger ghusl in the Hanafi school. Only insertion of the glans (ḥashafah) does.
This ruling applies regardless of desire or intention, as the text focuses solely on the nature of the object.
5
Distinguish the Fasting Context
The fasting rule follows the purity rule: since ghusl is not obligatory, the fast remains valid and no qada' is needed. This reinforces that the act does not nullify purity or the fast.
Some scholars might argue that any insertion invalidates fast, but Hanafis hold the fast is only broken by actual intercourse or ejaculation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتح القدير: إن في إدخال الأصبع الدبر خلافاً في إيجاب الغسل فليعلم ذلك وقد أخذه . من التنجيس ولفظه : رجل أدخل أصبعه في دبره وهو صائم اختلفوا في وجوب الغسل والقضاء والمختار أنه لا يجب الغسل ولا القضاء لأن الأصبع ليس آلة للجماع فصار بمنزلة الخشبة. ذكره في الصوم.

Commentary
This passage reports a difference of opinion regarding the obligation of ghusl when a finger is inserted into the anus. The relied-upon (mukhtar) position is that no ghusl is required, and if one is fasting, no qada' is needed either. The reason is that the finger is not an instrument of intercourse, akin to inserting a stick. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi principle that ghusl is only obligatory for insertion of a sexual organ (the glans) into a private part.
